Oath Breaking When Permission Is Granted but Unknown
Intra-Hanafi dispute on permission and oath-breaking

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on oath-breaking when permission is granted but unknown, and explain the linguistic basis for Abu Hanifa's position distinguishing idhn from rida.

Core Idea
Permission (idhn) requires awareness; without knowledge, an oath is broken — Abu Hanifa's linguistic reasoning prevails.

This passage addresses a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: does an oath to avoid speech break if permission is given but the swearer is unaware? The answer hinges on the linguistic nature of 'idhn' and its distinction from internal states like satisfaction (rida). Understanding this clarifies the Hanafi emphasis on the external, communicative aspect of permission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Oath Scenario
The oath: 'I will not speak to him except with his permission.' Permission is granted but the swearer does not know until after speaking. The legal question is whether breaking the oath (hanth) occurs.
The scenario hinges on the swearer’s lack of awareness.
2
State Abu Hanifa’s Ruling and Linguistic Proof
Abu Hanifa rules that hanth occurs. He derives 'idhn' from 'adhan' (announcement) or 'udhn' (ear), both requiring hearing and knowledge. Since the swearer did not know, the permission is not realized, so speaking violates the oath.
This is the position of the matn and zahir al-riwayah.
3
State Abu Yusuf’s Ruling and Analogy to Rida
Abu Yusuf rules no hanth. He argues that 'idhn' means release (itlaq), completed by the grantor alone, analogous to satisfaction (rida), which is an internal state effective without the other’s knowledge.
Abu Yusuf uses qiyas to rida.
4
Analyze the Hanafi Rebuttal
The Hanafi response (supporting Abu Hanifa) distinguishes idhn from rida: rida is a heart action not requiring external communication, while idhn is inherently communicative (rooted in hearing/informing). Therefore, knowledge is necessary for idhn to take effect.
The rebuttal refutes the analogy by showing a difference in the underlying nature.
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
The commentary upholds Abu Hanifa’s view as stronger, stating that the purpose of the oath (to avoid speech without aware permission) necessitates knowledge. The mufta bihi is that hanth occurs.
Abu Yusuf’s view is considered questionable (محل نظر).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اليمين في الكلام . اور اگر قسم کھائی فلاں کی اجازت کے بغیر کلام نہیں کروں گا اس نے اجازت دے دی اور اسے معلوم نہیں اس نے کلام کیا حانث ہو جائے گا وَلَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلِّمُهُ إِلَّا بِإِذْنِهِ فَاذِنَ لَهُ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمُ بِالْإِذْنِ حَتَّى كَلَّمَهُ حَنَثَ لااَنَّ الْإِذْنَ مُشْتَقٌّ مِنَ الْآذَانِ الَّذِي هُوَ الْإِعْلَامُ أَوْ مِنَ الْوُقُوعِ فِي الْأُذُنِ وَكُلُّ ذَلِكَ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ إِلَّا بِالسَّمَاعِ وَقَالَ أَبُو يُوسُفَ لَا يَحْنَثُ لِأَنَّ الْإِذْنَ هُوَ الْإِطْلَاقُ وَإِنَّهُ يَتِمُّ بِالْإِذْنِ كَالرِّضَاءِ قُلْنَا الرِّضَاءُ مِنْ أَعْمَالِ الْقَلْبِ وَلَا كَذَلِكَ الْإِذْنُ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ وہ بغیر اجازت کلام نہ کرے گا۔ پھر اسے اجازت ہوگئی۔ مگر اجازت کے بارے میں معلوم نہیں ۔ یہاں تک کہ اس نے ( مخلوف علیہ سے) گفتگو کر لی تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اذن (اجازت) اذان سے لیا گیا ( مشتق) ہے۔ جو بمعنی ” آگاہ کرنے کے ہے۔ یا وقوع اذن ( کان میں پڑنا) سے مشتق ہے۔ ہر ایک کا تحقق سماعت کے بغیر نہیں ہوتا۔ امام ابو یوسف کا قول ہے کہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اسلئے کہ اذن بمعنی اطلاق کے ہے۔ جو رضا کی طرح صاحب اذن ( اجازت دینے والا) سے مکمل ہو جاتا ہے۔ اور ہم (احناف) کہتے ہیں ۔ رضامند ہونا اعمال قلب (دل) میں سے ہے۔ اسی طرح اذن (اجازت) کا معاملہ جو کہ اوپر گذر چکا ہے۔ تشریح لفظ اذن یا تو اذان بمعنی "آگاہ کرنا" سے مشتق ہے یا اُذن سے جس کا معنی کان میں پڑنا ہے بہر دو تقدیر دونوں صورتوں کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ عدم سماعت یا سماع ( یعنی سنے بغیر ) اس کا ثبوت ناممکن ہو تو جب حالف کو اجازت مل گئی لیکن اسے معلوم نہیں تو بات کرنے سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ امام ابو یوسف کے ہاں حالف صورت مذکورہ میں حانث نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک اذن بمعنی اطلاق کے ہے اس کیلئے مخلوف علیہ کی اجازت کافی ہے خالف کے علم میں آئے یا نہ آئے امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ جس طرح رضامندی کا عمل ہے کہ اس میں عمل وسماع ضروری نہیں یہاں بھی اس طرح مخلوف علیہ کا اذن کافی ہے۔ لیکن یہ قول محل نظر ہے اسلئے کہ رضا مندی افعال قلب سے ہے اور ان اعمال کیلئے علم وسماع ضروری نہیں اور اگر یمین کی غرض اور حٹ کے لزوم پر غور کرنے سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ مخلوف علیہ کی اجازت سے آگاہ ہونا یا سماع لازمی ہے۔
Oath regarding speech. And if one swore: 'I will not speak to him except with his permission,' and he gave permission, and the swearer did not know of the permission until he spoke to him, he becomes a breaker of the oath. Because 'idhn' (permission) is derived from 'adhan' which means informing, or from occurrence in the ear, and all of that is not realized except by hearing. Abu Yusuf said: He does not break the oath, because permission means release, and it is completed by the one giving permission, like satisfaction. We (Hanafis) said: Satisfaction is from actions of the heart, and permission is not like that as previously mentioned. Translation: And if someone swore that he would not speak without permission. Then permission was given to him, but he did not know about the permission. Until he conversed with the person on whom the oath was taken, then he becomes a breaker of the oath. Because 'idhn' (permission) is derived from 'adhan', which means informing, or from 'occurrence in the ear'. In both cases, its realization is not possible without hearing. Imam Abu Yusuf's statement is that he does not break the oath, because according to him 'idhn' means release, which is completed by the one granting permission, like satisfaction. And we (Hanafis) say: Satisfaction is from the actions of the heart, and the matter of permission is different as passed above. Explanation: The word 'idhn' is either derived from 'adhan' meaning 'to inform' or from 'udhn' meaning 'to enter the ear'. In both eventualities, the requirement is that without hearing, its proof is impossible. So when the swearer received permission but did not know, then speaking makes him break the oath. According to Imam Abu Yusuf, the swearer in the mentioned case will not break the oath because in his view 'idhn' means release, and for that, the permission of the person on whom the oath is taken is sufficient, whether the swearer knows or not. Imam Abu Yusuf says: Just as satisfaction is an action where action and hearing are not necessary, here too the permission of the person on whom the oath is taken is sufficient. But this statement is questionable because satisfaction is from the actions of the heart, and for those actions, knowledge and hearing are not necessary; but if one reflects on the purpose of the oath and the obligation of breaking, it becomes clear that being informed of or hearing the permission of the person on whom the oath is taken is necessary.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of permission (idhn) on an oath of avoidance. The ruling from the matn (originally from Imam Muhammad's work) is that if a person swears not to speak to someone except with that person's permission, then the one granting permission does so, but the swearer does not know about it and speaks, he breaks his oath (hanth). The reasoning is linguistic: the word idhn (permission) is derived from adhan (announcement/informing) or from udhn (ear), both of which require hearing and knowledge for their realization. Since the swearer did not hear or know of the permission, his speaking is in breach of the oath. Imam Abu Yusuf disagrees; he considers idhn to mean 'release' (itlaq), which is akin to satisfaction (rida). Just as satisfaction is an internal state that takes effect without the other party's knowledge, so permission is effective upon being granted by the authorized person, regardless of the swearer's awareness. The Hanafi response (from Abu Hanifa's side) distinguishes between internal states (like satisfaction) and external permissions, which require awareness to be valid. The commentary upholds Abu Hanifa's view as stronger, noting that the purpose of the oath is to prevent speech without the other's awareness, so knowledge is necessary. The mufta bihi (operative position) is Abu Hanifa's ruling.

Key Terms
إذن (idhn): Permission or authorization from the person on whom the oath is taken
حنث (hanth): Breaking an oath by violating its condition
رضاء (rida): Satisfaction or consent, an act of the heart

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, why does a person break his oath if he speaks after permission is given but he does not know about it?
A) Because permission is invalid without knowledge
B) Because the linguistic root of idhn implies awareness
C) Because the oath was absolute, so any speech breaks it
D) Because the one granting permission must also be informed

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, permission (idhn) is effective only when the swearer knows of it, otherwise speaking breaks the oath – a ruling rooted in the linguistic derivation of idhn from hearing and informing.

When Does the Month Start in an Oath? — Negative vs Positive Oaths
Ruling on when the month starts in an oath not to speak

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between a negative oath (avoidance) and a positive oath (vow) by applying the Hanafi rule that a negative oath begins immediately while a positive oath leaves choice to the swearer.

Core Idea
In an oath not to speak for a month, the month starts immediately; in an oath to fast a month, the swearer may choose any month.

This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad deals with two types of oaths mentioning a month: one prohibits speech, the other requires fasting. The key difference lies in the default consequence if the month were not mentioned: perpetual avoidance is possible, but perpetual worship is not. This distinction determines when the month begins, applying the principle of 'indication of the situation' (dilalat hal).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two cases
Case 1: 'I will not speak to him for a month' (negative/avoidance oath). Case 2: 'By Allah, I will surely fast a month' (positive/worship oath).
The Arabic wording: لا يكلمه شهرا vs لا صومن شهرا.
2
Examine the consequence of omitting 'month'
In Case 1, if the month is not mentioned, the oath would be perpetual (ta'abbud) – the swearer could never speak to that person. In Case 2, if the month is not mentioned, the oath would not be perpetual because one cannot fast every day (Eid days etc.).
This shows the default nature of each oath type.
3
Determine the function of mentioning the month
In Case 1, the mention of 'month' excludes the time beyond it, leaving the immediate period after the oath included (by dilalathal – the anger at that moment). In Case 2, the mention only quantifies the fasting act; it does not tie the time to the oath moment.
Thus the month has a 'limiting' vs 'quantitative' function.
4
Apply the rule of indefinite nouns (nakirah)
In Case 2, 'shahran' is an indefinite noun in a positive oath, so specification is left to the swearer. They may choose any month to fulfill the oath.
In Case 1, the month is definite by context (the immediate period).
5
Conclude the ruling
For avoidance oaths, the month starts from the moment of oath. For worship oaths, the month is not immediately bound; the swearer has the choice.
This is the Hanafi position from Imam Muhammad, recorded in Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم اٹھائى لا يكلمه شهرا قسم اٹھانے کے وقت سے مہینہ شمار ہوگا قَالَ وَإِنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلِّمُهُ شَهْرًا فَهُوَ مِنْ حِيْنَ حَلْفٍ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْلَمْ يَذْكُرِ الشَّهْرَ تَتَابَّدُ الْيَمِينُ وَذِكْرُ الشَّهْرِ لِإِخْرَاجِ مَا وَرَاءَهُ فَبَقِيَ الَّذِي يَلِى يَمِيْنَهُ دَاخِلًا عَمَلًا بِدَلَالَةِ حَالِهِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا قَالَ وَاللَّهِ لَا صُوْمَنَّ شَهْرًا لِأَنَّهُ لَوْلَمْ يذكر الشَّهْرَ لَا يَتَأَبَّدُ الْيَمِينُ فَكَانَ ذِكْرُهُ لِتَقْدِيرِ الصَّوْمِ بِهِ وَإِنَّهُ مُنكِرْ فَ التَّعَيُّنُ إِلَيْهِ ترجمہ امام محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اس بات کی قسم کھائی کہ میں اس سے ایک مہینہ گفتگو نہیں کروں گا تو قسم کھانے کے ساتھ ہی سے اس کا مہینہ شروع ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اگر وہ مہینہ کا تذکرہ نہ کرتا تو پھر یہ تم ہمیشہ کے لئے ہو جاتی کہ وہ اس سے زندگی میں کبھی بھی بات نہیں کر سکتا تھا۔ بس مہینہ کے ذکر نے اس کے بعد کے زمانہ کو اس حکم قسم سے فارغ کر دیا ہے۔ لہذا اب اس حکم میں وہ زمانہ باقی رہ گیا جو تم کھانے کے ساتھ میں پایا جاتا ہے۔ اس کی جو موجودہ حالت ہے اس کو دلیل بناتے ہوئے یعنی اس غصہ کی بناء پر جو اس وقت اس کے دل میں بھرا ہوا ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر اس نے اس طرح کہا کہ واللہ میں ایک ماہ روزہ رکھوں گا۔ یعنی قسم کے وقت سے اس کا زمانہ متعین نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اگر وہ مہینہ کو ذکر نہیں کرتا پھر بھی اس پر ہمیشہ روزہ رکھنا واجب نہ ہوتا کیونکہ درمیان میں ممنوع دن بھی آتے ہیں اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ مہینہ کاذکر صرف اس لئے ہوتا ہے کہ اس سے روزہ کا اندازہ معلوم ہو جائے۔ اور چونکہ نکرہ کالفظ استعمال کر کے شہرا کہا ہے اس لئے کوئی مہینہ متعین نہیں ہوا اس لئے اسے وقت معین کرنے کا اختیار ہو گا ۔ یعنی اس پر قسم سے یہ واجب ہوا کہ کبھی بھی ایک مہینہ کے روزے رکھ لے۔ ساتھ ہی یہ اختیار بھی رہا کہ اپنی مرضی سے اس مہینہ کو معین کرے۔
Oath taken 'I will not speak to him for a month' - the month will be counted from the time of taking the oath. He (Imam Muhammad) said: And if he swore not to speak to him for a month, it is from the time of his oath, because if he had not mentioned the month, the oath would become perpetual. And the mention of the month is to exclude what is beyond it, so the time immediately following his oath remains included, acting according to the indication of his situation. Contrary to if he said: 'By Allah, I will surely fast a month,' because if he had not mentioned the month, the oath would not become perpetual. So his mentioning it was to estimate the fast by it, and that is an indefinite noun, so its specification is left to him. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If someone swore that he would not speak to him for a month, then the month starts from the moment of the oath. Because if he had not mentioned the month, the oath would become perpetual (he could never speak to him in his life). Only the mention of the month exempts the time after it from the ruling of the oath. Thus, the time that remains included is the time coinciding with his oath, acting on the indication of his current state (i.e., the anger he is feeling at that moment). Contrary to if he said: 'By Allah, I will surely fast a month.' Then the month is not specified from the time of the oath. Because if he did not mention the month, he would still not be obliged to fast perpetually, since prohibited days occur in between. From this it is understood that the mention of the month is only to estimate the fast by it. And since he used the indefinite word 'shahran' (a month), no specific month is determined, so he has the choice to specify the time. That is, the oath makes it obligatory that he fast a month at some time, and he also has the option to determine which month according to his will.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage from al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad deals with the interpretation of an oath that includes a time limit. The first case is an oath not to speak to someone for a month. The ruling is that the month begins immediately from the time of the oath. The reasoning: had the swearer not mentioned 'month', the oath would be perpetual (ta'abbud), meaning he could never speak to that person. The mention of 'month' excludes the period beyond it. Therefore, the period immediately after the oath is included because the context (dilalut halihi) indicates anger at that moment, and the purpose is to prevent speech in that immediate situation. The second case is an oath to fast for a month. Here, the month is not immediately determined. If he had not mentioned 'month', the oath would not be perpetual because it is a vow to perform an act of worship, and perpetual fasting is not required (due to prohibited days e.g., Eid). So the mention of 'month' is solely to specify the quantity of fasting, not to immediately bind it to the time of oath. Since the word 'shahr' (month) is indefinite in a positive oath, the swearer has the option to choose any month for fulfilling his oath. Thus, the fundamental difference between a negative oath (avoidance) and a positive oath (vow) lies in the nature of the default: perpetual avoidance is possible, perpetual worship is not.

Key Terms
يتأبد (yata'abbadu): To become perpetual; the oath lasts indefinitely
دلالة حال (dilalat hal): Indication of the current situation or context
نكرة (nakirah): Indefinite noun; here 'shahran' (a month) without specification

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, what is the ruling for an oath 'By Allah, I will not speak to Zaid for a month'?
A) The month starts from the next day
B) The month starts from the moment of oath
C) The swearer can choose any month to start
D) The oath is void because a month is too long

Key Takeaway
The month in an oath begins immediately only when the oath would otherwise be perpetual (avoidance), but not when the act is naturally intermittent (worship).

Oath Not to Speak: Reciting Quran in Prayer
Inter-madhhab dispute on oath-breaking by Quran recitation in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether reciting Quran or dhikr breaks an oath not to speak, and explain the Hanafi reliance on custom and the hadith to differentiate between prayer and non-prayer contexts.

Core Idea
Reciting Quran in prayer is not speech—the Lawgiver and custom redefine kalam for devotional acts.

When someone swears not to speak and then recites the Quran in prayer, does that break the oath? The Hanafi school says no, citing both sacred law and custom. But what about reciting outside prayer? And what does the Shafi'i school hold? This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind these differing positions, focusing on the pivotal role of legal and customary definitions of 'speech' (kalam).

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the main ruling from the text: reciting Quran in prayer does not break the oath; reciting outside prayer does break it, according to the initial view. Also note the later fatwa extending the exemption outside prayer.
The later fatwa is attributed to Faqih Abu al-Layth and others.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
State that Imam al-Shafi'i holds that any utterance, including Quran and dhikr, breaks the oath because they are speech in linguistic reality.
This is based on qiyas: all verbal expressions are kalam.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Explain the Shafi'i reliance on linguistic haqiqa: every articulated word is speech, so reciting Quran or making dhikr must be included in the oath.
Opposing dalil is purely linguistic.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Present the Hanafi evidence: the hadith 'Our prayer does not befit anything of the speech of people' and the argument that custom (urf) does not call a reciter or glorifier a 'speaker'.
Thus, legal and customary definitions trump linguistic reality.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, a Hanafi can recite Quran or say tasbih without worry of breaking the oath, while a Shafi'i would consider that a breakage. This affects how one advises a person who has sworn not to speak.
The later Hanafi fatwa makes the ruling even more lenient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر قسم کھائی کلام نہیں کرے گا پھر نماز میں قرآن پڑھا حانث نہیں ہوگا وَإِنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَتَكَلَّمُ فَقَرَأَ الْقُرْآنَ فِي صَلَاتِهِ لَا يَحْنِتُ وَإِنْ قَرَأَ فِي غَيْرِ صَلَاتِهِ حَنَثَ وَعَلَى هَذَا التَّسْبِيحُ وَالتَّهْلِيلُ وَالتَّكْبِيرُ وَفِي الْقِيَاسِ يَحْنِثُ فِيهِمَا وَهُوَ قَوْلُ الشَّافِعِيِّ لِأَنَّهُ كَلَامٌ حَقِيقَةٌ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ فِي الصَّلَاةِ لَيْسَ بِكَلَامٍ عُرْفًا وَلَا شَرْعًا قَالَ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ إِنَّ صَلَاتَنَا هَذِهِ لَا يَصْلُحُ فِيهَا شَيْءٌ مِنْ كَلَامِ النَّاسِ وَقِيلَ فِي عُرْفِنَا لَا يَحْنِثُ فِي غَيْرِ الصَّلَاةِ أَيْضًا لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُسَمَّى مُتَكَلَّمًا بَلْ قَارِئًا وَمُسَبِّحًا ...... ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں گفتگو نہیں کروں گا۔ پھر اس نے نماز کی حالت میں قرآن مجید کی تلاوت کی تو حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ لیکن اگر نماز کے علاوہ قرآن پاک کی تلاوت کی تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اسی طرح اگر سبحان اللہ یالا الہ الا اللہ یا اللہ اکبر نماز کی حالت میں کہا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ اور اگر نماز سے باہر کہا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ قیاس کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ نماز کی حالت میں ہو یا نہ ہو دونوں حالتوں میں حانث ہو جائے۔ امام شافعی کا یہی قول ہے۔ کیونکہ حقیقت میں یہ سب کلام ہی ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ نماز کی حالت میں نہ شرعا کلام ہے اور نہ عرفا ہے۔ کیونکہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہماری نماز ایسی چیز ہے کہ اس میں لوگوں کے کلام سے کچھ بھی لائق نہیں ہے (اس میں کسی قسم کے دنیاوی کلام کی گنجائش نہیں ہے۔ (رواه مسلم) اور بعض علماء نے فرمایا ہے کہ ہمارے عرف میں نماز کے علاوہ بھی تلاوت کرنے سے حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ قرآن یا سبیح وغیرہ پڑھنے والے کو متکلم نہیں کہتے ہیں۔ یعنی اسے باتیں کرنے والا نہیں کہا جاتا ہے۔ بلکہ اسے قاری یا تسبیح پڑھنے والا کہتے ہیں۔ فائدہ یہی قول فقیہ ابواللیث اور شیخ الاسلام و صدر شہید وعتابی رحمہم اللہ کا ہے۔ اور اسی پر فتوی ہے۔
And if he swore: 'I will not speak,' and he recited the Quran in his prayer, he does not break the oath. And if he recited outside his prayer, he breaks the oath. Likewise, tasbih, tahlil, and takbir. And by qiyas, he would break the oath in both cases, and that is the saying of al-Shafi'i, because in reality it is speech. And our evidence is that in prayer it is not considered speech by custom or by sacred law. The Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Indeed, this prayer of ours does not befit anything of the speech of people.' And it is said that in our custom, he does not break the oath even outside prayer, because he is not called a speaker (mutakallim) but rather a reciter (qari) and a glorifier (musabbih). Translation: And if someone swore that he will not speak, then he recited the noble Quran while in prayer, he does not break his oath. But if he recited the Quran outside prayer, he breaks his oath. Similarly, if he said 'Subhan Allah,' 'La ilaha illa Allah,' or 'Allahu Akbar' in prayer, he does not break his oath. And if he said them outside prayer, he breaks his oath. Qiyas would require that whether in prayer or not, he would break his oath; that is the saying of Imam al-Shafi'i, because in reality all of these are speech. And our evidence is that in prayer, it is not speech according to custom or law, because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'This prayer of ours does not befit anything of the speech of people.' (Narrated by Muslim) And some scholars said that in our custom, he does not break the oath even outside prayer, because one who recites Quran or tasbih is not called a speaker (mutakallim); rather, he is called a reciter (qari) or glorifier (musabbih). Benefit: This is the saying of Faqih Abu al-Layth, Shaykh al-Islam, Sadr al-Shahid, and al-Atabi (may Allah have mercy on them), and it is the fatwa.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage deals with an oath not to speak (لا يتكلم). The main ruling states that if the swearer recites Quran in prayer, he does not break his oath (hanth), but if he recites outside prayer, he does break it. The same applies to tasbih, tahlil, and takbir. This ruling is based on the legal and customary definition of 'speech' (kalam). The qiyas (analogical reasoning) would suggest that any utterance is speech and thus should break the oath in both cases. This is the position of Imam al-Shafi'i: because in linguistic reality (haqiqa), all these are speech. However, the Hanafi school differentiates: in prayer, these utterances are not considered speech by either custom (urf) or sacred law (shar'a). They cite the hadith: 'Our prayer does not befit anything of the speech of people' (Muslim), which explicitly excludes permissible prayer content from the category of human speech. Therefore, within prayer, these acts are considered devotional recitation (tilawah, dhikr), not conversation. Outside prayer, the default applies: they are speech in the common understanding, so they break the oath. However, a later preferred view (qil) of some Hanafi authorities, including Faqih Abu al-Layth, Shaykh al-Islam, Sadr al-Shahid, and al-Atabi, holds that even outside prayer, one does not break an oath not to speak by reciting Quran or dhikr because in common parlance one is not called a 'speaker' (mutakallim) but a reciter or glorifier. This is the mufta bihi (operative fatwa). Thus, the Hanafi school has two views: the earlier view differentiates between prayer and non-prayer; the later view extends the exemption to all recitations of Quran and dhikr outside prayer as well.

Key Terms
كلام (kalam): Human speech in common parlance, excluding Quran and dhikr
حانث (hanith): One who breaks an oath
تسبيح (tasbih): Uttering 'Subhan Allah'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the later Hanafi fatwa (mufta bihi), does reciting the Quran outside prayer break an oath not to speak?
A) Yes, because Quran is speech
B) No, because the reciter is called a qari, not a mutakallim
C) Yes, because the oath is absolute
D) No, because it is in prayer

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the definition of 'speech' in oaths is shaped by custom and sacred law, not just linguistic reality—hence Quran and dhikr, especially in prayer, do not break an oath not to speak.

Interpretation of 'Day' in Conditional Divorce
Ruling on the scope of 'yawm' in a conditional divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default Hanafi interpretation of 'yawm' when tied to a non-continuous action and explain the distinction between religious and judicial acceptance of intention.

Core Idea
In conditional divorce, 'yawm' with a non-prolonged action means absolute time – both day and night.

When a husband makes divorce conditional on speaking to someone on a certain 'day', a key question arises: does speaking at night also trigger the divorce? The Hanafi school, based on Quranic usage, gives a default answer that includes both night and day. However, the husband's inner intention can affect the religious ruling, and there is disagreement among the school's imams on whether that intention is accepted in court. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition and the act
The husband says: 'The day I speak to so-and-so, my wife is divorced.' The act is 'speaking' (kalam), which is an action that does not extend over time (la yamtaddu).
The nature of the act matters for interpreting 'day'.
2
Determine the default interpretation of 'yawm'
The matn states: it applies to night and day (huwa 'ala al-layli wa al-nahar). The rule: when 'yawm' is linked to a non-prolonged action, absolute time (mutlaq al-waqt) is intended.
3
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse 'Whoever turns his back to them on that day' (yawma'idhin) is cited. The turning back can happen at any time during the battle, not only in daylight, showing that 'yawm' can mean absolute time.
This is a dalil naqli – proof from scripture.
4
Understand the role of intention
If the husband only intended daytime, he is believed religiously (yudayyanu) but the court (qada') applies the default unless evidence supports his claim.
5
Note Abu Yusuf's opposing view
Abu Yusuf holds that the husband is not believed even in court, because claiming only daytime is contrary to common usage (muta'arif). The majority (Zahir al-Riwayah) accepts the claim in court if plausible.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم کھائی فلاں شخص سے گفتگو کروں تو میری بیوی کو طلاق تو بیوی کو کب طلاق ہوگی وَلَوْ قَالَ يَوْمَ أُكَلَّمُ فُلَانًا فَامْرَأَتُهُ طَالِقٌ فَهُوَ عَلَى اللَّيْلِ وَالنَّهَارِ لِاَنَّ اسْمَ الْيَوْمِ إِذَا قَرَنَ بِفِعْلٍ لَا يَمْتَدُّ يُرَادُ بِهِ مُطْلَقُ الْوَقْتِ قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى وَمَنْ يُوَلِّهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ دُبُرَهُ وَالْكَلَامُ لَا يَمْتَدُّ وَإِنْ عَلَى النَّهَارِ خَاصَّةً دُيِّنَ فِي الْقَضَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ مُسْتَعْمَلْ فِيهِ أَيْضًا وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوْسُفَ أَنَّهُ لَا يَدَيَّنُ فِي الْقَضَاءِ لِأَنَّهُ خِلَافُ الْمُتَعَارِفِ وَلَوْ قَالَ لَيْلَةً أُكَلَّمُ فُلَانًا فَهُوَ عَلَى اللَّيْلِ خَاصَّةً لِأَنَّهُ حَقِيقَةٌ فِي سَوَادِ اللَّيْلِ كَالنَّهَارِ لِلْبَيَاضِ خَاصَّةً وَمَا جَاءَ اسْتِعْمَالُهُ فِي مُطْلَقِ الْوَقْتِ ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ جس دن میں فلاں سے گفتگو کروں میری بیوی کو طلاق ہے۔ تو یہ کلام دن اور رات دونوں پر ہو گا۔ یعنی خواہ دن میں گفتگو کرے یا رات میں اس کی بیوی کو طلاق ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ یوم (دن) کا لفظ جب کسی ایسے فعل سے متعلق ہو جو دیر پا ( دراز) نہ ہو تو اس سے مطلق وقت مراد ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ فرمان باری تعالیٰ ہے وَمَنْ يُوَتِهِمْ يَوْمَئِذٍ دُبُرَهُ یعنی جو شخص کہ آج کے دن کا فروں سے پیٹھ پھیرے گا۔ یعنی جہاد میں کسی بھی وقت کافروں سے پیٹھ پھیر نامستحق غضب ہے اور کلام بھی ایسا فعل نہیں ہے جو دیر پا ہو اور اگر اس نے فقط دن ہی کی نیت کی
Oath taken: 'If I speak to so-and-so, my wife is divorced.' When will the wife be divorced? And if he said: 'The day I speak to so-and-so, my wife is divorced,' then it applies to night and day, because when the word 'day' is connected to an action that does not extend, absolute time is intended. Allah the Exalted says: 'And whoever turns his back to them on that day' (al-Anfal 16). And speech is not something that extends. And if he intended only the day specifically, he is believed in the court (in his oath) because 'day' is also used for daytime. And from Abu Yusuf: he is not believed in the court because it is contrary to common usage. And if he said: 'The night I speak to so-and-so,' then it is specifically for night, because it is literally used for the darkness of the night just as 'day' is specifically for the whiteness (daylight). And its usage for absolute time has occurred. Translation: And if someone swore that 'The day I speak to so-and-so, my wife is divorced,' then this statement applies to both day and night. That is, whether he speaks during the day or at night, his wife will be divorced. Because when the word 'day' (yawm) is connected to an action that is not prolonged, absolute time is meant. As Allah's statement: 'And whoever turns his back on them on that day' – meaning at any time during the battle. And speech is also an action that is not prolonged. And if he intended only the day specifically, he is believed in the court (in his oath) because the word is also used for daytime. And from Abu Yusuf: he is not believed in the court because it is contrary to common usage. And if he said: 'The night I speak to so-and-so,' then it applies specifically to night, because literally it refers to the darkness of the night, just as 'day' is specifically for the whiteness. And its usage for absolute time has been reported.
Source pages p. 97

Commentary
This passage discusses the interpretation of a conditional divorce tied to speaking on a 'day' (yawm). The ruling from the matn (and relied upon) is that 'day' in such a context includes both daytime and nighttime. The reasoning: when the word 'day' is linked to an action that is not prolonged or continuous (like speaking), it is understood to mean 'absolute time' (mutlaq al-waqt) – meaning anytime, not just daylight. This is supported by the Quranic usage in Surah al-Anfal: 'Whoever turns his back to them on that day (yawma'idhin)' – which applies to turning back at any point during the battle, daytime or night. Since speaking is also not a prolonged action, the same principle applies: 'day' means any time. However, the swearer may have only intended the daytime in his heart. In that case, he is believed regarding his religious duty (yudayyinu) but not in court (qada') – meaning the court does not accept his claim unless there is evidence. The court applies the default interpretation (includes night). In contrast, if the condition is 'night' (laylah), it applies only to nighttime specifically, because 'night' is literally used for darkness, not for daytime. There is also a view from Abu Yusuf that even if he intended only daytime, he is not believed even in court because that interpretation contradicts normal usage. The passage concludes that the general ruling is that 'day' includes night and day; 'night' only includes night.

Key Terms
يوم (yawm): Day; in the context of a condition tied to a non-prolonged action, it includes both day and night (absolute time)
دين في القضاء (diyyun fi al-qada'): To be believed in court regarding one's intention
متداول / متعارِف (muta'arif): Common usage; the conventional understanding of a word

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the default Hanafi interpretation, if someone says 'The day I speak to Zaid, my wife is divorced,' and he speaks to Zaid at night, does the divorce occur?
A) Yes, because 'yawm' in this context includes both night and day
B) No, because 'yawm' only means daytime
C) It depends on the swearer's intention
D) Yes, but only if he intended night as well

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'yawm' in a conditional divorce linked to a non-continuous action defaults to absolute time covering both day and night; the husband's contrary intention is accepted religiously but not necessarily in court.

Oath on a Person Identified by Relationship: When the Relationship Ends
Ruling on oath concerning a person identified by ownership relation when that relation ends

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on oaths tied to relational attributes and state Imam Muhammad's exception for identification-based attributes.

Core Idea
If ownership ends, the oath is safe; if a relational label ends, Muhammad says the oath remains.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between attributions of ownership (idafat milk) and relational attributions (idafat nisbah) in oaths. While there is consensus that selling the slave cancels the oath, a dispute arises when the attribute is merely for identification—as with 'wife' or 'friend.' This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind each position and highlights its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Oath Scenario
Read the passage and understand the three cases: oath not to speak to 'slave of X', 'wife of X', or 'friend of X'.
The swearer does not intend a specific individual; the oath is tied to the attribute.
2
State the General Hanafi Ruling
For idafat milk (slave of X), if the slave is sold, the oath is not broken. This is agreed upon.
The attribute of ownership no longer exists, so the oath's subject is gone.
3
Examine Imam Muhammad's Exception
For idafat nisbah (wife, friend), Muhammad holds that the oath is broken even after divorce or enmity because the attribute is merely for identification.
The text from al-Riyadat compares it to physically pointing: the person is the same.
4
Analyze the Difference in Reasoning
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf focus on the attribute's existence; Muhammad focuses on the actual person intended. Identify which reasoning is used.
The thamarah al-khilaf: in practice, does the swearer commit hanth or not?
5
Determine the Mufta Bihi
Although the general position (zahir al-riwayah) is no hanth, Muhammad's view is more cautious and often relied upon in fatwa.
Tarjih authority: the text presents Muhammad's view as the reasoned exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ مَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ عَبْدَفُلَانِ وَلَمْ يَنْوِ عَبْدًا بِعَيْنِهِ أَوِ امْرَأَةَ فُلَانِ اَوْ صَدِيقَ فُلَانِ فَبَاعَ فُلَانٌ عَبْدَهُ أَوْبَانَتْ مِنْهُ امْرَأَتُهُ أَوْ عَادَى صَدِيقَهُ فَكَلَّمَهُمْ لَمْ يَحْنِتُ لأَنَّهُ عَقَدَيَمِيْتُهُ عَلَى فِعْلٍ وَاقِعٍ فِي مَحَلَّ مُضَافٍ إِلَى فَلَانٍ أَمَّا إِضَافَةُ مِلْكِ أَوْإِضَافَهُ نِسْبَةٍ وَلَمْ يُوجَدْ فَلا يَحْنِتُ قَال هَذَا فِي إِضَافَةِ الْمِلْكِ بِالْاتِفَاقِ وَفِي إِضَافَةِ النَّسْبَةِ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَحْدِثُ كَالْمَرْأَةِ وَالصَّدِيقِ قَالَ فِى الرِّيَادَاتِ لِاَنَّ هَذِهِ الْإِضَافَةَ لِلتَّعْرِيفِ لَانَّ الْمَرْأَةَ. وَالصَّدِيقَ مَقْصُودَ ان بِالهِجْرَانِ فَلَا يُشْتَرَطُ دَوَامُهَا فَيَتَعَلَّقُ الْحُكْمُ بِعَيْنِهِ كَمَا فِي الْإِشَارَةِ
Whoever swears not to speak to the slave of so-and-so, and he did not intend a particular slave, or [similarly] the wife of so-and-so, or the friend of so-and-so, then so-and-so sells his slave, or his wife becomes separated from him (banat), or he becomes hostile to his friend, and then he speaks to them, he does not break the oath because he made his oath on an action occurring in a subject that is attributed to so-and-so, either by ownership (idafat milk) or by relation (idafat nisbah). And [the attribute] is not found (so no hanth). He said: This in the case of idafat milk is agreed upon. In the case of idafat nisbah, according to Muhammad, he would break the oath, like the wife and friend. He said in al-Riyadat: Because this idafah is for definition (ta'rif); indeed the wife and friend are intended for hijran (boycott/avoidance), so their continuity is not stipulated, so the ruling attaches to the very person (bi 'aynihi) just as in the case of pointing (al-isharah).
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage addresses oaths that identify a person by their relationship to another, such as 'the slave of Zaid,' 'Zaid's wife,' or 'Zaid's friend.' The scenario: a person swears not to speak to 'the slave of Zaid' without intending a specific slave. Later, Zaid sells the slave (so the slave is no longer owned by Zaid), or Zaid's wife gets divorced (so she is no longer his wife), or Zaid becomes hostile to his friend (so the friendship ends). If the swearer then speaks to that person, does he break the oath? The ruling is that he does not break the oath because the oath was made on a location (mahall) that is attributed to Zaid. The attribute (ownership or relation) no longer exists, so the oath's subject is gone. There is agreement (bil-ittifaq) on this for ownership attributes (idafat milk). However, for relational attributes (idafat nisbah) like wife and friend, Imam Muhammad holds that the oath is broken because the purpose of the attribute is merely to identify (ta'rif) the person. The intention behind the oath is to avoid that specific person, regardless of whether the relationship continues. The text cites al-Riyadat: the ruling attaches to the very person (bi 'aynihi) just as if the person was physically pointed to. The authority weight: the first view (no hanth) is from the zahir al-riwayah for ownership; for relational, there is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf (Muhammad's view). The mufta bihi likely follows Muhammad's view as it is more cautious. The text ends with 'Wajh' which likely continues but is cut off in our window.

Key Terms
إِضَافَةُ مِلْكِ (idafat milk): Attribution of ownership; e.g., 'slave of Zaid' indicates Zaid owns him.
إِضَافَةُ نِسْبَةٍ (idafat nisbah): Attribution by relationship (e.g., wife, friend); used for identification.
حِنْث (hanth): Breaking or violating an oath, requiring expiation (kaffarah).
تَعْرِيف (ta'rif): Identification; the function of an attribute to specify which person is meant.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, what is the status of an oath not to speak to 'the wife of Zaid' if Zaid divorces her, according to Imam Muhammad?
A) The oath is not broken because the attribute no longer exists.
B) The oath is broken because the attribute is merely for identification.
C) The oath becomes invalid because the subject is unclear.
D) The oath requires a new intention to be valid.

Key Takeaway
For relational attributes, Imam Muhammad considers the oath binding on the person regardless of the relationship's continuation, a view often preferred in fatwa for caution.

Non-Specific Oaths and Relationship Change: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling from Jami' al-Saghir with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a non-specific oath regarding a slave, wife, or friend, and identify the points of disagreement between Imam Muhammad and the other two imams regarding the effect of a change in relationship.

Core Idea
An oath tied to a relationship is broken only if the relationship persists; dispute arises when the description is merely identificatory.

This lesson examines a specific case from Al-Jami' al-Saghir: someone swears not to speak to 'so-and-so's slave' (or wife/friend) without specifying which one. Later, the relationship ends. Is the oath broken? The answer depends on whether the oath was intended to avoid the person because of their connection to that third party or because of personal enmity. This creates a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the other two founding imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case
The person swears non-specifically about a slave, wife, or friend of a named person (e.g., 'I will not speak to Zaid's slave'). Then the relationship ends (sale, divorce, friendship ends). Then he speaks to that person.
2
Determine the ruling in the Jami' al-Saghir narration
According to that narration, he does not break the oath (no hanth). Reason: it is possible his intention was to avoid them because of their relationship to Zaid, not their person.
3
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Muhammad holds that for wife and friend, the oath is broken even after the relationship ends, because the description is only for identification. For slave, he agrees with no hanth.
4
Analyze the proof (dalil) for each view
The Jami' view relies on doubt (shakk); the oath could be tied to the relationship. Muhammad argues that personal enmity is the real cause, so the oath attaches to the individual regardless of the relationship.
5
Apply the practical consequence (thamarah)
In a fatwa, one must consider both views; precaution would be to avoid speaking to the person even after the relationship ends, or make expiation if one does speak.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مَا ذُكِرَ هَهُنَا وَهُوَ رِوَايَةُ الْجَامِعِ الصَّغِيرِ أَنَّهُ يَحْتَمِلُ أَنْ يَكُونَ غَرْضُهُ هِجْرَانَهُ لِأَجَلِ الْمُضَافِ إِلَيْهِ وَلِهَذَا لَمْ يُعَيِّنْهُ فَلَا يَحْنَثُ بَعْدَ زَوَالِ الْإِضَافَةِ بِالشَّكِّ

ترجمہ: اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں فلاں شخص کے غلام سے بات نہیں کروں گا اور کسی خاص غلام کی نیت نہیں کی یا فلاں شخص کی بیوی سے یا فلاں کے دوست سے بات نہیں کروں گا۔ پھر اس فلاں شخص نے اپنا غلام بیچ دیا۔ یا اس کی بیوی اس سے طلاقِ بائن پا کر علیحدہ ہوگئی۔ یا اس کے دوست سے دشمنی ہوگئی۔ پھر اس نے اس غلام یا عورت یا دوست سے بات کر لی تو حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنی قسم ایسے فعل پر رکھی ہے جو ایسے حل میں واقع ہو گا جس کی نیت فلاں شخص کی طرف ہے۔ یعنی اپنی بات کرنے کو ایسے آدمیوں سے متعلق رکھا جن کو اس فلاں شخص کے ساتھ تعلق ہے خواہ وہ تعلق ملکیت کا ہو جیسے فلاں کا غلام۔ یا نکاح کا تعلق ہو یا دوستی قائم ہو۔ اب جب کر تعلق ان کے ساتھ قائم نہیں رہا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ مصنف نے فرمایا ہے کہ نسبتِ ملک میں تینوں آئمہ کا اتفاق ہے کہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اور دوسری نسبت کی صورت میں امام محمد کے نزدیک حانث ہوگا۔ جیسے کہ اس کی بیوی یا دوست سے کلام کیا حالانکہ نکاح اور دوستی باقی نہیں ہے تو بھی حانث ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد نے زیادات میں اس کی وجہ یہ بیان کی ہے کہ ایسی نسبت صرف پہچان کے لئے ہوتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اصل مقصود یہ ہے کہ اس عورت سے اور اس شخص سے کلام کرنا چھوڑ دے۔ کیونکہ ان دونوں سے ذاتی نفرت ہے اور فلاں کی بیوی یا دوست ہونا صرف ان کی پہچان کے لئے ہے۔ اس لئے بیوی اور دوستی کے رشتہ کا ہمیشہ رہنا کچھ شرط نہیں ہے۔ اس لئے حکم ہر شخص کی ذات سے متعلق ہو گا۔ جیسے اشارہ کرنے میں ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی مثلاً یوں کہا کہ فلاں کے اس دوست سے یا فلاں کی اس بیوی سے کلام نہیں کروں گا۔ پس جب کبھی ان دونوں سے کلام کرے گا حانث ہوگا۔ اگر چہ اس شخص سے دوستی باقی نہ رہے۔ اور جو روایت یہاں مذکور ہے یعنی فلاں کے ساتھ نسبت نہ رہنے سے حانث نہ ہوگا یہ جامع صغیر کی روایت ہے اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ شاید اس کی غرض یہ ہو کہ ان دونوں کو فلاں شخص سے تعلق کی بناء پر چھوڑے۔ اسی وجہ سے اس نے کسی بیوی یا کسی دوست کو معین نہیں کیا ہے اور یہ بھی ممکن ہے کہ ان دونوں کی ذات سے اسے نفرت ہو اس طرح شک پیدا ہو گیا۔ پس جبکہ اس شخص کی طرف نسبت باقی نہ رہی تو اب شک کی وجہ سے حانث نہیں ہوگا۔
What is mentioned here is a narration of Al-Jami' al-Saghir: It is possible that his intent was to abandon him for the sake of the one to whom he is related, and for this reason he did not specify him. So he does not break the oath after the relationship [the connection] is removed, due to doubt.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from Al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding an oath that is general and non-specific. The case is: someone swears not to speak to 'so-and-so's slave' or 'so-and-so's wife' or 'so-and-so's friend' without specifying which slave, wife, or friend. If the relationship ends (master sells slave, wife divorced finally, friendship ends), and the oath-taker then speaks to that person, he does not break his oath according to this narration. The reasoning: the oath is tied to the relationship, not the individual. However, Imam Muhammad disagrees regarding wife and friend: he holds that the oath is broken even after the relationship ends, because the description is only for identification and the real cause is personal enmity. The three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) agree on the slave case. The author explains that the ruling here (non-breaking) is based on doubt: it is possible the intention was to avoid them because of their connection to that person, so when the connection ends, the oath is no longer applicable. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf follow the Jami' al-Saghir narration for non-specific cases, while Muhammad applies his general principle. The practical consequence: a person who swears non-specifically about a wife or friend must be careful if the relationship changes, as there is disagreement.

Key Terms
يَمِين (yamīn): An oath sworn by Allah to do or not do something; breaking it requires expiation.
حَنِث (ḥanith): Broken or violated an oath; the state of having failed to fulfill the oath.
إِضَافَة (iḍāfah): Genitive construction or attribution; here, the relationship between the person and the thing (e.g., 'slave of so-and-so').
مُضَافٌ إِلَيْهِ (muḍāfun ilayhi): The second term of the idāfah; the person or thing to which the first is related (e.g., 'so-and-so' in 'slave of so-and-so').

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following statements is true regarding the intra-Hanafi dispute on a non-specific oath about a wife?
A) All three imams agree that the oath is broken after divorce.
B) Imam Muhammad holds the oath is not broken after divorce.
C) Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold the oath is not broken after divorce.
D) The dispute also applies to slaves.

Key Takeaway
In non-specific oaths concerning a wife or friend, the Hanafi school has internal disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say no hanth after relationship ends, Imam Muhammad says hanth because the description is identificatory.

Specific Oath on Slave, Wife, Friend, and House with Indication – Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on specific oaths using idafah and isharah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding oaths on specific property vs. persons using idafah and isharah, and identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
When an oath specifies by pointing, the ruling differs depending on whether the object is property (tied to ownership) or a person (tied to the person's essence).

In this passage, we encounter an important intra-Hanafi dispute about oaths that use both attribution (idafah) and indication (isharah). The dispute centers on whether the oath attaches to the person/thing itself or to the relationship of ownership. Understanding this distinction is crucial for issuing correct fatwas in such cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath formulation and scenarios
Recognize that the oath specifies a particular slave, wife, friend, or house by both idafah (attribution) and isharah (pointing). Note that the dispute arises when the relationship (ownership for slave/house, marriage/friendship for wife/friend) ends.
2
Distinguish property from personal relations
Classify the object: slaves and houses are property subject to ownership; wives and friends are personal relationships. The Sheikhain (Abu Hanifa & Abu Yusuf) treat these categories differently.
3
State Sheikhain's position and their ta'lil
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, for slave/house, the oath is tied to ownership; if ownership ends, speaking/entering does not break the oath. For wife/friend, the oath attaches to the person regardless of relationship, because enmity can be personal. Their reasoning: the motive for the oath is enmity towards the owner, not the slave/house itself.
The Sheikhain argue that property and slaves lack personal status for enmity.
4
State Muhammad & Zufar's position and their ta'lil
According to Muhammad and Zufar, in all cases (including slave and house), the oath attaches to the thing itself as indicated by isharah. The idafah is merely for identification and becomes irrelevant once isharah specifies the object. Thus, speaking to the slave after sale breaks the oath, just as speaking to the wife after divorce.
They emphasize that isharah is stronger than idafah for identification.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a man swears 'I will not speak to this slave of Zaid' and Zaid sells the slave, according to Sheikhain he can speak without hanth; according to Muhammad & Zufar, speaking would break the oath and require kaffarah.
This dispute affects fatwa in cases of oaths on specific property or persons.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ كَانَتْ يَمِينُهُ عَلَى عَبْدٍ بِعَيْنِهِ بِأَنْ قَالَ عَبْدَ فُلَانٍ هَذَا أَوْ امْرَأَةَ فُلَانٍ بِعَيْنِهَا أَوْ صَدِيقَ فُلَانٍ بِعَيْنِهِ لَمْ يَحْنَثْ فِي الْعَبْدِ وَحَنِثَ فِي الْمَرْأَةِ وَالصَّدِيقِ وَهَذَا قَوْلُ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَأَبِي يُوسُفَ. وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ يَحْنَثُ فِي الْعَبْدِ أَيْضًا وَهُوَ قَوْلُ زُفَرَ. وَإِنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَدْخُلُ دَارَ فُلَانٍ هَذِهِ فَبَاعَهَا ثُمَّ دَخَلَهَا فَهُوَ عَلَى هَذَا الْاِخْتِلَافِ. وَجْهُ قَوْلِ مُحَمَّدٍ وَزُفَرَ أَنَّ الْإِضَافَةَ لِلتَّعْرِيفِ وَالْإِشَارَةُ أَبْلَغُ مِنْهَا لِكَوْنِهَا قَاطِعَةً لِلشَّرِكَةِ، فَاعْتُبِرَتِ الْإِشَارَةُ وَلَغَتِ الْإِضَافَةُ، وَصَارَ كَالصَّدِيقِ وَالْمَرْأَةِ. وَلَهُمَا أَنَّ الدَّاعِيَ إِلَى الْيَمِينِ مَعْنًى فِي الْمُضَافِ إِلَيْهِ لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ الْأَعْيَانَ لَا تُهْجَرُ وَلَا تُعَادَى لِذَوَاتِهَا، وَكَذَا الْعَبْدُ لِسُقُوطِ مَنْزِلَتِهِ، بَلْ لِمَعْنًى فِي مَالِكِهَا، فَتَقَيَّدَ الْيَمِينُ بِحَالِ قِيَامِ الْمِلْكِ، بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا كَانَتِ الْإِضَافَةُ نِسْبَةً كَالصَّدِيقِ وَالْمَرْأَةِ لِأَنَّهُ يُعَادَى لِذَاتِهِ، فَكَانَتِ الْإِضَافَةُ لِلتَّعْرِيفِ، وَالدَّاعِي لِمَعْنًى فِي الْمُضَافِ إِلَيْهِ غَيْرُ ظَاهِرٍ لِعَدَمِ التَّعْيِينِ، بِخِلَافِ مَا تَقَدَّمَ.

ترجمہ: اور اگر اس کی قسم اس فلاں شخص کے کسی معین غلام پر ہو مثلاً کہا کہ فلاں شخص کے اس غلام سے یا معین بیوی یا دوست پر ہو یعنی مثلاً فلاں شخص کی اس بیوی یا اس دوست سے کلام نہیں کروں گا۔ پھر فلاں شخص کی طرف ان لوگوں کی نسبت نہ رہی اور ان سے کوئی تعلق باقی نہ رہا تو امام ابوحنیفہ و ابو یوسف رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک غلام سے کلام کرنے میں حانث نہ ہوگا۔ اور عورت اور دوست سے کلام کرنے میں حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام محمد نے کہا ہے کہ غلام سے کلام کرنے میں بھی حانث ہوگا۔ امام زفر کا بھی یہی قول ہے۔ اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں فلاں شخص کے اس گھر میں نہیں جاؤں گا۔ پھر اس دوسرے شخص نے اپنے اس گھر کو بیچ دیا اس کے بعد مذکور شخص اس گھر میں داخل ہو گیا تو اس کے حکم میں بھی وہی اختلاف مذکور ہے۔ یعنی شیخین کے نزدیک حانث نہ ہوگا۔ اور امام محمد و زفر رحمۃ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ نسبت تو شناخت کے لئے ہوتی ہے۔ اور اشارہ کر دینے سے پوری پوری شناخت ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اشارہ کرنے سے شرکت کا احتمال بالکل ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ بخلاف نسبت کے۔ اس طرح یہاں شرکت کا اعتبار ہوا اور نسبت بیکار ہوگئی۔ اس لئے دوست اور بیوی کی طرح غلام اور گھر کا بھی حکم ہو گیا۔ اور شیخین رحمہما کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قسم کھانے پر آمادہ کرنے والی ایسی کوئی بات اس شخص یا چیز میں ضرور موجود ہے۔ یعنی فلاں شخص کی وجہ سے اس نے قسم کھائی ہے کہ اس کے غلام وغیرہ سے بات نہیں کروں گا۔ کیونکہ یہ چیزیں خود اپنے طور پر ایسی نہیں ہیں کہ ان کو چھوڑا جائے یا ان سے دشمنی رکھی جائے۔ اور یہی حال غلام کا بھی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا درجہ بہت ہی گھٹا ہوا ہے۔ یعنی اس قابل نہیں ہے کہ اس سے دشمنی کی جائے یا اس سے بولنا چھوڑ دیا جائے تو کچھ فائدہ ہو۔ بلکہ یہ چھوڑنا کسی ایسی وجہ سے ہے جو ان چیزوں کے مالک میں موجود ہے۔ تو قسم اسی وقت تک کے لئے باقی رہے گی جب تک کہ اس کی ملکیت باقی ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر ملکیت کی نسبت نہ ہو بلکہ دوسری طرح کی نسبت ہو۔ جیسے فلاں شخص کا دوست یا اس کی بیوی تو ان دونوں سے ذاتی دشمنی یا نفرت بھی قسم کا سبب ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے نسبت صرف پہچان کے لئے ہوئی۔ لیکن قسم کھانے کا سبب تو مضاف الیہ یعنی جس کی طرف اس کی نسبت کی گئی ہے خاص اس میں کسی بات کا ہونا ظاہر نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے اس نے معین نہیں کیا ہے۔ بخلاف پہلی صورت کے یعنی جبکہ ملکیت کی نسبت ہو تو یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ اس وقت قسم کھانے کا سبب فلاں مخصوص شخص میں کوئی بات ہے۔
If his oath is upon a specific slave, such that he said 'this slave of so-and-so' or 'this specific wife of so-and-so' or 'this specific friend of so-and-so', he does not become a breaker of the oath regarding the slave, and becomes a breaker regarding the woman and the friend. This is the statement of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Muhammad said: He becomes a breaker regarding the slave as well, and this is the statement of Zufar. If he swore not to enter this house of so-and-so, then he sold it, then entered it, then it is upon this same disagreement. The scope of the statement of Muhammad and Zufar: that the idafah is for identification, and the pointing is more effective than it because it cuts off partnership, so the pointing is considered and the idafah becomes invalid, and it becomes like the friend and the woman. And for them both (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): that the motive to the oath is a meaning in the one to whom it is related, because these specific things are not abandoned nor enmity is shown for their own essences, and likewise the slave due to the fallenness of his status, but rather due to a meaning in his owner, so the oath is tied to the state of the existence of ownership, contrary to when the idafah is a relationship like the friend and the woman, because he is shown enmity for his own essence, so the idafah is for identification, and the motive for a meaning in the one to whom it is related is not apparent due to lack of specification, contrary to what preceded.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute that applies when the oath specifies the person by both idafah (attribution) and isharah (pointing/indication), e.g., saying 'this slave of so-and-so' or 'this wife of so-and-so' or 'this friend of so-and-so'. The ruling differs based on whether the object is a slave/property (subject to ownership) or a wife/friend (personal relationship). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sheikhain): For a specified slave, if the ownership ends (slave sold) and the oath-taker speaks to him, he does not break his oath; for a wife or friend, even if the relationship ends, he does break his oath if he speaks to them. Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold that for all three (including the slave), the oath is broken if he speaks to them after the relationship ends. The same rule applies to a specific house (whether entering after sale). The reasoning: Muhammad and Zufar argue that the pointing (isharah) is stronger than the idafah for identification; the idafah becomes irrelevant, so the oath attaches to the person/thing itself, regardless of the relationship. The Sheikhain argue that for slaves and property, the reason for the oath is a meaning in the owner (enmity towards the owner), and since slaves have low status, they are not personally hated; therefore the oath is tied to the ownership. For wife and friend, enmity can be towards the person themselves, so the idafah is merely for identification and the oath attaches to the person regardless of the relationship. The practical implication: in fatwa, the difference matters when a person swears about a specific slave or house of another: according to one view, he breaks the oath if he speaks after ownership ends; according to the other, he does not. This is a well-known dispute within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
إِشَارَة (ishārah): Pointing with hand or gesture to specify a particular thing; considered stronger than idafah for identification.
مُعَيَّن (mu'ayyan): Specific, determined; a particular slave, wife, friend, etc., identified by pointing or description.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears 'I will not enter this house of Bakr.' Later, Bakr sells the house. The man then enters the house. According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, does he break his oath?
A) Yes, he breaks the oath because he entered the same house.
B) No, he does not break the oath because the ownership ended.
C) Yes, according to all Hanafi imams.
D) No, according to Imam Muhammad.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has an internal dispute on whether an oath on a specific property (slave/house) using idafah and isharah is tied to ownership or to the thing itself, with practical consequences for kaffarah.

Oath on Owner of a Cloak
Ruling that an oath on an owner of a cloak is broken even after sale, with talil that the attribute is purely identificatory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why an oath referencing an owner of a cloak remains binding even after the cloak is sold, and apply the principle of purely identificatory attributes to similar oath scenarios.

Core Idea
An oath attached to a person via an inanimate object is broken by speaking to that person, regardless of the object's ownership.

This lesson examines a ruling from Imam Muhammad in Al-Jami' al-Saghir concerning oaths that refer to a person through an object they possess. The key insight is that when the attribute is purely for identification and bears no inherent cause for enmity, the oath remains attached to the person even after the object is sold. Understanding this distinction helps you apply the correct ruling in similar oath cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
Determine what the oath-taker swore and what action he later performed. The ruling is that hanth occurs (he breaks the oath).
The act is speaking to the same person after the cloak is sold.
2
Locate the Dalil
The text provides a reason (ta'lil): the idafah (owner of this cloak) only serves for identification (ta'rif).
Imam Muhammad states: 'li-anna hadhihi al-idafah la yahtamil illa al-ta'rif'.
3
Analyze the Rationale
The rationale is that a person is not hated because of his cloak; the cloak has no inherent meaning that would cause enmity. Thus, the oath attaches to the person himself, not the object.
Compare with cases where ownership is of a human (slave) where legal effects differ.
4
Apply the Principle
Apply this principle to any similar oath that uses an inanimate object's ownership as a descriptor. The oath is broken regardless of change in ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلِّمُ صَاحِبَ هَذَا الطَّيْلَسَانِ فَبَاعَهُ ثُمَّ كَلَّمَهُ حَنِثَ لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ الْإِضَافَةَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ إِلَّا التَّعْرِيفَ لِأَنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَا يُعَادَى لِمَعْنًى فِي الطَّيْلَسَانِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ.

ترجمہ: اور محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں اس چادر والے سے بات نہیں کروں گا۔ اس کے بعد چادر والے نے اپنی چادر کسی کے پاس بیچ دی اس وقت اس سے قسم کھانے والے نے بات کی تو بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس وقت یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ چادر والے کہنے سے مقصود اس کی پہچان کے سوا دوسری کوئی بات نہیں ہے اور اس کا احتمال بھی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ چادر میں ایسی کوئی بات نہیں ہے جس سے آدمی سے دشمنی کی جائے۔ اس لئے چادر والا کہنا ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اشارہ سے کہا کہ میں اس آدمی سے بات نہیں کروں گا۔
He (Muhammad) said: And whoever swore not to speak to the owner of this cloak, then he sold it, then he spoke to him, he breaks the oath, because this idafah does not accept except identification, because a person is not shown enmity due to a meaning in the cloak, so it becomes like when he pointed to him.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage from Imam Muhammad (in Al-Jami' al-Saghir) provides a clear ruling: if someone swears not to speak to 'the owner of this cloak', and the owner sells the cloak, then the oath-taker later speaks to that person, he has broken his oath. The reason is that the attribute 'owner of this cloak' is purely for identification; there is no inherent meaning in the cloak that could be the cause of enmity. Therefore, the oath attaches to the person himself, not to his possession. This is contrasted with the previous case of 'slave of so-and-so', where ownership of a human being has legal significance and the oath may be tied to the owner's interest. The point is that a cloak is an inanimate object; no one hates a person because of his cloak. So the idafah here is simply a description. The ruling becomes identical to when the oath-taker pointed to the person directly (isharah).

Key Terms
طَيْلَسَان (ṭaylasān): A cloak or hooded garment; here used as an example of an object that is not inherently the cause of enmity.
صَاحِب (ṣāḥib): Owner, possessor; the person who owns the cloak.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears, 'I will not speak to the owner of this cloak.' The owner then sells the cloak. The man later speaks to him. What is the ruling?
A) He does not break his oath because the person is no longer the owner.
B) He breaks his oath because the description was only for identification.
C) He breaks his oath only if he pointed at him.
D) He does not break his oath because the cloak is an inanimate object.

Key Takeaway
An oath that identifies a person by an inanimate object is broken by speaking to that person even after he ceases to own the object, because the attribute is purely descriptive.

Oath on a Young Man Who Becomes Old
Ruling that an oath on a person is not affected by a change in his age attribute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that in oaths, temporary attributes attached to a present person are irrelevant (laghw), and determine whether an oath is broken when the attribute changes.

Core Idea
An oath binds to the person, not to a passing description like youth.

Imagine you swear not to speak to a specific person because they are young. Years later, they become old. Does speaking to them break your oath? According to the Hanafi school, the oath remains binding because it was attached to the person, not the attribute of youth. The attribute is considered 'laghw' (irrelevant) when the person is present.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and its description
Read the oath: 'I will not speak to this young man.' The description 'young' is a temporary attribute of age.
2
Note that the person is present
The phrase 'this young man' indicates the oath-taker pointed to a specific person who was present. In Hanafi law, when the person is present, the attribute is considered redundant.
Presence (hudur) is key; absent persons are treated differently.
3
Recognize the attribute is not the motive
The text states that this attribute is not a motive (dā'iyah) for the oath. The oath is likely due to enmity or a personal reason, not the youth itself.
4
Apply the ruling
Since the oath attaches to the person, a change in the attribute (young → old) does not prevent hanth (breaking the oath). Speaking to him now breaks the oath, and kaffarah is due.
Kaffarah applies as per the rules of breaking an oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلِّمُ هَذَا الشَّابَّ فَكَلَّمَهُ وَقَدْ صَارَ شَيْخًا حَنِثَ لِأَنَّ الْحُكْمَ تَعَلَّقَ بِالْمُشَارِ إِلَيْهِ إِذِ الصِّفَةُ فِي الْحَاضِرِ لَغْوٌ وَهَذِهِ الصِّفَةُ لَيْسَتْ بِدَاعِيَةٍ إِلَى الْيَمِينِ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ مِنْ قَبْلُ.

ترجمہ: اگر کسی نے ایسی قسم کھائی کہ میں اس نوجوان سے بات نہیں کروں گا پھر اس سے اس حالت میں بات کی کہ وہ ادھیڑ عمر کو پہنچ چکا ہے تو بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس حکم کا تعلق اس سے ہوگا جس کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ حاضر شخص میں صفت کو بیان کرنا غیر مفید بات ہے۔ اور یہ صفت ایسی نہیں ہے جو قسم کھانے کا باعث ہو جیسا کہ پہلے گزر چکا ہے۔
And whoever swore not to speak to this young man, then he spoke to him while he had become an old man, he breaks the oath, because the ruling attaches to the one pointed to, since the attribute in the present is irrelevant, and this attribute is not a motive to the oath, as has preceded.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This ruling addresses an oath where the person is described by a temporary attribute like 'young' (shābb). If the person ages (becomes shaykh/an old man), but is still the same individual, speaking to him breaks the oath. The reason is that for a present person, descriptive attributes (like youth) are considered irrelevant (laghw) in oaths; what matters is the person himself. The attribute 'young' is not the cause (dā'iyah) for the oath; the oath-taker's enmity or purpose is directed at the individual, not the quality of youth. Therefore, a change in the attribute does not affect the oath. This principle is consistent with the earlier case of the cloak owner: when the attribute is not the motivating factor, the oath attaches to the person.

Key Terms
شَابّ (shābb): A young man; a temporary description of age.
شَيْخ (shaykh): An old man; successor to the shābb after aging.
صِفَة (ṣifah): Attribute or description of a person (e.g., young, old).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears, 'I will not speak to this young man.' Years later, the young man has become old. The man then speaks to him. What is the ruling?
A) He does not break his oath because the person is no longer young.
B) He breaks his oath because the oath was on the person, not the attribute.
C) He breaks his oath only if he pointed at him when he was young.
D) He does not break his oath because the attribute was insignificant.

Key Takeaway
An oath on a present person is not voided by a change in his temporary description.

Oath Not to Speak to Fulan's Slave, Wife, or Friend, and Entering His House After Sale
Intra-Hanafi dispute on oaths and ownership change

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on oaths tied to ownership versus personal relationships, and apply the distinction to determine whether an oath is broken after a property transfer.

Core Idea
An oath tied to ownership lapses with the property; an oath tied to a person's role remains binding.

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute about whether oaths involving a person's property or relationships remain binding after a change in circumstances. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that oaths regarding slaves and houses are annulled when ownership changes, while oaths about wives and friends persist. Imam Muhammad disagrees, viewing all attributions as pure identification. We will examine the reasoning behind each position and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenarios and the ruling question
Examine the two fact patterns: (1) swearing not to speak to someone's slave, wife, or friend, and (2) swearing not to enter someone's house. The common legal issue is whether the oath remains binding after the relationship (ownership or marriage/friendship) is severed.
Keep the distinction between ownership-based and attribute-based relationships in mind.
2
State the position of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf)
For oaths regarding slaves and houses, the two shaykhs rule that the oath lapses when ownership ends because the motivating cause (sabab) is enmity towards the owner. However, for oaths regarding friends and wives, the oath remains because the cause could be personal enmity towards the individual.
This distinction is based on the nature of the relationship: ownership is temporary and external, while friendship and marriage are personal attributes.
3
State the opposing view of Imam Muhammad (and Zufar)
Imam Muhammad holds that all such attributions are merely for identification, like pointing. Once the person or thing is identified, the oath is fixed and does not change with ownership or relationship changes.
This view treats all attributions as equally identificatory, regardless of the underlying relationship.
4
Analyse the proofs (dalil) for each side
The two shaykhs argue that the oath's cause is enmity towards the owner, so when ownership ends, the cause ends. Imam Muhammad argues that identification is permanent; the oath's cause is irrelevant once the person is identified.
Both sides rely on ijtihad and interpretation of the oath-taker's intention.
5
Apply the distinction to determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: If Zayd swears not to speak to Bakr's slave and Bakr sells the slave, according to the two shaykhs, speaking to the former slave does not break the oath; according to Imam Muhammad, it does. Similarly for entering a sold house.
The mufta bihi is the view of the two shaykhs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اليمين في الكلام
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم
شخص کی اس بیوی یا اس دوست سے کلام نہیں کروں گا۔ پھر فلاں شخص کی طرف ان لوگوں کی نسبت نہ رہی اور ان سے کوئی تعلق باقی نہ رہا تو امام ابوحنیفہ وابو یوسف رحمہما اللہ کے نزدیک غلام سے کلام کرنے میں حانث نہ ہوگا۔ اور عورت اور دوست سے کلام کرنے میں حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور امام محمد نے کہا ہے کہ غلام سے کلام کرنے میں بھی حانث نہ ہوگا، کہا ہے کہ غلام سے بھی کلام کرنے میں بھی حانث نہ ہوگا ۔ امام زفر کا بھی یہی قول ہے اور امام شافعی و مالک واحمد رحمہ اللہ علیہم کا بھی یہی قول ہے)۔
اگرکسی نے یہ تم کھائی ہمیں فلاں شخص کے اس گھر میں نہیں جاؤں گا۔ پھر اس دوسرے شخص نے اپنے اس گھر کو بیچ دی اس کے بعد مشخص اس گھر میں داخل ہو گیا تو اس کے حکم میں بھی وہی اختلاف مذکور ہے۔ یعنی شیخین کے نزدیک حانث نہ ہوگا۔ اورامام محمد وزفر رحمۃ اللہ علیہما کے نزدیک حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ نسبت تو شناخت کے لئے ہوتی ہے۔ اور اشارہ کر دینے سے پوری پوری شناخت ہو جاتی ہے۔ کیونکہ اشارہ کرنے سے شرکت کا احتمال بالکل ختم ہو جاتا ہے۔ بخلاف نسبت کے اس طرح یہاں شرکت کا اعتبار ہوا اور نسبت بیکار ہوگئی۔ اس لئے دوست اور بیوی کی طرح غلام اور گھر کا بھی حکم ہو گیا اور شیخین رحمہما کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قسم کھانے پر آمادہ کرنے والی ایسی کوئی بات اس شخص یا چیز میں ضرور موجود ہے۔ یعنی فلاں شخص کی وجہ سے اس نے قسم کھائی ہے کہ اس کے غلام وغیرہ سے بات نہیں کروں گا۔ کیونکہ یہ چیزیں خود اپنے طور پر ایسی نہیں ہیں کہ ان کو چھوڑا جائے یا ان سے دشمنی رکھی جائے۔ اور یہی حال غلام کا بھی ہے۔ کیونکہ اس کا درجہ بہت ہی گھٹا ہوا ہے۔ یعنی اس قابل نہیں ہے کہ اس سے دشمنی کی جائے یا اس سے بولنا چھوڑ دیا جائے تو کچھ فائدہ ہو بلکہ یہ چھوڑ نا کسی ایسی وجہ سے ہے جو ان چیزوں کے مالک میں موجود ہے۔ تو قسم اسی وقت تک کے لئے باقی رہے گی جب تک کہ اس کی ملکیت باقی ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر ملکیت کی نسبت نہ ہو بلکہ دوسری طرح کی ملکیت ہو۔ جیسے فلاں شخص کا دوست یا اس کی بیوی تو ان دونوں سے ذاتی دشمنی یا نفرت بھی قسم کا سبب ہو سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے نسبت صرف پہچان کے لئے ہوئی۔ لیکن قسم کھانے کا سبب تو مضاف الیہ یعنی جس کی طرف اس کی نسبت کی گئی ہے۔ خاص اس میں کسی بات کا ہونا ظاہر نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اسی لئے اس نے معین نہیں کیا ہے۔ بخلاف پہلی صورت کے یعنی جبکہ ملکیت کی نسبت ہو تو یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ اس وقت قسم کھانے کا سبب فلاں مخصوص شخص میں کوئی بات ہے۔
The chapter of oaths in speech. Ashraf al-Bidaya, Urdu Sharh of Hidayah, volume 6. If a person swears: 'I will not speak to this wife of so-and-so or this friend of so-and-so,' and then that relationship is severed and no connection remains, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, he does not become sinful by speaking to the slave, but he becomes sinful by speaking to the woman and friend. Imam Muhammad said he does not become sinful by speaking to the slave either (and Imam Zufar also holds this view, as do Imam Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad). If someone swears: 'By Allah, I will not enter so-and-so's house,' and then that person sells his house, and the oath-taker enters it, then the same difference of opinion applies: according to the two shaykhs, he does not become sinful; according to Imam Muhammad and Zufar, he becomes sinful. Because attribution is for identification, and pointing gives complete identification, removing any possibility of share (common ownership), unlike attribution which can imply share. Therefore, the slave and house are treated like the friend and wife. The proof of the two shaykhs is that the cause motivating the oath must be present in that person or thing. He swore because of so-and-so, not because of his slave etc., since these things are not in themselves such that one would abandon them or have enmity towards them. This is also the case with the slave, whose status is low, not deserving enmity; rather, abandoning speech with them is due to a reason in the owner. So the oath remains only as long as the ownership remains. In contrast, if the relationship is not of ownership but of friendship or marriage, personal enmity or aversion could be the cause of the oath, so the attribution is only for identification, and the cause of the oath is not apparent in the one to whom attribution is made, so it is not restricted.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning oaths that involve the property or relationships of a person. It covers two scenarios: (1) swearing not to speak to the slave, wife, or friend of a specific person, and (2) swearing not to enter a specific person's house which is later sold. The core issue is whether the oath continues to be binding after the relationship of ownership or attribution ceases. The two shaykhs (Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) hold that the oath regarding slaves and houses (items of ownership) is tied to the owner's possession; once ownership ends, the oath is no longer binding, and speaking to the former slave or entering the sold house does not break the oath. In contrast, oaths regarding wives and friends are based on personal attributes, so they remain binding even if the relationship changes. Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar differ, holding that all such oaths are only for identification and thus remain in effect even after sale or severance. The text provides the reasoning: the two shaykhs argue that the motivating cause for the oath lies in the owner, not the owned items, so the oath lapses with ownership. The dissenting view considers the attribution as purely identificatory, like pointing, and thus permanent. The passage then explains the proofs for each position.

Key Terms
حانث (ḥānith): One who breaks his oath and becomes sinful, either by doing what he swore not to do or vice versa
نسبت (nisbat): Attribution or relation to a person, used for identification (e.g., 'the slave of Zayd')
اشارہ (ishārah): Pointing, a method of identification that uniquely specifies the subject
قسم (qasam): An oath swearing by Allah to do or not do something

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the two shaykhs, if someone swears not to speak to 'Amr's slave,' and 'Amr sells the slave, then speaking to that slave:
A) Breaks the oath
B) Does not break the oath
C) Only breaks if done publicly
D) Only breaks if the slave was present

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, oaths motivated by enmity towards an owner lapse when ownership ends, but oaths motivated by personal relationships remain binding.
