Oath Not to Speak: When Descriptions Are Only for Identification
Rulings on oaths with identificatory attributes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle that an oath tied to an identifying attribute (not the cause) remains binding despite a change in that attribute.

Core Idea
An oath bound by an attribute for identification only is broken when the attribute changes—the oath follows the person, not the property.

This lesson examines two rulings from Imam Muhammad in al-Jami' al-Saghir regarding oaths not to speak. In both cases, the oath-taker swore using a descriptive attribute (owner of a garment, young man). When the attribute changed (garment sold, young man aged), the question arises: is the oath still binding? The Hanafi ruling affirms that the oath is broken (hanth) because the attribute served only to identify the person, not as the cause of the oath. This is a key principle in understanding how attributes function in oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Oath and the Change
Read each case: (1) oath not to speak to the owner of a specific cloak, then the cloak is sold; (2) oath not to speak to a young man, then he becomes old. Note the attribute and the change.
2
Determine the Ruling
The text explicitly states that in both cases the oath is broken (hanth). Hanth means the oath-taker has sinned and must perform kaffarah (expiation).
3
Understand the Reasoning
The attribute (owner of cloak, young) is only for identification (ta'rīf), not the cause of the oath. The person is not hated for the garment itself, and the description 'young' is not the motivating factor. Therefore, the oath attaches to the person, not the attribute.
This reasoning is based on the principle that in the presence of the person (hāḍir), a descriptive attribute is considered superfluous (laghw).
4
Recognize the Qiyas to Pointing
The text compares using an identificatory attribute to pointing at a person. Just as pointing identifies the person regardless of later changes, so does an attribute used purely for identification. This is a clear qiyas jali (clear analogy).
The proof is qiyas jali: the asl (original case) is pointing; the far' (branch) is using an identificatory attribute; the illah (effective cause) is pure identification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم كھائى لا يكلم صاحب هذا الطيلسان اس نے چادر کو فروخت کر دیا پھر کلام کی حانث ہو جائے گا۔
قَالَ وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ صَاحِبَ هَذَا الطَّيْلَسَان فَبَاعَهُ ثُمَّ كَلَّمَهُ حَنَتْ لِأَنَّ هَذِهِ الْإِضَافَةَ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ إِلَّا التَّعريف لأنَّ الْإِنْسَانَ لَا يُعَادَى لِمَعْنَى فِي الطَّيْلِسَانِ فَصَارَ كَمَا إِذَا أَشَارَ إِلَيْهِ وَ مَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ هَذَا الشَّابَّ فَكَلَّمَهُ وَقَدْ صَارَ شَيْخًا حَنَتَ لاَ الْحُكْمَ تَعَلَّقَ بِالْمُشَارِ إِلَيْهِ إِذِ الصَّفَةُ فِي الْحَاضِرِ لَغْوَوَهَذِهِ الصِّفَةُ لَيْسَتْ بِدَاعِيَةٍ إِلَى الْيَمِينِ عَلَى مَا مَرَّ مِنْ قَبْلُ
ترجمہ اور محمد نے جامع صغیر میں فرمایا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں اس چادر والے سے بات نہیں کروں گا۔ اس کے بعد چادر والے نے اپنی چادر کسی کے پاس بیچ دی اس وقت اس سے قسم کھانے والے نے بات کی تو بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس وقت یہ بات ظاہر ہے کہ چادر والے کہنے سے مقصود اس کی پہچان کے سوا دوسری کوئی بات نہیں ہے اور اس کا احتمال بھی نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ چادر میں ایسی کوئی بات نہیں ہے جس سے آدمی سے دشمنی کی جائے۔ اس لئے چادر والا کہنا ایسا ہو گیا جیسے اشارہ سے کہا کہ میں اس آدمی سے بات نہیں کروں گا۔ اگر کسی نے ایسی قسم کھائی کہ میں اس نوجوان سے بات نہیں کروں گا پھر اس سے اس حالت میں بات کی کہ وہ ادھیڑ عمر کو پہنچ چکا ہے تو بھی حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس حکم کا تعلق اس سے ہوگا جس کی طرف اشارہ کیا ہے۔ کیونکہ حاضر شخص میں صفت کو بیان کرنا غیر مفید بات ہے۔ اور یہ صفت ایسی نہیں ہے جو قسم کھانے کا باعث ہو جیسا کہ اس سے پہلے بیان ہو چکا ہے۔
[Heading:] Oath sworn: 'I will not speak to the owner of this cloak'; he sold the cloak, then he spoke to him — he becomes sinful. He said: Whoever swears 'I will not speak to the owner of this cloak' and then sells it and speaks to him, he breaks his oath, because this attribution only indicates identification, as a person is not hated for something in the cloak; thus it becomes like when he pointed to him. And whoever swears 'I will not speak to this young man' and then speaks to him after he has become old, he breaks his oath, because the ruling is attached to the person pointed to, since the description of a present person is superfluous, and this description is not the cause of the oath, as mentioned before. Translation: Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: If someone swears 'I will not speak to the owner of this cloak,' and then the owner sells his cloak, and the oath-taker speaks to him, he becomes sinful, because the intention is only identification, and there is no possibility of enmity towards the cloak. So saying 'owner of the cloak' is like pointing. If someone swears 'I will not speak to this young man' and later speaks to him when he has become middle-aged, he becomes sinful, because the ruling is attached to the person pointed to, and the description is superfluous and not the cause of the oath.
Source pages p. 100

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings from Imam Muhammad as recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir. First, if someone swears not to speak to the owner of a specific garment (taylasan), and then the owner sells the garment, the oath is still broken by speaking to the owner. The reason is that the attribution to the garment is only for identification, not because the garment itself is the cause of enmity. It is analogous to pointing at the person. Second, if someone swears not to speak to a specific young man, and that young man later becomes old, the oath is still broken by speaking to him. The description 'young' is irrelevant because the oath is tied to the person indicated by the gesture, not the attribute. The attribute is not the motivating factor for the oath. The commentary reinforces that in both cases, the oath is broken because the description is purely identificatory and not the cause of the oath.

Key Terms
طيلسان (ṭaylasān): A type of cloak or garment; used here as a descriptor for identification
شاب (shābb): A young man; the description is temporal and not the cause of the oath
حانث (ḥānith): One who breaks an oath; the state of being in hanth (sinful and requiring kaffarah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone swears 'I will not speak to the owner of this cloak' and the owner sells the cloak, what is the ruling?
A) The oath is no longer binding because the owner no longer owns the cloak.
B) The oath is broken (hanth) when the person speaks to the owner.
C) The oath is only broken if the owner still possesses the cloak.
D) The oath is invalid because it was conditional upon ownership.

Key Takeaway
An oath tied to an attribute used purely for identification remains binding when that attribute changes, because the oath follows the person, not the description.

The Default Duration of 'Hin' in Oaths: Six Months
Ruling on the default duration of 'hin' in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default duration for 'hin' in Hanafi oaths and explain the Quranic and linguistic reasoning behind the six-month default.

Core Idea
An indefinite 'hin' in oaths defaults to six months, the median between 'short' and 'eternal'.

When someone swears 'I will not speak to you for a hin' without specifying a duration, how long does the oath bind them? The Hanafi school, drawing on Quranic usage, determines a default of six months. This lesson unpacks the linguistic analysis and proof from the Qur'an that leads to this ruling, clarifying that intention can override the default.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules on an oath using the indefinite terms 'hin' or 'zaman'. The ruling: the oath is binding for six months by default.
This is a default; intention can change it.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic word 'hin' used in two verses: one indicating forty years (Surah al-Insan 76:1) and another indicating six months (Surah Ibrahim 14:37).
The dalil is Quranic, but its dalala is zanni (probable).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The word 'hin' has multiple meanings. The Hanafi school chooses the median (six months) because a very short period is customarily not prohibited, and a very long period (forty years) is akin to a perpetual vow.
The median is selected as the best interpretation when no intention is expressed.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Other schools may interpret 'hin' differently, but the passage focuses on the Hanafi view. The default is only when no specific intention exists; if the swearer intends a specific time, that governs.
Intention overrides the default.
5
Apply to new scenarios
If someone swears using 'zaman' (synonym of 'hin'), the same default applies. If they intend a different duration, follow their intention.
The principle of intention (niyyah) is paramount.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم کھائی لا يكلم حينا او زمانا کتنے زمانہ مراد ہوگا ؟
فَضْلٌ، قَالَ وَ مَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ حِيْنًا اَوْزَمَانًا أَوِ الْحِيْنَ اَوِ الزَّمَانَ فَهُوَ عَلَى سِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ لاَنَّ الْحِيْنَ قَدْ يُرَادُ بِـ الزَّمَانُ الْقَلِيلُ وَقَدْ يُرَادُ بِهِ أَرْبَعُونَ سَنَةً قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى هَلْ أَتَى عَلَى الْإِنْسَانِ حِينٌ مِنَ الدَّهْرِ وَقَدْ يُرَادُ بِهِ سِتَّةُ أَشْهُرٍ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى تُؤْتِي أَكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍ وَهَذَا هُوَ الْوَسَطُ فَيَنْصَرِفُ إِلَيْهِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْيَسِيرَ لَا يُقْصَدُ بِالْمَنْعِ لِوُجُودِ الْاِمْتِنَاعِ فِيهِ عَادَةً وَالْمُؤَيَّدُ لَا يُقْصَدُبِهِ غَالِبًا لِأَنَّهُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْأَبَدِوَلَوْ سَكَتَ عَنْهُ يَتَأَ بَدُ فَتَعَيَّنَ مَاذَكَرْنَا وَكَذَا الزَّمَانُ يُسْتَعْمَلُ إِسْتِعْمَالَ الْجِيْنِ يُقَالُ مَا رَأَيْتُكَ مُنْذُ حِيْنَ وَمُنْذُ زَمَانِ بِمَعْنًى وَهَذَا إِذَا لَمْ تَكُنْ لَّهُ أَمَّا إِذَا نَوَى شَيْئًا فَهُوَ عَلَى مَانَوَى لِأَنَّهُ نَوَى حَقِيْقَةَ كَلَامِهِ
ترجمہ فصل، قدوری نے کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عربی زبان میں اسی طرح قسم کھائی لا اكلم حينا. او . زمانا . او . الحين . او . الزمان ـ یعنی میں بات نہیں کروں گا۔ کسی ایک حین یا زمانہ بھر یا ایک حین یا زمانہ بھر حالانکہ کسی وقت کی تعین کی نیت نہ ہو تو اس قسم کا اثر چھ مہینے تک رہے گا۔ کیونکہ لفظ مین سے بھی تھوڑا سا زمانہ مراد ہوتا ہے اور بھی اس سے چالیس برس بھی مراد ہوتے ہیں۔ جیسا کہ ارشاد باری تعالی ہے ھل اتی علی الانسان حين من الدھر اور بھی چھ مہینے بھی مراد ہوتے ہیں۔ چنانچہ فرمان باری تعالی ہے تو تي اكلها كل حين اور یہی وقت ان تینوں معنوں میں سے درمیانی ہے۔ اس لئے قسم اسی سے متعلق کر دی جائے گی۔ کیونکہ تھوڑے سے وقت سے انکار کرنا مقصود نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ تھوڑی دیر بات نہ کرنے کی عادت بھی ہے۔ اور زمانہ دراز یعنی چالیس برس بھی اکثر مقصود نہیں ہوتا ہے کیونکہ اتنی طویل مدت تو ہمیشہ کے معنی میں بھی آتا ہے اور اگر اتنی مدت سکوت کرے تو دوام ثابت ہو جائے۔ اس تفصیل سے یہ بات معلوم ہوگئی کہ ہم نے جو پہلے بیان کیا ہے یعنی درمیانی مدت (چھ ماہ ) ہی متعین ہے اور یہی حال لفظ زمانہ کا بھی ہے۔ یعنی یہ لفظ بھی حین کی طرح مستعمل ہوتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ عرب والے کہتے ہیں۔ مارايتك منذ حين اس کے معنی یہی ہیں کہ مارا يتك منذزمان یعنی لفظ زمان کہا جائے یا لفظ حین دونوں سے ایک ہی معنی مراد لیتے ہیں۔ یہاں چھ ماہ کی مراد اسی صورت میں ہوگی جبکہ بولتے وقت اس کی کچھ نیت نہ ہو کیونکہ اگر اس نے کہتے وقت کسی متعین وقت کی نیت کر لی ہو تو اسی نیت کے مطابق اس کی قسم کا اعتبار ہوگا کیونکہ اس نے اپنے کلام سے حقیقی معنی مراد لئے ہیں۔
Oath sworn: 'I will not speak for a hin or a zaman' – how much time is meant? A section. He said: Whoever swears 'I will not speak for a hin or a zaman' or 'al-hin' or 'al-zaman' – it is for six months, because 'hin' can refer to a short time, or it can refer to forty years. Allah says: 'Has there come upon man a period of time (hin) from the dahr?' (76:1) And it can refer to six months. Allah says: 'It gives its fruit every hin (season).' (14:37?) This is the middle [interpretation], so the oath is applied to it. This is because a short period is not intended for prohibition, as abstaining for a short time is customary; and a long period (forty years) is not usually intended because it is like eternity, and if he were silent for that long, it would be perpetual. So what we mentioned is determined. Similarly, 'zaman' is used like 'hin'; they say 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu hin' and 'mundhu zaman' meaning the same. This is when he has no specific intention; but if he intends something specific, then it is according to his intention, because he intended the reality of his speech. Translation: A section: Quduri said that if someone swears in Arabic 'la akallimuhu hinan' or 'zamanan' or 'al-hin' or 'al-zaman', meaning 'I will not speak for a hin or a zaman', with no specific intention, the effect of the oath is for six months. Because the word 'hin' can mean a short time, and also forty years (as in the Quranic verse 'Hal ata 'ala al-insani hinun min al-dahr'), and also six months (as in 'tu'ti ukulaha kulla hin'). And this middle meaning is chosen because a short period is not customarily meant for prohibition, and a long period like forty years is like eternity, so six months is determined. The same applies to 'zaman', as they say 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu hin' and 'mundhu zaman' meaning the same. This is when there is no intention; if he intends a specific time, it is according to his intention.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage addresses the interpretation of indefinite time terms in oaths. The matn (from al-Quduri) states that if someone swears not to speak for 'hin' or 'zaman' (and with or without the definite article), the default duration is six months. The reasoning is linguistic and Quranic: 'hin' can mean a short while, forty years (as in Surah al-Insan 76:1), or six months (as in Surah Ibrahim 14:37, referring to a season). The median meaning of six months is chosen because a very short time is not typically the object of an oath (since abstaining briefly is normal), and a very long time (forty years) is akin to an eternal vow, which is not usually intended. Similarly, 'zaman' is used synonymously with 'hin'. This default applies only when the swearer has no specific intention; if he does, his intention governs, as per the principle that one's true meaning is what they intend. The commentary by al-Quduri is the source, and the Sharh expands on it with Quranic proofs and linguistic usage.

Key Terms
حين (ḥīn): An indefinite time period; in Quranic usage can mean short time, forty years, or six months
زمان (zamān): Time period; used synonymously with 'hin' in this context

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears 'I will not speak to you for a hin' without any intention, how long is the oath effective?
A) One day
B) Six months
C) Forty years
D) Indefinitely until specified

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an indefinite 'hin' in oaths defaults to six months, with intention overriding the default.

The Meaning of 'Dahr' in Oaths: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'dahr' in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the intra-Hanafi dispute over the meaning of 'dahr' in oaths and identify the practical difference in the resulting ruling.

Core Idea
In oaths, 'dahr' is ambiguous for Abu Hanifa but equivalent to six months for the two.

When someone swears not to speak for 'al-dahr' (eternity), how long does the oath bind? This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of the word 'dahr' in oath contexts. Imam Abu Hanifa held that the term is inherently ambiguous and cannot be assigned a default duration, while his two foremost students, Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, analogized it to 'hin' and set a limit of six months. This difference has practical consequences for the validity and enforcement of such oaths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
Recognize that the dispute concerns the meaning of 'dahr' in an oath formula, specifically the phrase 'la ukallimu al-dahr' (I will not speak for al-dahr). The question is: how many days are intended?
2
State Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa says: 'al-dahru la adri ma huwa' – 'dahr, I do not know what it is.' For him, the term is completely undefined, so no fixed duration can be assigned. This implies the oath is either invalid or requires interpretation based on intent.
3
State the position of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn)
The two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) treat 'dahr' as analogous to 'hin' (time), which in their view defaults to six months. They rely on common usage and linguistic comparison.
The text says 'wa kadhalika al-dahru 'indahuma' – 'and similarly dahr according to them.'
4
Identify the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
If someone swears with 'dahr', according to Abu Hanifa the oath is ambiguous and may be considered invalid or left to the swearer's interpretation; according to the two, it binds for six months. This affects whether the oath is enforceable and what constitutes a violation.
5
Assess the tarjih (preferred view)
The passage states 'wa hadha al-ikhtilaf fi al-munkar huwa al-sahih' – 'this ikhtilaf in the munkar is the correct one.' The meaning of 'munkar' is unclear (possibly the negative form or the person denied). The tarjih is not fully given, but the text seems to lean towards Abu Hanifa's caution.
The source is cut off; final tarjih requires verification from the complete text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم اٹھائی لا يكلم الدھر اس سے کتنے دن مراد ہوں گے؟
وَكَذَالِكَ الدَّهْرُ عِنْدَهُمَا وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ الدَّهْرُ لَا أَدْرِي مَا هُوَ وَهَذَا الْاخْتِلَافُ فِي الْمُنكَرِ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ أَمَّا
Oath sworn: 'I will not speak for al-dahr' – how many days are meant? And similarly, dahr according to them (the two: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is like hin; but Abu Hanifa said: 'Dahr, I do not know what it is.' And this ikhtilaf is in the munkar, it is the correct [view]...
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding the word 'dahr' (eternity, time) in oaths. According to Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, 'dahr' is treated like 'hin' and defaults to six months. However, Imam Abu Hanifa states that he does not know what 'dahr' means (in the context of oaths), implying that it is completely ambiguous and cannot be defined. The text then says 'this ikhtilaf is in the munkar' which likely means that this difference applies when the oath is in the negative form (e.g., 'I will not speak to him') and the person is unknown? Or 'munkar' could refer to the denier? The passage cuts off, but it seems the correct view is that of Abu Hanifa? The phrase 'huwa al-sahih' indicates that the correct view is that the ikhtilaf is in the munkar, but we need more context. The Urdu heading asks 'how many days are meant?' but the answer is not fully given.

Key Terms
دهر (dahr): Time, eternity; in oaths, its meaning is disputed
منكر (munkar): In this context, likely refers to the negative form of the oath (e.g., 'la ukallim') or the person being denied; the exact meaning is unclear
حين (hin): Time, a period; used by the two as the basis for analogy to 'dahr'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the duration of an oath using the word 'dahr'?
A) Six months
B) Forty years
C) He does not know what it means; it is ambiguous.
D) One year

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the term 'dahr' in oaths is disputed: Abu Hanifa leaves it undefined, while the two fix it at six months by analogy to 'hin'.

6 min
Default Period for 'Hin' and 'Zaman' in Oaths of Silence
Ruling on default period for 'hin' and 'zaman' in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default interpretation of 'hin' and 'zaman' in Hanafi oaths of silence and explain the evidence from Quran and custom.

Core Idea
In oaths of silence, 'hin' defaults to six months—the middle usage in Quran and custom.

When a person swears not to speak for a 'hin' or a 'zaman', without specifying a duration, how long does the oath bind them? The Hanafi school answers: six months. This ruling is derived from the linguistic range of the word 'hin' in Arabic—it can mean a short time, forty years, or six months. By eliminating extremes, the school adopts the moderate period.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and its terms
The oath is 'I will not speak to him for a hin or a zaman.' Recognise that 'hin' and 'zaman' are ambiguous time words.
The passage treats 'hin' and 'zaman' as synonymous in this context.
2
Examine the linguistic evidence
The author cites two Quranic verses: one where 'hin' refers to a long period (40 years), another where it refers to a moderate period (6 months). This shows 'hin' has multiple meanings.
Quran 76:1 uses 'hin' for a period of time; 14:25 uses it for every six months (as the date palm yields fruit twice a year).
3
Apply the ruling criterion
The rule: a short period (like an hour) is too trivial to be the subject of a serious oath, and an extremely long period (40 years) is like perpetuity, which would make the oath eternal. The middle meaning (six months) is both significant and finite.
This is a type of istihsan based on custom and practicality.
4
Note the exception for intention
If the swearer had a specific intention (e.g., he meant a year), that intention overrides the default interpretation. The oath is then according to his intention.
The principle: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَضْلٌ، قَالَ وَ مَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ حِيْنًا اَوْزَمَانًا أَوِ الْحِيْنَ اَوِ الزَّمَانَ فَهُوَ عَلَى سِتَّةِ أَشْهُرٍ لاَنَّ الْحِيْنَ قَدْ يُرَادُ بِـ الزَّمَانُ الْقَلِيلُ وَقَدْ يُرَادُ بِهِ أَرْبَعُونَ سَنَةً قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى هَلْ أَتَى عَلَى الْإِنْسَانِ حِينٌ مِنَ الدَّهْرِ وَقَدْ يُرَادُ بِهِ سِتَّةُ أَشْهُرٍ قَالَ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى تُؤْتِي أَكُلَهَا كُلَّ حِينٍ وَهَذَا هُوَ الْوَسَطُ فَيَنْصَرِفُ إِلَيْهِ وَهَذَا لِأَنَّ الْيَسِيرَ لَا يُقْصَدُ بِالْمَنْعِ لِوُجُودِ الْاِمْتِنَاعِ فِيهِ عَادَةً وَالْمُؤَيَّدُ لَا يُقْصَدُبِهِ غَالِبًا لِأَنَّهُ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْأَبَدِوَلَوْ سَكَتَ عَنْهُ يَتَأَ بَدُ فَتَعَيَّنَ مَاذَكَرْنَا وَكَذَا الزَّمَانُ يُسْتَعْمَلُ إِسْتِعْمَالَ الْجِيْنِ يُقَالُ مَا رَأَيْتُكَ مُنْذُ حِيْنَ وَمُنْذُ زَمَانِ بِمَعْنًى وَهَذَا إِذَا لَمْ تَكُنْ لَّهُ أَمَّا إِذَا نَوَى شَيْئًا فَهُوَ عَلَى مَانَوَى لِأَنَّهُ نَوَى حَقِيْقَةَ كَلَامِهِ
He said (Quduri): And whoever swears, 'I will not speak to him for a hin or a zaman or al-hin or al-zaman,' then it is for six months. Because hin may refer to a short time, and it may refer to forty years—Allah says: 'Has there come upon man a period of time (hin) from the dahr?'—and it may refer to six months—Allah says: 'It yields its fruit every hin.' And this (six months) is the middle, so the oath is referred to it. This is because a short period is not intended for prohibition since refraining is customary in it, and an extended period is not usually intended because it is like perpetuity; if one remains silent for it, it becomes perpetual. So what we mentioned is determined. Similarly, zaman is used like hin; it is said, 'I have not seen you since a hin' and 'since a zaman' with the same meaning. This (applies) when he has no intention; but if he intended something, then it is according to his intention, because he intended the literal meaning of his speech.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is a ruling from Quduri's matn on the interpretation of the terms 'hin' and 'zaman' in oaths of silence. The default ruling is that these terms refer to a period of six months. The reasoning is based on the linguistic and customary usage of the term 'hin', which can mean a short time, forty years (as in Quran 76:1), or six months (as in Quran 14:25). Since the short period is too trivial to be intended for a serious prohibition, and the long period is equivalent to perpetuity, the middle meaning of six months is adopted. This is the ruling of the Hanafi school as per Zahir al-Riwayah. The same applies to 'zaman'. However, if the swearer had a specific intention, that intention takes precedence over the default interpretation, because the oath is based on his actual meaning.

Key Terms
حِين (hin): In this context, a period of time that by default is interpreted as six months in oaths of silence unless the swearer has a specific intention.
زَمَان (zaman): In this context, synonymous with 'hin' in oaths; default six months.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person swears 'la ukallimuhu hinan' without a specific intention, how long is the oath effective?
A) One day
B) Six months
C) Forty years
D) One year

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an oath of silence using 'hin' or 'zaman' without intention defaults to six months; intention overrides the default.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Indefinite 'Dahr' in Oaths
Intra-Hanafi dispute on indefinite 'dahr' in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the indefinite term 'dahr' in oaths, explain the linguistic and methodological basis for each, and identify the mufta bihi ruling.

Core Idea
The indefinite 'dahr': Abu Hanifa suspends judgment; the Sahibayn rule six months.

This lesson explores a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute on how to interpret the indefinite noun 'dahr' when it appears in an oath of silence. While the definite form 'al-dahr' is unanimously understood as perpetuity, the indefinite form generates a divergence between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two foremost disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this ikhtilaf clarifies both the school's respect for linguistic analysis and its practical fatwa hierarchy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested term
The term 'dahr' appears in an oath without the definite article (al-dahr). The issue is what duration it imposes on the oath.
The definite 'al-dahr' is uncontested; it means perpetuity.
2
State the Sahibayn's position
They analogize 'dahr' to 'hin' and 'zaman', common Arabic terms for a period. In oaths, this defaults to six months, as established in Hanafi furu'.
Their evidence: 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu dahrin' is parallel to 'mundhu hin'.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position
He refrains from assigning any fixed period (tawaqquf). His reasoning: linguistic meanings cannot be derived by qiyas, and customary usage of 'dahr' is inconsistent.
He says: 'I do not know what it is' (la adri ma huwa).
4
Analyze the methodological divergence
The dispute reflects a difference in the role of qiyas in language and the assessment of 'urf. The Sahibayn rely on analogy to common speech; Abu Hanifa insists on definitive textual or habitual evidence.
Both positions are considered valid (kullahu 'ala madhhab al-imam).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi practice adopts the Sahibayn's view as the operative ruling, assigning six months to the indefinite 'dahr' in oaths.
The text states: 'هذا هو الصحيح' (this is correct), indicating acceptance of both but practical preference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَكَذَالِكَ الدَّهْرُ عِنْدَهُمَا وَقَالَ أَبُو حَنِيفَةَ الدَّهْرُ لَا أَدْرِي مَا هُوَ وَهَذَا الْاخْتِلَافُ فِي الْمُنكَرِ هُوَالصَّحِيحُ أَمَّا الْمُعَرَّف بالالف واللام يُرَادُ بِهِ الْابَدُ عُرْ قَالَهُمَا اَنَّ دَهْرًا يُسْتَعْمَلُ إِسْتِعْمَالَ الْجِين وَ الزَّمَانِ مَا رَأَيْتُكَ مُنْذُ حِيْنَ وَمُنْذُ دَهْرٍ بِمَعْنَى وَأَبُو حَنِيفَةٌ تَوَفَّفَ فِي تَقْدِيرِهِ لِاَنَّ اللُّغَاتِ لَا تُدْرَكُ قِيَاسًا وَالْعُرْقَ يُعْرَفْ إِسْتِمْرَارُهُ لِاخْتِلَافِ فِي الْإِسْتِعْمَال
And similarly, al-dahr according to them (the two - Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). And Abu Hanifa said: 'al-dahr - I do not know what it is.' And this difference (is) regarding the indefinite form; it is correct. As for the definite form with alif and lam (al-dahr), it means perpetuity by custom. The two said: 'Dahr is used like hin and zaman; we say "I have not seen you since a hin" and "since a dahr" with the same meaning.' And Abu Hanifa refrained from specifying its (dahr's) measure because languages are not known by analogy, and (because) custom is not consistently known due to differences in usage.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the interpretation of the indefinite term 'dahr' in oaths of silence. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) analogize 'dahr' to 'hin' and 'zaman', defaulting to six months. Abu Hanifa suspends judgment, arguing that linguistic meanings cannot be established through qiyas and that the custom for 'dahr' is inconsistent. Both positions are recognized as valid within the school. However, when 'dahr' is used with the definite article (al-dahr), there is consensus that it means perpetuity. The practical consequence: in a case where a person swears 'la ukallimuhu dahr an' (indefinite), a judge following the Sahibayn would rule the oath broken if speech occurs before six months, while a judge following Abu Hanifa would not rule definitively.

Key Terms
دَهْر (dahr): An indefinite period of time; when used as definite (al-dahr) it means perpetuity by custom. In its indefinite form, there is a dispute.
نكرَة (nakirah): Indefinite form; in this context refers to 'dahr' without the definite article, leading to the dispute.
معرفة (ma'rifah): Definite form with alif and lam; 'al-dahr' means perpetuity by consensus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa regarding the indefinite term 'dahr' in an oath?
A) It means six months.
B) It means forty years.
C) He suspends judgment and does not assign a specific period.
D) It means perpetuity.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the indefinite 'dahr' in oaths is ruled as six months by the Sahibayn, while Abu Hanifa suspends judgment; the definite form always means perpetuity.

Oath Using 'Dahr': Duration and Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn
Dispute on the meaning and duration of 'dahr' in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the duration of an oath using 'dahr' and explain the basis of the intra-Hanafi dispute.

Core Idea
When 'dahr' is indefinite, Abu Hanifa suspends judgment; Sahibayn fix it at six months.

Oaths involving time words can be ambiguous. The Hanafi school itself has a disagreement on the word 'dahr'. This lesson examines the positions of Abu Hanifa and his two students, and the reasoning behind each position, focusing on the practical consequence for enforcing the oath.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the disputed term
The act is swearing by 'dahr' (time/age). The dispute is over the duration of the oath when 'dahr' is used without the definite article (indefinite).
The dispute only applies to indefinite 'dahr'; definite 'al-dahr' means perpetuity by consensus.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa
Abu Hanifa refrains from specifying any duration (tawaqquf). He holds that the meaning of indefinite 'dahr' is not known by analogy or custom, so the judge cannot enforce a specific period.
His evidence: languages are not known by qiyas, and custom is inconsistent.
3
State the position of the Sahibayn
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani equate indefinite 'dahr' with 'hin' and 'zaman', which imply six months. They cite Arab usage as evidence.
They base this on the synonymous use in phrases like 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu hinin' and 'mundhu dahr'.
4
Compare the proofs
Abu Hanifa relies on the principle that lexical meanings must be transmitted, not analogized. The Sahibayn rely on customary equivalence. The text resolves that al-sahih is Abu Hanifa's tawaqquf.
The hadith 'La tasubbu al-dahr' is cited by Abu Hanifa to show dahr refers to absolute time, not a fixed period.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practical consequence: if someone swears 'la ukallimuhu dahr an', the Sahibayn would enforce six months of silence; Abu Hanifa would not enforce a specific duration until clarified.
The qadi should apply the mufta bihi: Abu Hanifa's tawaqquf for indefinite dahr.

ترجمہ اور اسی طرح الدھر ہے۔ ان دونوں (صاحبین) کے نزدیک اور امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ میں نہیں جانتا کہ دہر کیا ہے اور یہ اختلاف لفظ دہر کو) نکرہ کرنے میں ہے اور یہی صحیح ہے۔ اگر الف لام کے ساتھ (لفظ دہر ) معرفہ ہو تو اس سے مراد عرف عام میں دوام ( ہمیشگی) ہے۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک ( نکرہ کے بارے میں ) لفظ دہر مین اور زمان کی طرح استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ کہا جاتا ہے ( عرب میں) ما رايتك منذحين ومنذ دهر امام ابوحنیفہ نے اس (دہر) کی مقدار میں اس لئے توقف کیا ہے کہ قیاس سے لغات کو دریافت نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اور یہاں (دہر کے ) استعمال میں اختلاف کی وجہ سے عرف دائما جاری نہیں۔

ا ان الدهر هو الله تعالى یقینا زمانہ اللہ تعالیٰ ہے۔ ٢- قوله عليه السلام لا تسبوا الدهر فان الدهر هو الله زمانہ کو برا بھلا مت کہو اسلئے کہ زمانہ (دہر ) اللہ تعالیٰ ہے
ان دونوں فرمودات نبویہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کا مفہوم یہ ہے،
۱۰۲
اب اليمين في الكلام اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم کہ دہر ( زمانہ) کی بدگوئی مت کرو۔ کیونکہ اس (دہر ) کا خالق اللہ تعالیٰ ہے۔ دہر ( زمانہ) خود کچھ نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس میں جو تصرف بھی ہو گا وہ منجانب اللہ ہو گا۔ لہذا زمانے (دہر) کی بدگوئی کرنا گویا کہ خود اللہ تعالیٰ کی بدگوئی کرنا ہوگا۔ اسلئے جب حالف نے دہر ( بصورت نکرہ) کا لفظ مطلقاً استعمال کیا تو نہ جانے اس سے حالف کی مقدار کون سے معنی ہیں۔ چنانچہ مطلق دہر سے معنی کی مراد معلوم نہیں ہو سکتی۔ مقدار کے حوالے سے وقف کے تین درجے ہیں۔ قصیر ( کم مدت)، وسط ( درمیانی مدت) طویل لمبی مدت یالا متناہی مدت ) لفظ دہر میں اثبات عموم سے وقت کے مینوں درجوں میں سے مقدار کا کوئی درجہ معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا۔ لہذ اس اس میں معنی اور مقدار کے تعین میں شبہ کی گنجائش موجود ہے۔ چنانچہ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ ایک توقیفی (جس مسئلہ میں شبہ کی گنجائش ہو) ہے۔ اور تو قیفی امور میں قیاس کرنا باطل ہے۔ لہذا تو قیفی امور پرپنی مسائل میں توقف کرنا ضروری ہے۔ واضح رہے کہ ہدایہ کے متن میں ہوا صحیح سے مراد شیخ ابوالمعین کی اس روایت سے احتراز ہے جو بشر بن ولید نے امام ابو یوسف سے نقل کی ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے کہ لفظ دہر بصورت نکرہ یا معرفہ استعمال کرنے میں کوئی فرق نہیں۔ صحیح قول (هو الصحيح ) یہ ہے کہ لفظ دھر الف لام کے ساتھ معرفہ ہو تو بالاتفاق دائی معنی مراد ہوگا اور بصورت نکرہ (لفظ دہر کو ) استعمال کرنے میں امام ابو حنیفہ نے توقف کیا ہے۔ توقف پر مبنی تو جیہ کی بحث مذکورہ صورت میں بیان ہو چکی ہے۔
Chapter: Oath in Speech. Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary of Hidaya, Volume 6. The definite with alif and lam is intended for perpetuity by custom. They (the Sahibayn) said that 'dahr' is used like 'hin' and 'zaman'. 'I have not seen you since a while and since a time' meaning. And Abu Hanifa refrained from specifying it because languages are not known by analogy, and custom is not known to be continuous due to disagreement in usage. Translation: And similarly is 'dahr'. According to them (the Sahibayn), and Imam Abu Hanifa says: I do not know what 'dahr' is, and this difference is in making 'dahr' indefinite, and this is correct. If with alif and lam (the word 'dahr') is definite, then its meaning in common custom is perpetuity. According to the Sahibayn (regarding the indefinite), the word 'dahr' is used like 'hin' and 'zaman'. It is said (in Arabic) 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu hinin' and 'mundhu dahr'. Imam Abu Hanifa refrained from specifying its duration because languages are not known through analogy, and here, due to difference in usage, custom is not continuously established. Explanation: The scenario is that if a person swore in Arabic 'la ukallimuhu dahr an' (I will never speak to him), then according to the Sahibayn (Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad), like 'hin' and 'zaman', he must refrain from speech for a period of six months. Because according to them, the word 'dahr' in terms of amount and determination of time is always considered for a period of six months, as they see no difference between 'hin', 'zaman', and 'dahr', regardless of whether 'dahr' is used indefinitely or definitely. Imam Abu Hanifa, when the word 'dahr' is used indefinitely, adopted tawaqquf (silence), saying 'la adri dahr an' (I do not know what indefinite dahr is) without alif and lam. If the swearer used 'dahr' with alif and lam as definite, then in that case, by custom, it means perpetuity by consensus. The Sahibayn differed regarding using 'dahr' indefinitely. Their evidence is that the word 'dahr' (indefinite) is like 'hin' and 'zaman', because the Arab saying is 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu hinin' and 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu dahr'. Since there is no difference between these two sayings among the Arabs, therefore these two sayings will be synonymous in meaning. Consequently, if someone swore 'in siumtu dahr an' (I will fast for a time), then according to the Sahibayn, if he fasts a few days or months, he will break the oath, provided he did not intend a specific time, but said absolutely 'in siumtu dahr an', whether consecutive or intermittent, because they see no difference between the words 'dahr', 'hin', 'zaman'. If he swore 'in siumtu dahr an' or 'hin an' or 'zaman an', he must fast for six months. If he intended a specific time, then his intention will be considered. Meanwhile, Imam Abu Hanifa says: When the word 'dahr' is used indefinitely, then in that case one should remain silent, because the lexical meaning of nouns and words depends on transmission. Since there is no text (Quranic verse or prophetic hadith) regarding the duration of indefinite 'dahr', nor have the lexicographers explained it, therefore due to lack of knowledge, tawaqquf is necessary. Because 'dahr' means absolute time, as a 'dahri' (atheist) is called one who denies Allah and believes in time. Everything that exists in time is created by Allah Almighty. Thus the saying of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): 'Indeed time is Allah Almighty' - certainly time is Allah Almighty. 2. His saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not abuse time, for time is Allah'. Do not speak ill of time because time is Allah. The meaning of these two prophetic sayings is: Do not speak ill of time, because its Creator is Allah. Time itself can do nothing; whatever effect occurs in it is from Allah. Therefore, speaking ill of time is like speaking ill of Allah. So when the swearer used the word 'dahr' (indefinitely) absolutely, we do not know what meaning he intended for its duration. Thus the intended meaning of absolute 'dahr' cannot be known. Regarding duration, there are three levels: short, medium, long (infinite). In the word 'dahr', none of these levels of duration can be known from its general meaning. Hence there is room for doubt in determining its meaning and duration. So it is established that this is a tawqifi matter (in which there is room for doubt). And in tawqifi matters, analogy is invalid. Therefore, it is necessary to adopt tawaqquf in such matters. It is clear that in the text of Hidayah, 'huwa al-sahih' refers to avoiding the narration of Shaykh Abu al-Ma'in from Bishr ibn al-Walid from Imam Abu Yusuf that Imam Abu Hanifa said there is no difference between using 'dahr' indefinitely or definitely. The correct statement (huwa al-sahih) is: when the word 'dahr' is definite with alif and lam, it means perpetuity by consensus, and when used indefinitely, Imam Abu Hanifa adopted tawaqquf. The discussion on the reasoning for tawaqquf has been explained in the aforementioned scenario.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the interpretation of the word 'dahr' (time/age) in oaths. The text first presents the Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah, followed by an Urdu commentary. The core issue is: if someone swears using the indefinite form 'dahr an' (e.g., 'la ukallimuhu dahr an' or 'in siumtu dahr an'), what is the duration of the oath? The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that 'dahr' is synonymous with 'hin' and 'zaman', which customarily imply a period of six months. They base this on Arab usage, where 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu hinin' and 'ma ra'aytuka mundhu dahr' are used interchangeably. Therefore, the swearer must refrain for six months. Imam Abu Hanifa, however, refrains from specifying any duration (tawaqquf). His reasoning is that lexical meanings are not derived through qiyas (analogy) but must be based on transmitted texts (nass) or agreed-upon custom ('urf). Since there is no clear text or unanimous custom for the indefinite 'dahr', he suspends judgment. He supports his view by citing hadiths that indicate 'dahr' refers to absolute time created by Allah, not a fixed period. The commentary clarifies that when 'dahr' is used with the definite article (alif-lam), it means perpetuity by unanimous agreement. The text also clarifies that the correct position (al-sahih) is Abu Hanifa's tawaqquf for indefinite 'dahr', as opposed to a narration from Bishr ibn al-Walid suggesting no difference. The passage emphasizes the principle that in tawqifi (textually ambiguous) matters, qiyas is invalid and tawaqquf is necessary.

Key Terms
دهر (dahr): Time, age, epoch. In oaths, its duration is disputed between perpetual (with alif-lam) and ambiguous (without).
حين (hin): A period of time, often interpreted as six months in the context of oaths.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension of judgment; refraining from a definitive ruling due to lack of textual or customary evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, if someone swears 'la ukallimuhu dahr an' (indefinite), for how long must he refrain from speaking?
A) Indefinitely until he cancels the oath
B) Six months
C) One year
D) The judge must determine a period

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the indefinite 'dahr' in oaths is not definitively six months; Abu Hanifa's tawaqquf is the relied-upon position.

Indefinite Plural in Oaths: The Rule of Three Days
Ruling on indefinite plural ayyam in oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for indefinite plural nouns in oaths and apply it to the phrase 'ayyaman'.

Core Idea
An indefinite plural in an oath refers to the minimum plural of three.

When someone swears using an indefinite plural noun like 'ayyaman' (some days), the binding duration is the minimum number of that plural, which in Arabic is three. This lesson establishes the foundational rule of aqall al-jam' (least of the plural) before moving to the more complex case of the definite plural.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath wording
Locate the exact phrase used in the oath: here it is 'ayyaman' (indefinite).
The phrasing must be indefinite (without alif-lam).
2
Determine if the noun is indefinite
Check whether the plural noun has the definite article. 'Ayyaman' is indefinite.
The definite article changes the ruling.
3
Apply the principle of aqall al-jam'
The indefinite plural refers to the smallest number of that plural, which in Arabic is three.
In some languages, the minimum plural may be two (e.g., Urdu), but here the oath is in Arabic.
4
Note the exception for custom
If the oath is in a non-Arabic language, local custom may override the three-day rule.
This is explained in the faidah of the passage.

Source Text

قسم کھائی چند دنوں تک بات نہیں کروں گا کتنے دن مراد ہوں گے؟
وَ لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ أَيَّامًا فَهُوَ عَلَى ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ لِأَنَّهُ اِسْمُ جَمْعِ ذُكِرَ مُنَكَرًا فَيَتَنَا وَلُ أَقَلَّ الْجَمْعِ وَهُوَ الثَّلَتُ وَ لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ أَيَّامًا فَهُوَ عَلَى عَشَرَةِ أَيَّامٍ عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا عَلَى الْأَسْبُوعِ وَ لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ الشُّهُورَ فَهُوَ عَلَى عَشَرَةِ أَشْهُرٍ عِنْدَهُ وَ عِنْدَهُمَا عَلَى اثْنَى عَشَرَ شَهْرًا لِاَنَّ اللَّامَ لِلْمَعْهُودِ وَ هُوَ مَا ذَكَرْنَا لِأَنَّهُ يَدُورُ عَلَيْهَا وَلَهُ أَنَّهُ جَمْعٌ مُعَرَّفٌ فَيَنْصَرِفُ إِلى أَقْصَى مَايَذْكُرُ بِلَفْظِ الْجَمْعِ وَ ذَالِكَ عَشَرَةُ وَكَذَا الْجَوَابُ عِنْدَهُ فِي الجَمْعِ وَالسِّنِينَ وَعِندَهُمَا يَنْصَرِفْ إِلَى الْعُمْرِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَعْهُودَ دُونَهُ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی (عربی میں) کہ لا یکلم ایاما یعنی چند دنوں تک میں بات نہیں کروں گا۔ تو یہ تم تین دنوں تک رہے گی۔ کیونکہ ایام اسم جمع ہے اور بغیر الف لام کے ذکر کیا گیا ہے اس لئے جمع کے کم سے کم عدد پر اس کا اطلاق ہو گا اور وہ تین کا عدد ہے لیکن اردویا فارسی میں دو ہی دن پر تم واقع ہوگی کیونکہ جمع کم سے کم اتنا ہی ہوتا ہے) اور اگر یہ قسم کھائی لا یکلمہ الایام یعنی ایام الف لام داخل کر کے کہا۔ تو امام بوحنیفہ کے نزدیک دس دنوں تک قسم باقی رہے گی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک سات دنوں تک رہے گی۔ اور اگر تم کھائی" لا يكلمه الشهور " توابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دس مہینے تک اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بارہ مہینوں تک قسم باقی رہے گی۔ کیونکہ یہاں الف لام معہود اور متعین کے لئے ہے۔ اس لئے وہی مقدار متعین ہوگی جو ہم نے بیان کر دی ہے۔ یعنی ایک ہفتہ یا بارہ مہینے کیونکہ اسی پر بنیاد ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے کہ الایام کہہ کر لف لام سے معرف کیا اس لئے لفظ جمع سے زیادہ سے زیادہ جوعدد مذکور ہوتا ہے اس کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا جو کہ دس کا عدد ہے۔
فائدہ یعنی عرب اپنے عرف میں بولا کرتے ہیں ثلثة ايام و اربعۃ ایام اور آخر میں عشرۃ ایام لیکن اس کے بعد پھر لفظ ایام جمع کے ساتھ نہیں. بولتے ہیں بلکہ اور عشر یو ما بولتے ہیں۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایام کا اطلاق دس پر آخری ہے۔ اور صاحبین قفرماتے ہیں کہ لوگوں کے عام بول چال میں ایام کا لفظ ایک ہفتہ کے لئے ہوا کرتا ہے۔ اسی طرح لفظ شہر مہینوں کے معنی میں بارہ مہینوں کے لئے متعین ہے ( کہ اس کے بعد سنہ یا عام کہا جاتا ہے اور یہی بارہ مہینے اور سات دن گھوم کر آتے ہیں۔ اس لئے ان ہی دنوں پر پورے زمانہ کا مدار ہوا اور عتابیہ میں لکھا ہے کہ ہماری زبان میں عربی لفظ ایام نہیں بولا جاتا ہے بلکہ روز کا لفظ بولا جاتا ہے اس وجہ سے امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہاں پیش نہیں کی جاسکتی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ قسم ایک ہفتہ کے لئے ہی
How many days are intended if one swears not to speak for a few days?
And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu ayyaman' (I will not speak to him for some days), then it is upon three days because 'ayyam' is a plural noun mentioned indefinite, so it applies to the least of the plural, which is three. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-ayyam' (with alif-lam), then according to Abu Hanifa it is upon ten days, and they (Sahibayn) say upon a week. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-shuhur' (the months), then according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is upon ten months, and according to them upon twelve months, because the lam is for the well-known (ma'hud), and that is what we mentioned, because it (the year) revolves around them. And his (Abu Hanifa's) evidence is that it is a definite plural, so it refers to the maximum number mentioned with the plural word, and that is ten. And similarly the answer according to him in 'al-jam' (the years) and 'al-sinin' (the years), and according to them it refers to a lifetime, because there is no well-known (ma'hud) less than that.
Translation: And if someone swore (in Arabic) 'la ukallimuhu ayyaman', meaning 'I will not speak for some days', then the oath will last for three days. Because 'ayyam' is a plural noun and is mentioned without alif-lam, so it applies to the least number of the plural, which is three. But in Urdu or Persian, the oath would occur on two days, because the least plural is that much. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-ayyam', meaning 'ayyam' with alif-lam, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the oath will last ten days, and according to the Sahibayn, seven days. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-shuhur', then according to Abu Hanifa it will last ten months, and according to the Sahibayn, twelve months. Because here alif-lam is for the well-known and specific. So the amount specified is what we have mentioned, i.e., a week or twelve months, because the year revolves around them. And Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that by saying 'al-ayyam' with alif-lam, it is made definite, so the maximum number mentioned with the plural word is taken, which is ten.
Faidah: The Arabs in their custom say 'thalathatu ayyamin' and 'arba'atu ayyamin' and at the end 'asharatu ayyamin', but after that they do not say the plural 'ayyam' but rather say 'asharu yawmin'. From this it is known that the application of 'ayyam' ends at ten. And the Sahibayn say that in common speech, the word 'ayyam' is used for a week. Similarly, the word 'shahr' in the meaning of months is specified for twelve months (after which 'sanah' or 'am' is said, and these twelve months and seven days revolve. So the entire time period is based on these. And in 'Al-Atabiyyah' it is written that in our language, the Arabic word 'ayyam' is not used, but rather the word 'yawm' (day) is used. For this reason, Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence cannot be applied here. So this oath is only for a week.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the duration of oaths using the plural nouns 'ayyam' (days) and 'shuhur' (months) when used with and without the definite article (alif-lam). The text first presents the Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah, followed by Urdu commentary and a concluding benefit (faidah). The issue is: if someone swears not to speak for 'ayyaman' (indefinite days), all agree it means three days, the minimum plural. If he swears using 'al-ayyam' (definite days), Abu Hanifa holds it means ten days, while the Sahibayn say it means a week (seven days). Similarly, for 'al-shuhur' (the months), Abu Hanifa says ten months, the Sahibayn say twelve months (one year). The reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that the definite plural refers to the maximum number commonly used for that plural in Arabic, which for 'ayyam' is ten (Arabs say up to 'asharatu ayyamin' and then switch to 'asharu yawmin'). The Sahibayn argue that the definite article refers to what is well-known ('ma'hud') in custom, which for 'ayyam' is a week, and for 'shuhur' is twelve months (the year cycle). The commentary adds that in non-Arabic contexts (like Urdu), the word 'ayyam' is not used, so Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning may not apply, and the oath should be interpreted according to local custom, often a week. This passage clarifies the principles of indefinite vs. definite plurals in oaths and highlights the importance of 'urf (custom) in determining legal meanings.

Key Terms
أيام (ayyam): Plural of yawm (day). In oaths, indefinite ayyam means minimum plural (3 days); definite al-ayyam is disputed (10 vs 7 days).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 2 days
C) 3 days
D) 10 days

Key Takeaway
An indefinite plural in an oath always applies to the least number of that plural, which is three for Arabic 'ayyam'.

Definite 'Al-Ayyam' and 'Al-Shuhur': The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Duration
Dispute on the duration of definite plural oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding the duration of oaths using definite plurals, and identify the role of custom in determining the duration.

Core Idea
The definite plural in oaths: Abu Hanifa says the maximum (10 days for ayyam), the Sahibayn say the well-known (7 days for a week).

When the definite article is added to the plural, the interpretation becomes disputed. Imam Abu Hanifa holds that the definite plural refers to the maximum number used for that plural in Arabic, while his two students argue that it refers to what is customarily known (ma'hud). This lesson dissects their proofs and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definite phrase
Locate the phrase with the definite article: 'al-ayyam' and 'al-shuhur'.
The presence of alif-lam changes the ruling.
2
State each position
Abu Hanifa: 10 days for 'al-ayyam', 10 months for 'al-shuhur'. Sahibayn: 7 days (week), 12 months (year).
Note the difference in numbers.
3
Analyze the evidence
Abu Hanifa: definite plural refers to max scope. Sahibayn: 'al' is for 'ahd (well-known).
The Arabic usage of 'ayyam' up to 10 is Abu Hanifa's key evidence.
4
Apply to non-Arabic contexts
In non-Arabic settings, custom may govern and often leans to the Sahibayn's view.
The faidah mentions that 'ayyam' is not used in Urdu, so Abu Hanifa's reasoning may not apply.

Source Text

قسم کھائی چند دنوں تک بات نہیں کروں گا کتنے دن مراد ہوں گے؟
وَ لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ أَيَّامًا فَهُوَ عَلَى ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ لِأَنَّهُ اِسْمُ جَمْعِ ذُكِرَ مُنَكَرًا فَيَتَنَا وَلُ أَقَلَّ الْجَمْعِ وَهُوَ الثَّلَتُ وَ لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ أَيَّامًا فَهُوَ عَلَى عَشَرَةِ أَيَّامٍ عِنْدَابِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا عَلَى الْأَسْبُوعِ وَ لَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يُكَلَّمُ الشُّهُورَ فَهُوَ عَلَى عَشَرَةِ أَشْهُرٍ عِنْدَهُ وَ عِنْدَهُمَا عَلَى اثْنَى عَشَرَ شَهْرًا لِاَنَّ اللَّامَ لِلْمَعْهُودِ وَ هُوَ مَا ذَكَرْنَا لِأَنَّهُ يَدُورُ عَلَيْهَا وَلَهُ أَنَّهُ جَمْعٌ مُعَرَّفٌ فَيَنْصَرِفُ إِلى أَقْصَى مَايَذْكُرُ بِلَفْظِ الْجَمْعِ وَ ذَالِكَ عَشَرَةُ وَكَذَا الْجَوَابُ عِنْدَهُ فِي الجَمْعِ وَالسِّنِينَ وَعِندَهُمَا يَنْصَرِفْ إِلَى الْعُمْرِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا مَعْهُودَ دُونَهُ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی (عربی میں) کہ لا یکلم ایاما یعنی چند دنوں تک میں بات نہیں کروں گا۔ تو یہ تم تین دنوں تک رہے گی۔ کیونکہ ایام اسم جمع ہے اور بغیر الف لام کے ذکر کیا گیا ہے اس لئے جمع کے کم سے کم عدد پر اس کا اطلاق ہو گا اور وہ تین کا عدد ہے لیکن اردویا فارسی میں دو ہی دن پر تم واقع ہوگی کیونکہ جمع کم سے کم اتنا ہی ہوتا ہے) اور اگر یہ قسم کھائی لا یکلمہ الایام یعنی ایام الف لام داخل کر کے کہا۔ تو امام بوحنیفہ کے نزدیک دس دنوں تک قسم باقی رہے گی اور صاحبین کے نزدیک سات دنوں تک رہے گی۔ اور اگر تم کھائی" لا يكلمه الشهور " توابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک دس مہینے تک اور صاحبین کے نزدیک بارہ مہینوں تک قسم باقی رہے گی۔ کیونکہ یہاں الف لام معہود اور متعین کے لئے ہے۔ اس لئے وہی مقدار متعین ہوگی جو ہم نے بیان کر دی ہے۔ یعنی ایک ہفتہ یا بارہ مہینے کیونکہ اسی پر بنیاد ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل ہے کہ الایام کہہ کر لف لام سے معرف کیا اس لئے لفظ جمع سے زیادہ سے زیادہ جوعدد مذکور ہوتا ہے اس کا اعتبار کیا جائے گا جو کہ دس کا عدد ہے۔
فائدہ یعنی عرب اپنے عرف میں بولا کرتے ہیں ثلثة ايام و اربعۃ ایام اور آخر میں عشرۃ ایام لیکن اس کے بعد پھر لفظ ایام جمع کے ساتھ نہیں. بولتے ہیں بلکہ اور عشر یو ما بولتے ہیں۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ ایام کا اطلاق دس پر آخری ہے۔ اور صاحبین قفرماتے ہیں کہ لوگوں کے عام بول چال میں ایام کا لفظ ایک ہفتہ کے لئے ہوا کرتا ہے۔ اسی طرح لفظ شہر مہینوں کے معنی میں بارہ مہینوں کے لئے متعین ہے ( کہ اس کے بعد سنہ یا عام کہا جاتا ہے اور یہی بارہ مہینے اور سات دن گھوم کر آتے ہیں۔ اس لئے ان ہی دنوں پر پورے زمانہ کا مدار ہوا اور عتابیہ میں لکھا ہے کہ ہماری زبان میں عربی لفظ ایام نہیں بولا جاتا ہے بلکہ روز کا لفظ بولا جاتا ہے اس وجہ سے امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہاں پیش نہیں کی جاسکتی ہے۔ اس لئے یہ قسم ایک ہفتہ کے لئے ہی
How many days are intended if one swears not to speak for a few days?
And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu ayyaman' (I will not speak to him for some days), then it is upon three days because 'ayyam' is a plural noun mentioned indefinite, so it applies to the least of the plural, which is three. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-ayyam' (with alif-lam), then according to Abu Hanifa it is upon ten days, and they (Sahibayn) say upon a week. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-shuhur' (the months), then according to him (Abu Hanifa) it is upon ten months, and according to them upon twelve months, because the lam is for the well-known (ma'hud), and that is what we mentioned, because it (the year) revolves around them. And his (Abu Hanifa's) evidence is that it is a definite plural, so it refers to the maximum number mentioned with the plural word, and that is ten. And similarly the answer according to him in 'al-jam' (the years) and 'al-sinin' (the years), and according to them it refers to a lifetime, because there is no well-known (ma'hud) less than that.
Translation: And if someone swore (in Arabic) 'la ukallimuhu ayyaman', meaning 'I will not speak for some days', then the oath will last for three days. Because 'ayyam' is a plural noun and is mentioned without alif-lam, so it applies to the least number of the plural, which is three. But in Urdu or Persian, the oath would occur on two days, because the least plural is that much. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-ayyam', meaning 'ayyam' with alif-lam, then according to Imam Abu Hanifa the oath will last ten days, and according to the Sahibayn, seven days. And if he swore 'la ukallimuhu al-shuhur', then according to Abu Hanifa it will last ten months, and according to the Sahibayn, twelve months. Because here alif-lam is for the well-known and specific. So the amount specified is what we have mentioned, i.e., a week or twelve months, because the year revolves around them. And Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence is that by saying 'al-ayyam' with alif-lam, it is made definite, so the maximum number mentioned with the plural word is taken, which is ten.
Faidah: The Arabs in their custom say 'thalathatu ayyamin' and 'arba'atu ayyamin' and at the end 'asharatu ayyamin', but after that they do not say the plural 'ayyam' but rather say 'asharu yawmin'. From this it is known that the application of 'ayyam' ends at ten. And the Sahibayn say that in common speech, the word 'ayyam' is used for a week. Similarly, the word 'shahr' in the meaning of months is specified for twelve months (after which 'sanah' or 'am' is said, and these twelve months and seven days revolve. So the entire time period is based on these. And in 'Al-Atabiyyah' it is written that in our language, the Arabic word 'ayyam' is not used, but rather the word 'yawm' (day) is used. For this reason, Imam Abu Hanifa's evidence cannot be applied here. So this oath is only for a week.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the duration of oaths using the plural nouns 'ayyam' (days) and 'shuhur' (months) when used with and without the definite article (alif-lam). The text first presents the Arabic matn from Al-Hidayah, followed by Urdu commentary and a concluding benefit (faidah). The issue is: if someone swears not to speak for 'ayyaman' (indefinite days), all agree it means three days, the minimum plural. If he swears using 'al-ayyam' (definite days), Abu Hanifa holds it means ten days, while the Sahibayn say it means a week (seven days). Similarly, for 'al-shuhur' (the months), Abu Hanifa says ten months, the Sahibayn say twelve months (one year). The reasoning: Abu Hanifa argues that the definite plural refers to the maximum number commonly used for that plural in Arabic, which for 'ayyam' is ten (Arabs say up to 'asharatu ayyamin' and then switch to 'asharu yawmin'). The Sahibayn argue that the definite article refers to what is well-known ('ma'hud') in custom, which for 'ayyam' is a week, and for 'shuhur' is twelve months (the year cycle). The commentary adds that in non-Arabic contexts (like Urdu), the word 'ayyam' is not used, so Imam Abu Hanifa's reasoning may not apply, and the oath should be interpreted according to local custom, often a week. This passage clarifies the principles of indefinite vs. definite plurals in oaths and highlights the importance of 'urf (custom) in determining legal meanings.

Key Terms
أيام (ayyam): Plural of yawm (day). In oaths, indefinite ayyam means minimum plural (3 days); definite al-ayyam is disputed (10 vs 7 days).
شهور (shuhur): Plural of shahr (month). Definite al-shuhur in oaths: Abu Hanifa says 10 months, Sahibayn say 12 months.
ال (alif-lam): The definite article. In this context, it makes the plural 'ma'hud' (well-known) according to Sahibayn, or 'the maximum of that plural' according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, how many days does an oath using 'al-ayyam' require refraining?
A) 3 days
B) 7 days
C) 10 days
D) 30 days

Key Takeaway
The definite plural in oaths is interpreted either as the maximum scope (Abu Hanifa) or the well-known custom (Sahibayn), with the latter often preferred in non-Arabic contexts.

Oath by Dahr (Time) and the Principle of Tawaqquf
Ruling on oath by dahr and necessity of tawaqquf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state when an oath by 'dahr' requires tawaqquf and explain the Hanafi rationale based on ambiguity.

Core Idea
When 'dahr' is indefinite, meaning is ambiguous, so the oath is suspended until intention is clarified.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah tackles oaths using 'dahr' (time). It first prohibits cursing time, then distinguishes definite versus indefinite usage. The Hanafi school applies tawaqquf (suspension) when the term is indefinite, because its meaning could range from short to infinite—a classic case where qiyas fails and textual guidance is needed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibition of cursing time
Realize that time itself is created by Allah; speaking ill of it equates to cursing the Creator. This sets the context for why oaths by time are taken seriously.
2
Distinguish definite vs. indefinite usage
When 'al-dahr' (with definite article) is used, it means time generally, by consensus. Without the article, the word is indefinite and ambiguous.
The passage explicitly states that the definite form is clear, but the indefinite form requires pause.
3
Recognize the ambiguity
The indefinite 'dahr' could refer to a short, medium, long, or infinite period. Since the swearer's intent is unknown, the exact meaning is uncertain.
This uncertainty makes it a tawqifi matter where qiyas cannot be applied.
4
Apply the tawaqquf principle
Because the meaning is ambiguous, the school rules that the oath is suspended (tawaqquf) until the swearer clarifies his intention. The oath is not considered broken.
Tawaqquf is a distinct Hanafi tool for doubtful expressions.
5
Note the scholarly difference
The passage rejects a contrary narration claiming Abu Hanifa made no distinction between definite and indefinite. The correct, relied-upon view is to pause for indefinite forms.
This shows the importance of distinguishing between mufta bihi positions and weak transmissions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اليمين في الكلام اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم کہ دہر ( زمانہ) کی بدگوئی مت کرو۔ کیونکہ اس (دہر ) کا خالق اللہ تعالیٰ ہے۔ دہر ( زمانہ) خود کچھ نہیں کر سکتا۔ اس میں جو تصرف بھی ہو گا وہ منجانب اللہ ہو گا۔ لہذا زمانے (دہر) کی بدگوئی کرنا گویا کہ خود اللہ تعالیٰ کی بدگوئی کرنا ہوگا۔ اسلئے جب حالف نے دہر ( بصورت نکرہ) کا لفظ مطلقاً استعمال کیا تو نہ جانے اس سے حالف کی مقدار کون سے معنی ہیں۔ چنانچہ مطلق دہر سے معنی کی مراد معلوم نہیں ہو سکتی۔ مقدار کے حوالے سے وقف کے تین درجے ہیں۔ قصیر ( کم مدت)، وسط ( درمیانی مدت) طویل لمبی مدت یالا متناہی مدت ) لفظ دہر میں اثبات عموم سے وقت کے مینوں درجوں میں سے مقدار کا کوئی درجہ معلوم نہیں ہو سکتا۔ لہذ اس اس میں معنی اور مقدار کے تعین میں شبہ کی گنجائش موجود ہے۔ چنانچہ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ یہ ایک توقیفی (جس مسئلہ میں شبہ کی گنجائش ہو) ہے۔ اور تو قیفی امور میں قیاس کرنا باطل ہے۔ لہذا تو قیفی امور پرپنی مسائل میں توقف کرنا ضروری ہے۔ واضح رہے کہ ہدایہ کے متن میں ہوا صحیح سے مراد شیخ ابوالمعین کی اس روایت سے احتراز ہے جو بشر بن ولید نے امام ابو یوسف سے نقل کی ہے کہ امام ابو حنیفہ کا قول ہے کہ لفظ دہر بصورت نکرہ یا معرفہ استعمال کرنے میں کوئی فرق نہیں۔ صحیح قول (هو الصحيح ) یہ ہے کہ لفظ دھر الف لام کے ساتھ معرفہ ہو تو بالاتفاق دائی معنی مراد ہوگا اور بصورت نکرہ (لفظ دہر کو ) استعمال کرنے میں امام ابو حنیفہ نے توقف کیا ہے۔ توقف پر مبنی تو جیہ کی بحث مذکورہ صورت میں بیان ہو چکی ہے۔
Chapter of oath in speech. In Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume six: Do not speak ill of time (dahr), because its creator is Allah Almighty. Time itself can do nothing; whatever happens is from Allah. So speaking ill of time is like speaking ill of Allah. Therefore, when a person swears using the word dahr in indefinite form, it is not known what meaning the swearer intended. The meaning of absolute dahr cannot be determined. Regarding duration, there are three levels: short, medium, long (or infinite). In the word dahr, none of these durations can be determined from the general meaning. Hence there is room for doubt. Thus it is known that this is a tawqifi (matter where doubt exists) matter, and analogy is invalid in tawqifi matters. Therefore, it is necessary to pause (tawaqquf) in such matters. It is clear that when the text of Hidayah says 'huwa al-sahih' (it is the correct view), it avoids the narration of Shaykh Abu al-Mu'in from Bishr ibn al-Walid from Imam Abu Yusuf that Imam Abu Hanifa said: there is no difference between using dahr as indefinite or definite. The correct view is that when dahr is definite with the definite article, it means time by consensus, but when indefinite, Imam Abu Hanifa paused. The discussion of the reasoning for pausing has been given.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling on oaths involving the word 'dahr' (time). The author first explains the prohibition of cursing time. Then, when used in an oath, the word 'dahr' in indefinite form is ambiguous, so the Hanafi school requires tawaqquf (suspension) – the oath is not immediately enforceable. The author distinguishes the correct view: when 'dahr' is definite (with alif-lam), it refers to time by consensus; but indefinite, Abu Hanifa paused, contrary to a reported narration from Imam Abu Yusuf that there is no difference. This illustrates the principle of tawaqquf in doubtful matters, where qiyas cannot be applied.

Key Terms
دہر (dahr): Time or age; in this context, used in oaths to refer to an indefinite period.
توقیفی (tawqīfī): A matter where doubt exists and qiyas is invalid; requires reliance on explicit text.
توقف (tawaqquf): Suspension or pausing; the ruling that an oath is not considered broken until the intention is clarified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when a person swears using the word 'dahr' without a definite article, the correct ruling is:
A) The oath is immediately binding.
B) The oath is invalid because time cannot be an object of oath.
C) The oath is suspended until intention is clarified.
D) The oath means one year.

Key Takeaway
The indefinite use of 'dahr' in oaths requires tawaqquf (suspension) because its meaning is ambiguous, reflecting the Hanafi principle of caution in doubtful matters.

Interpreting 'Many Days' in Conditional Manumission
Determines number of days for 'kathīra' in conditional manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi dispute over the interpretation of 'ayyāman kathīratan' in conditional manumission and identify the mufta bihi ruling for Persian/Urdu contexts.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'many days' in conditional manumission: linguistic maximum (10) vs customary repetition (7).

When a master says to his slave, 'If you serve me many days, you are free,' how many days constitute 'many'? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement based on whether one relies on linguistic limits (Abu Hanifa) or customary usage (Sahibayn). This lesson unpacks their arguments and shows how the custom-based view prevails in non-Arabic contexts.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Abu Hanifa holds that 'many days' means ten days, because 'ayyām' (days) in Arabic can only be used up to ten; beyond that, Arabs say 'ʿasharu ayyām'.
This is a linguistic maximum argument.
2
Identify the opposing view
Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that 'many days' means seven days, because customarily people consider a week as 'many', and any excess is repetition (takrār).
This is a customary ('urf) argument.
3
Examine the proofs
Abu Hanifa's proof: the plural 'ayyām' is a 'jam' al-qilla' (plural of few) which extends to ten. Sahibayn's proof: in custom, 'many days' is understood as a week; beyond that is repetition, so the first occurrence of 'many' is seven.
Both positions are based on valid usul methods: language vs custom.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: the slave must serve either 10 days (Abu Hanifa) or 7 days (Sahibayn) to earn freedom.
This affects the timing of the slave's liberation.
5
Apply tarjih
In Persian/Urdu contexts, the custom-based view of 7 days is preferred (mufta bihi) because the language uses a singular word for 'day' (roz) and custom treats a week as 'many'.
This highlights the role of local custom ('urf) in interpretation.

And whoever said to his slave 'In khadamtani ayyāman kathīratan fanta hurrun' (If you serve me many days, you are free), then 'al-ayyām al-kathīra' according to Abu Hanifa is ten days because it is the maximum that the name 'days' encompasses. And they (Sahibayn) said: seven days, because what exceeds it is repetition. And it is said: if the oath was in Persian, it goes to seven days because there they only use the singular word for day (روز) and not the plural. Translation: If a person said to his slave in Arabic, according to Abu Hanifa ten days are intended because the limit of 'days' is ten, and Sahibayn said seven days because excess is repetition. Some mashayikh said if the oath is in Persian, it is for seven days because Persian uses the singular 'roz' only. Explanation: In this case, the meaning of 'many days' according to Imam Abu Hanifa is ten days because that is the limit of the number of days, and according to Sahibayn seven days because according to them the basis is seven, and the rest are repetition; hence seven days are intended.
Source pages p. 104

Commentary
This ruling concerns a conditional manumission: the master says 'If you serve me many days, you are free'. The dispute is about 'many' (kathīra). Abu Hanifa says 10 days because 'ayyām' can only be used up to 10 in Arabic; beyond that, Arabs say 'عشر یوما'. Sahibayn say 7 days because common custom treats 'many days' as a week, and beyond that is repetition. The passage also notes that in Persian/Urdu, where 'day' is singular (روز), the customary week is applied. This shows the role of language and custom in interpreting ambiguous conditions.

Key Terms
أيام كثيرة (ayyām kathīra): Many days; in conditional contracts, interpreted based on linguistic/customary maximum.
تکرار (takrār): Repetition; Sahibayn argue that beyond seven days is repetition, so 'many' is seven.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) A lifetime.

Key Takeaway
The interpretation of ambiguous terms in conditional contracts depends on a combination of linguistic principles and local custom, leading to a legitimate internal Hanafi difference with context-dependent tarjih.

Oath to Free Child: Dead Then Live Birth
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fulfillment of manumission oath by dead then live child

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the fulfillment of a manumission oath when a dead child is born first, and explain the reasoning of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A dead child cannot be freed, so it does not fulfill an oath of manumission — the term 'child' is implicitly restricted to living beings when freedom is intended.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students (the Sahibayn) regarding the fulfillment of an oath to free a child. The key question: does a stillborn child count as a 'child' for the purpose of the oath? Understanding this dispute reveals how the meaning of a word can be restricted by the intended legal consequence, and how the nature of the consequence (freedom) limits the scope of the condition.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what Abu Hanifa holds in the given scenario: a man says to his slave-girl, 'If you give birth to a child, it is free,' and she gives birth first to a dead child, then to a live one. Abu Hanifa rules that only the live child becomes free.
The dead child does not fulfill the condition.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that neither child becomes free. They argue that the condition was fulfilled by the birth of the dead child, so the oath is dissolved without effect because a dead child cannot be freed.
For them, the literal occurrence of birth is enough.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The Sahibayn's dalil: The condition (birth of a child) is literally satisfied by any birth, including stillbirth. The word 'walad' (child) in Arabic includes stillborn children. Therefore, the oath is fulfilled, but since the consequence (freedom) cannot apply to a dead person, the oath ends with no legal effect.
They rely on the literal meaning and the fact that the oath has been spent.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa's response: The absolute name 'walad' is implicitly restricted by the attribute of life because the intended consequence (freedom) is a legal force that only applies to living beings. He analogizes it to explicitly saying 'a living child'. He distinguishes this from divorce or becoming umm walad, where life is not a restriction.
The nature of the consequence conditions the interpretation of the word.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: In the given scenario, if the slave-girl gives birth to a dead child then a live one, Abu Hanifa frees the live child; the Sahibayn free neither. The mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view.
This affects the legal status of the child and the fulfillment of the oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ قَالَ إِذَا وَلَدْتِ وَلَدًا فَهُوَ حُرٌّ فَوَلَدَتْ وَلَدًا مَيِّتًا ثُمَّ آخَرَ حَيًّا عَتَقَ الْحَيُّ وَحْدَهُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَا يَعْتِقُ وَاحِدٌ مِنْهُمَا لِأَنَّ الشَّرْطَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ بِوِلَادَةِ الْمَيِّتِ عَلَى مَا بَيَّنَّا فَيَنْحَلُّ الْيَمِينُ لَا إِلَى جَزَاءٍ لِأَنَّ الْمَيِّتَ لَيْسَ بِمَحَلٍّ لِلْحُرِّيَّةِ وَهِيَ الْجَزَاءُ وَلِأَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَنَّ مُطْلَقَ اسْمِ الْوَلَدِ مُقَيَّدٌ بِوَصْفِ الْحَيَاةِ لِأَنَّهُ قُصِدَ إِثْبَاتُ الْحُرِّيَّةِ جَزَاءً وَهِيَ قُوَّةٌ حِكْمِيَّةٌ تَظْهَرُ فِي دَفْعِ تَسَلُّطِ الْغَيْرِ وَلَا تَثْبُتُ فِي الْمَيِّتِ فَيَتَقَيَّدُ بِوَصْفِ الْحَيَاةِ فَصَارَ كَمَا لَوْ قَالَ إِذَا وَلَدْتِ وَلَدًا حَيًّا بِخِلَافِ جَزَاءِ الطَّلَاقِ وَحُرِّيَّةِ الْأُمِّ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَصْلُحُ مُقَيِّدًا
And if he said, 'If you give birth to a child, it is free,' and she gave birth to a dead child, then another living one, the living one alone becomes free according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: Neither of them becomes free because the condition has been fulfilled by the birth of the dead one, as we have explained, so the oath dissolves without a consequence because the dead one is not a locus for freedom, which is the consequence. And for Abu Hanifa (the argument is) that the absolute name 'child' is restricted by the attribute of life because he intended to establish freedom as a consequence, and it is a legal force that appears in repelling the authority of others, and it is not established in a dead one, so it is restricted by the attribute of life. Thus it is as if he said, 'If you give birth to a living child,' contrary to the consequence of divorce and the freeing of the mother because that does not serve as a restriction.
Source pages p. 105

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling from the chapter on oaths regarding manumission and divorce. It is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani (the Sahibayn). The scenario: a man says to his slave-girl, 'If you give birth to a child, it is free.' She first gives birth to a stillborn child, then later to a live one. The Sahibayn argue that since the condition (the birth of a child) was fulfilled by the first (dead) child, the oath has already been fulfilled without any effective consequence because a dead child cannot be freed. Therefore, neither child is freed. Abu Hanifa argues that the word 'child' (walad) in the context of manumission is implicitly restricted by the condition of life, because freedom is a legal capacity that only applies to a living being. Thus, the dead child does not fulfill the condition, and the oath only applies to the living child. He analogizes it to if the man had explicitly said 'a living child.' He distinguishes this from cases of divorce or becoming umm walad (a slave-girl who becomes free upon her master's death after bearing his child), where the attribute of life is not required. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school is Abu Hanifa's view, as it is the stronger and more precise legal reasoning.

Key Terms
وَلَد (walad): In this context, a child that is alive, because the consequence of freedom requires life.
حُرِّيَّة (hurriyya): Legal freedom, a capacity that allows one to own property and not be owned; it is a legal force (quwwa hukmiyya) that repels the authority of others.
جَزَاء (jaza'): The consequence of an oath, here the manumission of the child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man says to his slave-girl, 'If you give birth to a child, it is free,' and she gives birth first to a dead child and then to a live one, what is the ruling?
A) Only the dead child is free
B) Only the live child is free
C) Both are free
D) Neither is free

Key Takeaway
In manumission oaths, the term 'child' is implicitly restricted to living children because freedom requires life; thus a stillborn does not fulfill the condition.
