Conditional Divorce on Selling for Another: The Role of the Lam
Ruling on oath to sell a cloth for someone else then selling unknowingly due to mixing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two forms of lam in oath conditions and apply the ruling on unknowing sale through mixing.

Core Idea
The preposition 'lam' changes the condition: 'for you' requires action on your command; 'your cloth' requires ownership irrespective of command.

In Hanafi law, the wording of an oath matters down to the preposition. This lesson examines a case where a man swears to sell a cloth 'for you' versus 'your cloth' and then unknowingly sells it due to mixing. The ruling hinges on the function of the Arabic letter lam (ل).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two oath formulations
Recognize the difference between 'If I sell this cloth for you' (with lam attached to the verb) and 'If I sell your cloth' (with lam attached to the object).
The lam is a preposition that can indicate benefit or ownership.
2
Determine the lam's attachment
In the first, lam is attached to the sale (بيع); in the second, it is attached to the cloth (ثوب). This changes the legal requirement.
Examine the Arabic structure: 'bictu laka' vs 'thawban laka'.
3
Apply the rule for each formulation
For 'sale for you': the oath is broken only if the sale is done by the owner's command. For 'your cloth': the oath is broken when any cloth owned by that person is sold, regardless of command or knowledge.
This is the core ruling of the passage.
4
Analyze the mixing scenario
When the cloth is mixed and sold without knowledge, in the first formulation the absence of command means the oath is not broken; in the second, the sale of owned property breaks it.
The unknowing sale does not excuse the second formulation.
5
Generalize to other acts
The same distinction applies to any act that admits agency (niyaba), such as goldsmithing or tailoring, but not to personal acts like eating or drinking.
Acts that cannot be done through an agent do not allow this differentiation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے دوسرے کو کہا اگر یہ کپڑا میں تجھے بیچوں تو میری بیوی پر طلاق واقع ہو محلوف علیہ نے کپڑے کو خلط کر دیا ، پھر حالف نے بیچا اور وہ جانتا نہیں تھا، حانث نہیں ہو گا
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِغَيْرِهِ إِنْ بِعْتُ لَكَ هَذَا التَّوْبَ فَامْرَأَتُهُ طَالِقٌ فَلَبَّسَ الْمَحْلُوفُ عَلَيْهِ ثَوْبَا فِي ثِيَابِ الْحَالِفِ فَبَاعَهُ وَلَمْ يَعْلَمُ لَمْ يَحْدِثُ لِاَنَّ حَرْفَ اللَّامِ دَخَلَ عَلَى الْبَيْعِ فَيَقْتَضِى اِخْتِصَاصَهُ بِهِ وَذَالِكَ بِأَنْ يَفْعَلَهُ بِأَمْرِهِ إِذِ الْبَيْعُ يَجْرِى فِيهِ النِّيَابَةُ وَلَمْ يُوجَدُ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَاقَالَ إِنْ بِعْتُ ثَوْبًا لَكَ حَيْثُ يَحْنِتُ إِذَابَاعَ ثَوْبًا مَمْلُو كَا لَهُ سَوَاءٌ كَانَ بِأَمْرِهِ أَوْ بِغَيْرِ اَمْرِهِ عَلِمَ بِذَالِكَ أَوَلَمْ يَعْلَمْ لِاَنَّ حَرْفَ اللَّامِ دَخَلَ عَلَى الْعَيْنِ لِأَنَّهُ أَقْرَبُ إِلَيْهِ فَيَقْتَضِى اخْتِصَاصَ الْعَيْنَ بِهِ وَذَالِكَ بِأَنْ يَكُونَ مَمْلُوكًا لَهُ وَنَظِيرُهُ الصَّيَاغَةُ وَالْخِيَاطَةُ وَكُلُّ مَا يَجْرِى فِيهِ النِّيَابَةُ بِخِلَافِ الأَكْلِ وَالشَّرْبِ وَصَرْبِ الْغُلَامِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَحْتَمِلُ النِّيَابَةَ فَلَا يَفْتَرِقُ الْحُكْمُ فِيْهِ فِي الْوَجْهَيْنِ
ترجمہ اگر زید نے خالد سے کہا کہ اگر میں یہ کپڑا تمہارے لئے فروخت کروں تو میری بیوی کو طلاق ہے۔ اس کے بعد خالد نے اس کپڑے کو زید کے کپڑوں میں چھپا دیا۔ اور زید نے وہ سب کپڑے بیچ دیئے۔ اس وقت اسے یہ خبر نہیں تھی کہ وہ کپڑا بھی ان کپڑوں میں موجود ہے۔ اس لئے وہ حانث نہیں ہوا کیونکہ اس کا پہلے یہ کہنا کہ میں تمہارے لئے فروخت کروں اس کا تقاضا یہ ہے کہ اس کپڑے کو خاص خالد کے لئے بیچا جائے۔اس کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ خالد کے حکم سے اس کا یہ کپڑا بیچ ڈالے۔ کیونکہ بیچ ایسی چیز ہے کہ اس میں نیابت جاری ہوتی ہے (یعنی ایک آدمی دوسرے آدمی کی طرف سے بیچ سکتا ہے مگر یہ بات نہیں پائی گئی۔ بخلاف اس کے کہ اگر یوں کہا ہو کہ اگر میں نے تمہارا یہ کپڑا بیچا تو ایسی صورت میں حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ اس نے خالد کی ملکیت کا کپڑا بیچ ڈالا ہے اس لئے حانث ہوا خواہ خود اس کے حکم سے ہو یا حکم کے بغیر ہو۔ اور خواہ زید یہ بات جانتا ہو یا نہ جانتا ہو۔ کیونکہ اس نے اپنے پورے جملے میں جو تیرا کپڑا کہا ہے اس سے یہ کپڑا خالد کا ہی ہونا چاہئے۔ اس طرح سے کہ کپڑا اس کا مملوک ہو ۔ اس بیع کی مثال میں یہاں جو کم بیان کیا گیا ہی حکم ہر ایسے فعل میں بھی ہو گا جس میں ایک کے بدلہ دوسرا شخص بھی کام کر سکتا ہو (نائب بن سکتا ہو ) جیسے زرگری (سنار کا کام) اور سلائی کا کام ( اور ہبہ کرنا۔ صدقہ دینا۔ مکاتب بنانا اور غلام کو مارنا۔ ع) برخلاف کھانے، پینے اور اپنے لڑکے کو مارنے کے۔ کیونکہ ان کاموں میں سے کوئی بھی کام ایسا نہیں ہے جو دوسرے سے کرایا جائے ۔ اس لئے ان دونوں صورتوں میں حکم مختلف نہیں ہو گا
Someone said to another: 'If I sell this cloth for you, my wife is divorced.' The person for whom the oath was taken mixed the cloth with the oath-taker's clothes. Then the oath-taker sold it without knowing, and he is not considered to have broken his oath. Because the letter lam entered upon the sale, requiring its specification for that person, which means it must be done by his command, as sale admits agency, and this was not found. Unlike if he said 'If I sell a cloth of yours,' in which case he breaks the oath when he sells a cloth owned by that person, whether by his order or not, whether he knows or not. Because the letter lam entered upon the object (cloth), requiring its specification, meaning the cloth must be his property. The same applies to goldsmithing, tailoring, and everything that admits agency, unlike eating, drinking, and beating a child, because they do not admit agency, so the ruling does not differ between the two forms.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage discusses a conditional oath involving sale. The key is the difference between saying 'I sell for you' (li-ka) versus 'I sell your cloth' (thawban laka). In the first, the sale must be performed on behalf of the other person by his command because the lam indicates benefit to him. If the cloth gets mixed and sold accidentally without his order, the oath is not broken. In the second, the lam attaches to the cloth itself, indicating ownership; selling any cloth owned by that person breaks the oath regardless of prior knowledge. The rule extends to any acts that admit agency, like goldsmithing, sewing, or giving gifts, but not to personal acts like eating or drinking which cannot be done through an agent.

Key Terms
حرف اللام (ḥarf al-lām): The preposition 'li' used to indicate benefit ('for') or ownership ('belonging to').
نیابت (niyābāt): Agency; the ability to have another person perform an act on one's behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person says: 'If I sell for you this cloth, my wife is divorced.' The owner mixes it among his clothes, and he sells it unknowingly. According to Hanafi fiqh, is he considered to have broken his oath?
A) Yes, because he sold the cloth.
B) No, because he did not sell it by the owner's command.
C) Yes, because he owned the cloth already.
D) No, because divorce oaths are always invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Arabic preposition lam attached to the verb indicates benefit and requires the owner's command to fulfill an oath; attached to the object indicates ownership and triggers the oath upon sale of any owned item.

Conditional Manumission and Khiyar al-Shart
Ruling on conditional manumission when selling with khiyar al-shart

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that conditional manumission (ta'liq al-'itq) takes effect immediately upon the occurrence of its condition, even when ownership is revocable due to khiyar al-shart.

Core Idea
Conditional freedom triggers at contract formation because ownership is deemed present despite the option.

This lesson examines a specific scenario where a seller conditionally manumits a slave upon sale, and the sale occurs with a stipulation (khiyar al-shart). The Hanafi school rules that the slave becomes free immediately, even though the option allows cancellation. The same applies when the buyer conditionally manumits upon purchase. The reasoning hinges on treating conditional freedom like unconditional freedom regarding ownership. By the end, you will understand how this principle works and be able to apply it to similar cases.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The passage presents two cases: (1) seller says 'this slave is free if I sell him' and sells with khiyar al-shart; (2) buyer says 'if I buy him, he is free' and buys with khiyar al-shart. Recognize the parties and the condition.
2
Recognize the fulfillment of the condition
The condition (sale or purchase) occurs at the moment the contract is concluded. According to Hanafi law, the option does not negate the existence of the sale; it only gives a right to rescind.
3
Understand ownership during the option period
During khiyar al-shart, ownership is considered to remain with the seller (for the seller's option) or with the buyer (for the buyer's option) for purposes of manumission. This deemed ownership suffices to fulfill the condition.
4
Link to the principle: conditional like unconditional
The Hanafi principle 'al-mu'allaq ka al-munajjaz' (conditional is like unconditional) applies. In unconditional manumission, ownership is established before freedom; here, ownership is deemed established despite the option.
5
Apply the ruling to both parties
Whether the manumission is conditioned on selling (by the owner) or buying (by the buyer), the slave becomes free immediately upon the contract. The text confirms this is the view of all three major Hanafi scholars (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ایک شخص نے کہا یہ غلام آزاد ہے اگر میں اسے بیچوں، پھر خیار شرط کیساتھ بیچا تو غلام آزاد ہو جائیگا
وَمَنْ قَالَ هَذَا الْعَبْدُ حُرِّانُ بِعْتُهُ فَبَاعَهُ عَلَى أَنَّهُ بِالْخِيَارِ عَتَقَ لِوُجُودِ الشَّرْطِ وَهُوَ الْبَيْعُ وَالْمِلْكُ فِيهِ قَائِمٌ فَيُنَزَّلُ الْجَزَاءُ وَكَذَالِكَ لَوْقَالَ الْمُشْتَرِى إِنِ اشْتَرَيْتُهُ فَهُوَ حُرِّفَا شُتَرَاهُ عَلَى انَّهُ بِالْخِيَارِ يَعْتِقُ أَيْضًالَاتَ الشَّيْطَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ وَهُوَ الشَّرَاءُ وَالْمِلْكُ قَائِمٌ فِيهِ وَهَذَا عَلَى اَصْلِهِمَا ظَاهِرٌ وَكَذَا عَلَى أَصْلِهِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا الْعِبْقَ بِتَعْلِيقِهِ وَالْمُعَلَّقَ كَالْمُنَجَّزِ وَلَوْنَجْزَ الْعِلْقَ يَثْبُتُ الْمِلْكُ سَابِقَاعَلَيْهِ فَكَذَاهَذَا
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے یہ کہا کہ اگر میں اس غلام کو فروخت کروں تو یہ آزاد ہے۔ پھر اس غلام کو اس شرط پر فروخت کیا کہ مجھے اختیار حاصل ہے تو غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ شرط یعنی اسے بیچنا پایا گیا۔ اور غلام میں ابھی ملکیت قائم ہے۔ اس لئے جزاء ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ فائدہ .... اور اگر اس نے بلاشر و مکمل طور پر بیچ دیا تو غلام آزاد ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ فروخت ہوتے ہی آزاد ہو گیا ہے۔ اس لئے کہ غلام اب مالک کی ملکیت میں باقی نہ رہا۔ اور اگر کسی نے یہ کہا کہ اگر میں اسے خریدوں تو یہ آزاد ہے۔ اس کے بعد شرط خیار کے ساتھ اسے خرید لیا۔ یعنی اس شرط پر کہ اگر مجھے یہ پسند نہیں آیا تو تین دنوں میں اسے واپس کردوں گا۔ تو بھی یہ غلام آزاد ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ شرط یعنی خریداری پائی گی۔ اور اس پر ملکیت بھی باقی ہے۔ اور اس ملکیت کا موجودہ صورت میں باقی رہنا صاحبین کے مطابق تو ظاہر ہے۔ اسی طرح امام اعظم کے مسلک کے مطابق بھی ظاہر ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ آزادی شرطیہ ہے اور شرطیہ آزادی فی الحال بغیر شرط کے مانند ہوتی ہے۔ اور اگر خریدار جاکر (پسند نا پسند کی شرط پر ) خرید کر اسے منظور کرتے ہوئے اپنا اختیار ختم کر دیتا تو کہا جاتا کہ آزادی سے پہلے ملکیت ثابت ہوگئی ۔ یعنی اس نے اپنی جا کر یعنی پسند و نا پسند کا اختیار ختم کر کے خریداری مکمل اور پختہ کر لی پھر آزاد کر دیا۔ تو اسی طرح اس مسئلہ میں بھی ہوگا۔ یعنی وہ غلام خریدار کی ملکیت میں آکر آزاد ہو گیا۔ اور خیار شرط ختم ہو گیا۔
And whoever said: 'This slave is free if I sell him', and then he sold him with an option (khiyar al-shart), the slave becomes free because the condition (sale) is found and ownership remains in him, so the consequence applies. Similarly, if the buyer said: 'If I buy him, he is free', and then he bought him with an option, he also becomes free because the condition (purchase) is realized and ownership remains in him. This is apparent according to the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and also according to Imam Abu Hanifa, because this manumission is conditional and conditional is like unconditional; if unconditional, ownership is established beforehand, so here too.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage addresses the effect of selling a slave with an option (khiyar al-shart) when the owner has conditionally manumitted him upon sale. The ruling is that the slave becomes free immediately upon the contract, even though the option remains. The reason is that the condition of sale has been met, and during the option period ownership is still considered with the seller (or buyer) for the purpose of manumission, so the conditional freedom takes effect. The text analogizes to unconditional manumission where ownership is established before freedom. This applies whether the owner sells with an option or the buyer purchases with an option, according to the consensus of Abu Hanifa and the two companions.

Key Terms
خیار شرط (khiyār al-sharṭ): An option stipulated in a contract allowing either party to cancel within a specified period, typically three days.
تعلیق (ta‘līq): Conditional suspension of a legal effect upon a future event.
عتق (‘itq): Manumission; the act of freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A seller says: 'This slave is free if I sell him.' He sells the slave with a three-day option. What happens?
A) The slave is not free until the option period ends and the sale is confirmed.
B) The slave becomes free immediately upon sale.
C) The slave becomes free only if the buyer agrees.
D) The slave remains a slave because the option invalidates the sale.

Key Takeaway
Conditional manumission upon a sale or purchase takes effect immediately upon contract formation, even when an option (khiyar al-shart) allows the contract to be rescinded.

Oath Not to Sell Slave: Freeing or Mudabbar with Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on divorce oath if not selling slave then freeing or making mudabbar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the ruling of zahir al-riwayah and Imam Abu Yusuf regarding the scope of a husband's divorce statement made in response to one wife's accusation, and apply the principle of generality of speech.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'Every woman I have is divorced,' the general wording divorces all wives – intent does not restrict the literal meaning.

This passage presents two rulings: first, a conditional divorce triggered by not selling a slave is fulfilled if the slave is freed or made mudabbar. Second, a more subtle dispute arises when a husband responds to one wife's accusation of remarriage with a general divorce statement. The debate within the Hanafi school centers on whether the context restricts the generality of his words. The apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) holds that all wives are divorced, while Imam Abu Yusuf limits it to the questioning wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal question
In the second scenario, what is the husband's statement and what is the dispute about? The husband says 'Every woman I have is divorced thrice' in response to his wife's accusation. The dispute is whether this divorces all his wives or only the one who spoke.
2
State the position of zahir al-riwayah
According to the apparent transmission, all wives are divorced because the wording is general (عموم الكلام) and the husband added beyond the mere particle of response.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
State Imam Abu Yusuf's position
Imam Abu Yusuf holds that only the questioning wife is divorced because the statement was a direct response to her, and the husband's intent was to please her, which is not achieved by divorcing others.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
4
Compare the proofs
Evaluate the evidence: generality of words vs. contextual restriction. The apparent ruling relies on the literal meaning, while Abu Yusuf considers the context and purpose of the speech.
Hanafi usul: general terms are applied to all individuals unless there is a specific exception.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Under the apparent ruling, all wives are divorced and must observe iddah; under Abu Yusuf's view, only the questioning wife is divorced.
This affects maintenance, remarriage, and inheritance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کسی نے کہا اگر میں اپنا غلام یا باندی نہ بیچوں تو میری بیوی پر طلاق ، غلام آزاد کر دیا یا مکاتب بنادیا تو اس کی بیوی مطلقہ ہو جائے گی۔
وَمَنْ قَالَ إِنْ لَمْ اَبِعْ هَذَا الْعَبْدَ أَوْ هَذِهِ الْآمَةَ فَامْرَأَتُهُ طَالِقٌ فَاعْتَقَ اَوْ دَبَّرَ طُلِقَتِ امْرَأَتُهُ لِأَنَّ الشَّيْطَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ وَهُوَ عَدَمُ الْبَيْعِ لِفَوَاتِ مَحَلَيَةِ الْبَيْعِ وَإِذَا قَالَتِ الْمَرْأَةُ لِزَوْجِهَا تَزَوَّجْتَ عَلَيَّ فَقَالَ كُلُّ امْرَأَةٍ لِي طَالِقٌ ثَلَثًا طُلِقَتْ هَذِهِ الَّتِي حَلَفَتْهُ فِي الْقَضَاءِ وَعَنْ أَبِى يُوسُفَ أَنَّهَا لَا تُطَلَّقُ لِأَنَّهُ أَخْرَجَهُ جَوَابًا فَيَنْطَبِقُ عَلَيْهِ وَلَانَّ غَرْضَهُ إِرْضَ وَهَا وَهُوَ بِطَلَاقِ غَيْرِهَا فَيَتَقَيَّدُ بِهِ وَ وَجْهُ الظَّاهِرِ عُمُومُ الْكَلَامَ وَقَدْ زَادَ عَلَى حَرْفِ الْجَوَابِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے یہ کہا کہ اگر میں اپنا غلام یا باندی نہ بیچوں تو میری بیوی پر طلاق غلام آزاد کر دیا یا مکاتب بنادیا تو اس کی بیوی مطلقہ ہو جائے گی۔ اور جب عورت اپنے شوہر سے کہے کہ تم نے مجھ پر نکاح کیا تو شوہر نے کہا کہ میری ہر بیوی تین طلاقوں سے طلاق ہے تو وہ عورت جس نے اسے قسم دی تھی قضاء میں طلاق ہو جائے گی۔ اور ابویوسف سے روایت ہے کہ وہ طلاق نہیں ہوگی کیونکہ اس نے اسے جواباً نکالا ہے چنانچہ وہ اس پر منطبق ہوگا اور اس کا مقصد اسے راضی کرنا ہے اور وہ غیر کی طلاق سے راضی نہیں ہوتی اس لئے وہ اس کے ساتھ مقید ہوگا اور ظاہر روایت کا وجه عموم کلام ہے اور اس نے جواب کے حرف پر زیادہ کیا ہے
And whoever said: 'If I do not sell this slave or this slave-girl, my wife is divorced', and then he frees him or makes him mudabbar, his wife is divorced because the condition (non-sale) is realized due to the loss of the subject matter of sale. And when a woman says to her husband: 'You have married over me', and he says: 'Every woman I have is divorced thrice', then the woman who made him swear will be divorced according to the judicial ruling. And from Abu Yusuf: she is not divorced, because he issued it as a response, so it applies to her, and his purpose was to please her, and she is not pleased by the divorce of others, so it is restricted to her. The apparent position is based on the generality of the speech, and he added beyond the particle of response.
Source pages p. 115

Commentary
This passage covers two rulings. First: if a person conditionally divorces his wife upon not selling a slave, then frees the slave or makes him mudabbar (a slave whose freedom is deferred after death), the divorce takes effect because the condition (non-sale) is met since the slave is no longer a salable commodity. Second: a woman accuses her husband of having married another woman, and he responds 'All my wives are divorced thrice.' According to the absolute ruling (zahir al-riwayah), all his wives are divorced, including the one who spoke. But Imam Abu Yusuf holds that only that woman is divorced, because the husband's statement was a direct response to her and his intent was to soothe her, not to divorce others. The text sides with the general wording (عموم الكلام).

Key Terms
مدبر (mudabbar): A slave who is declared free upon the master's death; the declaration is a form of manumission that takes effect after death.
ظاہر روایت (zāhir al-riwāyah): The well-known and authoritative transmission within the Hanafi school, primarily from the six books of Imam Muhammad.
عموم الکلام (‘umūm al-kalām): The generality of the spoken words, interpreted according to their literal and inclusive meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A wife says to her husband: 'You have married another woman!' He responds: 'Every woman I have is divorced thrice.' According to the zahir al-riwayah, which wives are divorced?
A) Only the wife who spoke.
B) All his wives.
C) Only the new wife, if any.
D) None, because the statement was not an oath.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi jurisprudence, when a husband uses general wording like 'every woman I have is divorced,' it divorces all wives, regardless of the context of the conversation, unless there is a specific textual exception.

Oath on Wearing Wife's Spun Clothing: The Dispute and Its Proofs
Dispute between Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn on obligation of hady based on custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the obligation of hady when a wife spins cotton purchased after the oath, and explain the evidence for each position.

Core Idea
Abu Hanifa relies on custom; Sahibayn rely on strict ownership — the dispute is about the cause of ownership.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding an oath that makes the wearing of clothing from the wife’s spinning conditional upon giving hady. The central question: does the wife’s spinning create a cause of ownership for the husband, or must the cotton be owned at the time of the oath? We will explore the arguments of each side and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the condition
The husband says: 'If I wear (something made) from your spinning, it is hady.' He buys cotton after the oath, his wife spins it, weaves it, and he wears it. The dispute is about whether he must give that garment as hady.
Hady here means giving the garment in charity in Mecca.
2
State Abu Hanifa’s ruling
Abu Hanifa holds that the hady is obligatory because custom (urf) dictates that the wife’s spinning is from the husband’s property, so the condition is fulfilled.
He considers custom as a cause of ownership.
3
State the Sahibayn’s ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that the hady is not obligatory unless the cotton was owned by the husband at the time of the oath, because a vow is only valid on owned property or on a direct cause of ownership.
They require explicit ownership at the time of the oath.
4
Analyze the proofs
Abu Hanifa argues that custom makes the spinning a cause of ownership. The Sahibayn argue that spinning is not a direct cause of ownership, so the oats does not include cotton bought later.
Both sides use the same source but different interpretations of 'cause of ownership'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب اليمين فى لبس الثياب والحلى وغير ذالك
وَمَنْ قَالَ لِاِمْرَأَتِهِ إِنْ لَبِسْتُ مِنْ غَزْلِكَ فَهُوَهَدَى فَاشْتَرى قُطْنًا فَغَزَلَتْهُ فَنَسَجَتْهُ فَلَبِسَهُ فَهُوَهَدَى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَهْدِى حَتَّى تَغْزِلَ مِنْ قُطْنِ مَلَكَهُ يَوْمَ حَلْفٍ وَمَعْنَى الْهَدْيِ التَّصَدُّقُ بِهِ بِمَكَّةَ لِأَنَّهُ اِسْمٌ لِمَايُهُدَى إِلَيْهَا لَهُمَا أَنَّ النَّذْرَ إِنَّمَا يَصِحُ فِي الْمِلْكِ أَوْ مُضَافًا إِلَى سَبَبِ الْمِلْكِ وَلَمْ يُوجَدْلَانَّ اللُّبْسَ وَغَزَلَ الْمَرْأَةِ لَيْسَا مِن أَسْبَابِ مِلْكِهِ وَلَهُ اَنَّ غَزَلَ الْمَرْأَةِ يَكُونُ مِنْ قُطْنِ الزَّوْجِ وَالْمُعْتَادُ هُوَ الْمُرَادُ وَذَالِكَ سَبَبَبٌ لِمِلْكِهِ وَلِهَذَا يَحْنِتُ إِذَا غَزَلَتْ مِنْ قُطْنِ مَمْلُوكِ لَهُ وَقْتَ النَّذْرِ انَّ الْقُطْنَ لَمْ يَصِرْ مَذْكُورًا ترجمہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ اگر میں نے تمہارے کاتے ہوئے سوت کا کپڑا پہنا تو وہ ہدی ہے۔ اس کے بعد اس نے روئی خریدی اور اس عورت نے اسے کات کر اس کے دھاگہ سے کپڑا بن دیا جسے سلوا کر اس کے شوہر نے پہن لیا۔ تو وہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہدی ہے ( اور اگر چاہے تو اس کپڑے کی قیمت مکہ کے فقراء کو صدقہ کے طور پر دیدے) اور صاحبین نے کہا ہے کہ شوہر پر ہدی کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ البتہ عورت اس روئی کا سوت کاتے جس کا مالک قسم کے دن وہی شوہر ہوتو واجب ہو گئی (بعد کی خریدی ہوئی روٹی کے کپڑے کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا) یہاں ہدی کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کپڑے کو مکہ میں صدقہ کر دے۔ کیونکہ ہدی اس چیز کو کہتے ہیںجو مکہ کو ہدیتا بھیجی جائے اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نذراسی چیز میں صحیح ہوتی ہے جو بالفعل اپنی مملوکہ ہو یا سبب ملک کی طرف اس کی اضافت ہو ( مثلاً اگر میں اس غلام کو خریدوں تو یہ آزاد ہے ) اور ان دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی بھی یہاں نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ مرد کا پہنا اور عورت کا سوت کا تنا کچھ مرد کے ملک ہو جانے کے اسباب میں سے نہیں ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عادت اس طرح جاری ہے کہ عورت اپنے شوہر کی روئی سے سوت کاتی ہے۔ اور قسم کھانے میں اس کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے۔ جس کی عادت یا رواج ہو۔ اور یہ شوہر کے مالک ہو جانے کا سبب ہے۔ اسی لئے نذر کے وقت شوہر کی اپنی مملوکہ روئی سے جب بیوی کاتے تو شو ہر حانث ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہاں لفظوں میں روئی کا کوئی ذکر نہیں ہے (ف۔ رومی ملکوں میں عورت اپنے شو ہر کی مملو کہ روئی سے کا تا کرتی ہے۔ لہذا ان علاقوں میں امام اعظم کے قول پر فتویٰ ہوتا ہے اور مصر کے باشندوں میں عورت اپنی روئی کا نتی ہے اس لئے وہاں صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دیا جائے۔ (انبر)
تشریح ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Chapter: Oath concerning wearing clothes and jewelry and other things. And whoever said to his wife: 'If I wear (something made) from your spinning, it is a hady (sacrificial offering to Mecca),' then he bought cotton and she spun it, wove it, and he wore it – then it is a hady according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not obligatory for him to give hady unless she spun from cotton owned by him on the day of the oath. The meaning of hady is to give it in charity in Mecca, because it is a term for what is sent as a gift to it. Their (Sahibayn's) argument is that a vow is only valid regarding owned property or what is connected to a cause of ownership, and neither is present here, because wearing and the wife's spinning are not among the causes of his ownership. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that the wife's spinning is from the husband's cotton, and what is customary is intended, and that is a cause of his ownership. Therefore he becomes a sinner (hanth) if she spins from cotton owned by him at the time of the vow, because the cotton is not explicitly mentioned. [Urdu translation: If someone said to his wife... The meaning of hady is to give it in charity in Mecca... In Rumi countries, women spin from their husband's cotton, so fatwa is given according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, and in Egypt, women spin from their own cotton, so there fatwa is given according to Sahibayn's opinion. (from Anbar) Explanation: The translation is clear.]
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when an oath to give hady becomes binding. The scenario: a man tells his wife: 'If I wear clothing made from your spun thread, it is hady' (meaning he will give it as charity in Mecca). He later buys cotton, the wife spins it, weaves cloth, and he wears it. Abu Hanifa rules that the hady becomes obligatory because custom dictates that a wife spins from her husband's cotton, and this custom is the basis of the oath. Therefore, even though the cotton was bought after the oath, the spun thread is effectively considered from the husband's property. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the hady is not obligatory unless the cotton was owned by the husband at the time of the oath, because a vow is only valid on owned property or on property that will be acquired through a direct cause of ownership. Spinning by the wife is not a cause of ownership. The text concludes with a practical note: in regions like Rumi (Turkish) lands, women customarily spin from their husband's cotton, so Abu Hanifa's view is applied; in Egypt, women spin from their own cotton, so the Sahibayn's view is applied. This shows the role of custom (urf) in determining legal rulings.

Key Terms
هَدي (hady): A sacrificial animal or gift sent to Mecca; here, the clothing itself is to be given in charity in Mecca.
غزل (ghazl): Spinning (of thread); the act of making thread from cotton or wool.
نذر (nadhr): Vow; a promise to perform a good deed for Allah, often conditional.
عادة (adah): Custom; prevalent practice that influences legal interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition for hady obligation according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?
A) The wife must spin the thread herself.
B) The cotton must be owned by the husband at the time of the oath.
C) The husband must wear the garment for at least one day.
D) The garment must be given in charity locally.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of hady in this oath depends on whether custom or strict ownership is used to interpret the condition; the dispute is resolved by local custom.

Custom (Urf) as the Decisive Factor in the Hady Oath
Resolution of dispute based on local custom

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that custom (urf) determines the operative ruling in the hady oath case, and identify which view is followed based on regional practices.

Core Idea
Fatwa follows the dominant custom: where wives spin from husband’s cotton, follow Abu Hanifa; where they spin from their own, follow the Sahibayn.

The earlier lesson established the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Now we see how later Hanafi jurists resolved the difference: not by choosing one over the other absolutely, but by deferring to the local custom. This lesson explores the role of urf in legal application and how a mufti should determine the correct ruling in practice.

Guided Path
1
Recall the two views and their reliance on custom
Abu Hanifa uses custom as a cause of ownership; Sahibayn require explicit ownership at oath time. The passage then notes regional differences.
Custom is not a source of law in the same way as Quran, but it can determine the intended meaning of words.
2
Identify the regional application
In Turkish lands (Rumi), women customarily spin from their husband's cotton, so Abu Hanifa's view is followed. In Egypt, women spin from their own cotton, so the Sahibayn's view is followed.
The authority (Anbar) explicitly states this.
3
Formulate the principle
The operative ruling is based on the dominant custom (ghalib al-urf) of the locality. The mufta bihi is not fixed but varies.
This reflects the Hanafi maxim 'al-urf muhakkamun' (custom is authoritative).
4
Apply to a mixed scenario
If custom is mixed or unclear, the mufti should investigate the prevailing practice. If still unclear, some jurists advise caution, e.g., giving hady to be safe.
This is a practical fatwa methodology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وَمَنْ قَالَ لِاِمْرَأَتِهِ إِنْ لَبِسْتُ مِنْ غَزْلِكَ فَهُوَهَدَى فَاشْتَرى قُطْنًا فَغَزَلَتْهُ فَنَسَجَتْهُ فَلَبِسَهُ فَهُوَهَدَى عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ وَقَالَا لَيْسَ عَلَيْهِ أَنْ يَهْدِى حَتَّى تَغْزِلَ مِنْ قُطْنِ مَلَكَهُ يَوْمَ حَلْفٍ وَمَعْنَى الْهَدْيِ التَّصَدُّقُ بِهِ بِمَكَّةَ لِأَنَّهُ اِسْمٌ لِمَايُهُدَى إِلَيْهَا لَهُمَا أَنَّ النَّذْرَ إِنَّمَا يَصِحُ فِي الْمِلْكِ أَوْ مُضَافًا إِلَى سَبَبِ الْمِلْكِ وَلَمْ يُوجَدْلَانَّ اللُّبْسَ وَغَزَلَ الْمَرْأَةِ لَيْسَا مِن أَسْبَابِ مِلْكِهِ وَلَهُ اَنَّ غَزَلَ الْمَرْأَةِ يَكُونُ مِنْ قُطْنِ الزَّوْجِ وَالْمُعْتَادُ هُوَ الْمُرَادُ وَذَالِكَ سَبَبَبٌ لِمِلْكِهِ وَلِهَذَا يَحْنِتُ إِذَا غَزَلَتْ مِنْ قُطْنِ مَمْلُوكِ لَهُ وَقْتَ النَّذْرِ انَّ الْقُطْنَ لَمْ يَصِرْ مَذْكُورًا ترجمہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا کہ اگر میں نے تمہارے کاتے ہوئے سوت کا کپڑا پہنا تو وہ ہدی ہے۔ اس کے بعد اس نے روئی خریدی اور اس عورت نے اسے کات کر اس کے دھاگہ سے کپڑا بن دیا جسے سلوا کر اس کے شوہر نے پہن لیا۔ تو وہ امام ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہدی ہے ( اور اگر چاہے تو اس کپڑے کی قیمت مکہ کے فقراء کو صدقہ کے طور پر دیدے) اور صاحبین نے کہا ہے کہ شوہر پر ہدی کرنا واجب نہیں ہے۔ البتہ عورت اس روئی کا سوت کاتے جس کا مالک قسم کے دن وہی شوہر ہوتو واجب ہو گئی (بعد کی خریدی ہوئی روٹی کے کپڑے کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا) یہاں ہدی کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ اس کپڑے کو مکہ میں صدقہ کر دے۔ کیونکہ ہدی اس چیز کو کہتے ہیںجو مکہ کو ہدیتا بھیجی جائے اور صاحبین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ نذراسی چیز میں صحیح ہوتی ہے جو بالفعل اپنی مملوکہ ہو یا سبب ملک کی طرف اس کی اضافت ہو ( مثلاً اگر میں اس غلام کو خریدوں تو یہ آزاد ہے ) اور ان دونوں باتوں میں سے کوئی بھی یہاں نہیں پائی گئی ہے۔ کیونکہ مرد کا پہنا اور عورت کا سوت کا تنا کچھ مرد کے ملک ہو جانے کے اسباب میں سے نہیں ہے۔ اور امام ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ عادت اس طرح جاری ہے کہ عورت اپنے شوہر کی روئی سے سوت کاتی ہے۔ اور قسم کھانے میں اس کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے۔ جس کی عادت یا رواج ہو۔ اور یہ شوہر کے مالک ہو جانے کا سبب ہے۔ اسی لئے نذر کے وقت شوہر کی اپنی مملوکہ روئی سے جب بیوی کاتے تو شو ہر حانث ہو جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہاں لفظوں میں روئی کا کوئی ذکر نہیں ہے (ف۔ رومی ملکوں میں عورت اپنے شو ہر کی مملو کہ روئی سے کا تا کرتی ہے۔ لہذا ان علاقوں میں امام اعظم کے قول پر فتویٰ ہوتا ہے اور مصر کے باشندوں میں عورت اپنی روئی کا نتی ہے اس لئے وہاں صاحبین کے قول پر فتوی دیا جائے۔ (انبر)
تشریح ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
Chapter: Oath concerning wearing clothes and jewelry and other things. And whoever said to his wife: 'If I wear (something made) from your spinning, it is a hady (sacrificial offering to Mecca),' then he bought cotton and she spun it, wove it, and he wore it – then it is a hady according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: It is not obligatory for him to give hady unless she spun from cotton owned by him on the day of the oath. The meaning of hady is to give it in charity in Mecca, because it is a term for what is sent as a gift to it. Their (Sahibayn's) argument is that a vow is only valid regarding owned property or what is connected to a cause of ownership, and neither is present here, because wearing and the wife's spinning are not among the causes of his ownership. His (Abu Hanifa's) argument is that the wife's spinning is from the husband's cotton, and what is customary is intended, and that is a cause of his ownership. Therefore he becomes a sinner (hanth) if she spins from cotton owned by him at the time of the vow, because the cotton is not explicitly mentioned. [Urdu translation: If someone said to his wife... The meaning of hady is to give it in charity in Mecca... In Rumi countries, women spin from their husband's cotton, so fatwa is given according to Imam Abu Hanifa's opinion, and in Egypt, women spin from their own cotton, so there fatwa is given according to Sahibayn's opinion. (from Anbar) Explanation: The translation is clear.]
Source pages p. 120

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when an oath to give hady becomes binding. The scenario: a man tells his wife: 'If I wear clothing made from your spun thread, it is hady' (meaning he will give it as charity in Mecca). He later buys cotton, the wife spins it, weaves cloth, and he wears it. Abu Hanifa rules that the hady becomes obligatory because custom dictates that a wife spins from her husband's cotton, and this custom is the basis of the oath. Therefore, even though the cotton was bought after the oath, the spun thread is effectively considered from the husband's property. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the hady is not obligatory unless the cotton was owned by the husband at the time of the oath, because a vow is only valid on owned property or on property that will be acquired through a direct cause of ownership. Spinning by the wife is not a cause of ownership. The text concludes with a practical note: in regions like Rumi (Turkish) lands, women customarily spin from their husband's cotton, so Abu Hanifa's view is applied; in Egypt, women spin from their own cotton, so the Sahibayn's view is applied. This shows the role of custom (urf) in determining legal rulings.

Key Terms
هَدي (hady): A sacrificial animal or gift sent to Mecca; here, the clothing itself is to be given in charity in Mecca.
غزل (ghazl): Spinning (of thread); the act of making thread from cotton or wool.
نذر (nadhr): Vow; a promise to perform a good deed for Allah, often conditional.
عادة (adah): Custom; prevalent practice that influences legal interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in which region is the fatwa given on the Sahibayn's view?
A) Turkey
B) Egypt
C) Both regions
D) Neither region

Key Takeaway
Custom (urf) is the decisive factor: the operative ruling in the hady oath case follows the dominant practice of the locality.

Oath on Sleeping on a Bed: The Ruling on Accessories (Tab')
Ruling on whether a sheet or another mattress affects an oath on a bed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of tab' (accessory) to determine whether an oath on a bed is broken when additional bedding is present.

Core Idea
A sheet is an accessory (tab') to a bed, but a second mattress is a similar item that severs the connection.

This lesson examines a precise ruling in Hanafi fiqh concerning oaths. When a person swears not to sleep on a particular bed, sleeping on it with a sheet still breaks the oath. However, placing a second mattress on the bed changes the outcome. Why? The answer lies in the legal concept of tab' (accessory) versus mithl (similar item). Understanding this distinction is key to applying Hanafi rulings on oaths correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the oath
The person swore not to sleep on a specific bed (firash). Then he slept on it with a sheet over it.
The oath is considered broken if the act is deemed sleeping on the bed itself.
2
Classify the added item
The sheet (qaram) is considered a tab' (accessory) of the bed. A sheet is subordinate and typically used to cover the bed.
Tab' items are legally considered part of the main object.
3
Apply the tab' principle
Because the sheet is subordinate, sleeping on it is still considered sleeping on the bed. Therefore, the oath is broken (hanith).
The text says 'yu'addu nā'iman 'alayhi' — he is counted as sleeping on it.
4
Distinguish a similar item
If another mattress (firash akhar) is placed, it is mithl al-shay' (similar item), not subordinate. It severs the nisba (attribution) to the original bed.
A similar item is not tab' because it is like the first in function and nature.
5
Derive the general rule
Accessories (tab') do not change the subject of an oath; similar items (mithl) do. This rule applies to other oaths involving objects with potential accessories.
The underlying illa is the concept of 'tab'iyyah' (subordination).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ مَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَنَامُ عَلَى فِرَاشِ فَنَامَ عَلَيْهِ وَفَوْقَهُ قَرَامٌ حَنَتْ لِأَنَّهُ تَبْعٌ لِلْفِرَاشِ فَيُعَدُّ نَائِمًا عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ جُعِلَ فَوْقَهُ فِرَاشًا أَخَرَ فَنَامَ عَلَيْهِ لَا يَحْنِتُ لِاَنَّ مِثْلَ الشَّيْءِ لَا يَكُونُ تَبْعَالَهُ فَيَنْقَطِعُ النّبْسَةُ عَنِ الْأَوَّلِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی شخص نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ اس فرش پر نہیں سوؤں گا۔ پھر ایسے فرش پر سویا جس پر بار یک چادر تھی تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ چادر اس فرش کے تابع ہے۔ اس لئے وہ اس فرش پر سونے والا ہی سمجھا جائے گا۔ اور اگر فرش یعنی پچھونے کے اوپر دوسرا بچھونا بچھا کر اس پر سویا تو
And whoever swore, 'I will not sleep on a bed,' then slept on it while above it was a sheet, he breaks his oath because it is an accessory to the bed, so he is considered sleeping on it. And if another mattress was placed above it and he slept on it, he does not break his oath because a similar item is not an accessory to it, so the connection to the first is severed. (Then Urdu translation up to 'تو' incomplete.)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage concerns an oath not to sleep on a specific bed (farash). The ruling: if someone sleeps on the bed with a sheet covering it, he breaks his oath because the sheet is considered an accessory (tab’) of the bed. However, if he places another mattress on top and sleeps on that, he does not break the oath because the second mattress is a similar item (mithl al-shay’) that severs the direct connection to the original bed. The Urdu commentary explains that a sheet (chadar) is subordinate, but another mattress (dusra bichhona) is a separate object that breaks the attribution.

Key Terms
فِرَاش (firāsh): A bed or mattress; the object upon which one sleeps.
قَرَام (qarām): A sheet or cover that is placed on the bed; considered an accessory (tab') to the bed.
تَبْع (tabʿ): An accessory or subordinate item that is considered part of the main object in legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the ruling, why does placing a second mattress on the bed prevent the breaking of the oath?
A) Because the second mattress is larger than the first.
B) Because it is a similar item (mithl al-shay’) that severs the connection to the original bed.
C) Because the second mattress is considered a different type of bedding.
D) Because the oath only applies to the specific bed without any cover.

Key Takeaway
The distinction between an accessory (tab') and a similar item (mithl) determines whether an oath on a bed is broken when additional bedding is present.

Oaths on Sitting on the Ground: Carpet vs. Clothing
Ruling that sitting on a mat or carpet does not violate an oath to not sit on the ground

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between independent barriers (carpet/mat) and accessories (clothing) when applying an oath not to sit on the ground.

Core Idea
A carpet is not the ground; clothing is an accessory and does not prevent the oath.

An oath not to sit on the ground seems simple, but the Hanafi jurists have refined its application. This passage clarifies that only the natural earth surface counts as 'ground'. Sitting on an independent covering like a carpet does not break the oath, while mere clothing between you and the earth does, because clothing is considered an extension of the person.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath's object
The person swore not to sit on 'al-ard' (the ground). Determine what this term covers in common usage - the natural surface of the earth.
Consider the ordinary meaning, not technical definitions.
2
Examine the actual situation
He sat on a carpet (bisāṭ) or mat (haṣīr). Is anything between him and the ground? Yes, an independent object.
The carpet is a separate entity from his body and the earth.
3
Apply the linguistic criterion
In everyday language, one who sits on a carpet is not described as 'sitting on the ground'. The phrase denotes direct contact with the earth.
Urf (custom) determines common usage.
4
Distinguish accessories
Clothing is an accessory (tabi') to the person. It does not create a true barrier; legally, it is as if the person is directly on the ground.
Accessories are not independent obstacles.
5
Derive the ruling
If an independent covering (carpet, mat) is present, the oath is not broken. If only clothing intervenes, the oath is broken.
The key is whether the intervening object is independent or an accessory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَلَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يَجْلِسُ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ فَجَلَسَ عَلَى بِسَاطٍ أَوْ حَصِيرِ لَمْ يَحْنِثُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُسَمَّى جَالِسًا عَلَى الْأَرْضِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا حَالَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْأَرْضِ لِبَاسُهُ لِأَنَّهُ تَبْعٌ لَهُ فَلَا يُعْتَبَرَ حَائِلًا
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں بیٹھے گا پھر وہ بچھونے یا چٹائی پر بیٹھ گیا تو حانث نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اسے زمین پر بیٹھنا نہیں کہا جاتا۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب زمین اور اس کے درمیان اس کا لباس حائل ہو تو حانث ہو جائے گا کیونکہ لباس تابع ہے حائل شمار نہیں ہوگا۔
And if he swore, 'I will not sit on the ground,' then he sat on a carpet or a mat, he does not break his oath because he is not called 'sitting on the ground'. Contrary to the case when his clothing intervenes between him and the ground, because it is an accessory to him, so it is not considered an intervening barrier. (Then Urdu translation equivalent.)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage clarifies an oath regarding sitting on the ground (al-ard). If someone swears not to sit on the ground, and then sits on a carpet (bisāṭ) or mat (haṣīr), he does not break his oath because these are not considered the ground itself. However, if he sits directly on the ground with only his clothing between him and the ground, he does break the oath because his clothing is an accessory (tabʿ) to his body and does not constitute a separate barrier. The key distinction is that mats or carpets are independent objects, whereas clothing is attached to the person.

Key Terms
أَرْض (arḍ): The ground or earth; in oaths, it refers to the natural surface, not coverings upon it.
بِسَاط (bisāṭ): A carpet or spread, considered a separate object from the ground.
حَصِير (haṣīr): A mat, similar to bisāṭ in ruling.
تَبْع (tab‘): An accessory or follower; something that is attached and considered part of the person, like clothing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears not to sit on the ground and then sits on a carpet, does he break his oath according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because the carpet is on the ground.
B) Yes, because he is indirectly sitting on the ground.
C) No, because he is not called 'sitting on the ground' when on a carpet.
D) No, because carpets are exempted from oaths.

Key Takeaway
An oath not to sit on the ground is not broken when the person sits on an independent covering like a carpet or mat; only direct contact with the earth or contact with only an accessory (clothing) breaks the oath.

Oath on Sitting: Accessory vs. Similar Object
Ruling: sitting on a bed with a mat on top breaks the oath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi distinction between an accessory (tābiʿ) and a similar object (mithl) to determine whether an oath not to sit on a bed is broken.

Core Idea
A mat on a bed is an accessory; another bed on top severs the connection.

When a person swears not to sit on a specific bed, the ruling hinges on whether an object placed on the bed is considered an accessory or a similar independent item. This lesson clarifies that a mat or carpet is treated as part of the bed, while a second bed placed on top creates a new seat, cutting the legal connection (nisba). Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying oath rulings in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and act
First, determine the exact wording: 'I will not sit on this bed.' Then, the person performs an action: sitting on the same bed but with a mat or carpet placed on it.
The focus is on the original bed (sarīr) – its identity remains despite the covering.
2
Classify the placed object
Is the object an accessory (tābiʿ) like a mat or carpet, or is it a similar object (mithl) like another bed? An accessory is customarily considered part of the bed; a similar object is independent.
The ruling says 'like the first' (mithl al-awwal) severs the connection.
3
Apply the nisba rule
If the object is an accessory, the legal connection (nisba) to the original bed remains intact – the person is still considered sitting on the bed. If it is a similar object, the nisba is cut.
Nisba here means the attribution of the sitting act to the original bed.
4
Determine hanath (breaking of oath)
Since sitting on the original bed (even with an accessory) breaks the oath, the person becomes sinful (hānith) and must perform kaffārah. With a similar object on top, no hanath occurs.
Kaffārah for a broken oath is feeding/clothing ten poor people or fasting three days.
5
Contrast with hypotheticals
Consider variations: what if the mat is extremely thick or if the second bed is identical? The rule relies on customary perception (ʿurf): a mat is always an accessory; another bed, however thin, severs the link.
Custom (ʿurf) plays a key role in determining what counts as an accessory.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَجْلِسُ عَلَى سَرِيرِ فَجَلَسَ عَلَى سَرِيرِ فَوْقَهُ بِسَاطُ اَوْ حَصِيْرٌ حَنَتَ لِأَنَّهُ يُعَدُّ جَالِسًا عَلَيْهِ وَالْجُلُوسُ عَلَى السَّرِيرِ فِى الْعَادَةِ كَذَالِكَ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا جُعِلَ فَوْقَهُ سَرِيرًا اخَرَلَانَّهُ مِثْلُ الْأَوَّلِ فَقَطَعَ النِّسْبَتُهُ عَنْهُ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے قسم کھائی کہ تخت پر نہیں بیٹھے گا پھر اس تخت پر بیٹھا جس پر بچھونا یا چٹائی بچھی تھی تو حانث ہوگا کیونکہ اسے تخت پر بیٹھا سمجھیں گے۔ اور تخت پر بیٹھنا عادتاً ایسے ہی ہوتا ہے بخلاف اس صورت کے جب اس کے اوپر دوسرا تخت رکھا جائے تو حانث نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ دوسرا تخت پہلے کے مثل ہے اور اس نے نسبت قطع کر دی۔
And if he swore, 'I will not sit on a bed,' then he sat on a bed above which was a carpet or mat, he breaks his oath because he is considered sitting on it, and sitting on a bed customarily is like that. Contrary to the case when another bed is placed above it, for it is like the first and severs the connection from it. (Then Urdu translation equivalent.)
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage deals with an oath not to sit on a particular bed (sarīr). If a person sits on that bed with a mat or carpet laid on top, he breaks his oath because the mat is an accessory (tabʿ) and he is still considered to be sitting on the bed. However, if another bed is placed on top of the original one and he sits on that second bed, he does not break the oath because the second bed is a similar object that severs the connection to the original. This parallels the earlier ruling about sleeping on a bed with another mattress.

Key Terms
سَرِير (sarīr): A bed or couch, often a more structured piece of furniture.
نِسْبَة (nisba): Legal connection or attribution; here, the link between the person and the original bed.
حَنِثَ (hanitha): He broke his oath; the act of violating a solemn oath.
تَابِع (tābiʿ): Accessory; something that is customarily considered part of the main object.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The thickness of the object.
B) Whether the object is an accessory or a similar independent object.
C) The material of the object.
D) The height of the object.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi oath rulings, an accessory on a bed maintains the legal connection, while a similar object severs it – the key is customary classification, not physical separateness.

Oaths on Sleeping and Sitting: The Principle of Taba' and Custom
Rulings on oaths involving surfaces and subordinate items.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on oaths involving sleeping on a bed and sitting on the ground or a specific bed, and apply the concept of taba' (ancillary items) and custom to determine whether an oath is broken.

Core Idea
In Hanafi oaths, what is considered ancillary (taba') to a surface is ignored; only independent layers break the attribution.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents several cases where a person swears not to use a particular surface (bed, ground, specific bed). The rulings hinge on whether an intervening layer is customarily considered part of that surface or an entirely separate object. Understanding the principle of taba' and the role of custom will help you predict when an oath is broken.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general principle of taba'
An item that is subordinate (taba') to a main surface does not change the attribution. For example, a thin covering (qaram) on a bed is taba' to the bed, so sleeping on it still counts as sleeping on the bed. But a similar independent object (another bed) cuts off the relation.
2
Apply to bed with coverings
If one swears not to sleep on a bed and sleeps on it with a thin covering, the oath is broken because the covering is taba'. If another bed is placed on top, the oath is not broken because it is an independent layer.
3
Apply to ground with rugs vs. clothing
Swearing not to sit on the ground: sitting on a rug or mat does not break the oath because customarily one is not considered sitting directly on the ground. But if only one's clothing separates from the ground, it is taba' and the oath is broken.
4
Apply to a specific bed (sariir)
Swearing not to sit on a specific bed: sitting on it with a rug or mat on top breaks the oath because customarily one is still sitting on the bed. But placing another bed on top cuts the relation.
5
Note additional cases: walking and clothes
If one swears not to walk on the ground, walking with shoes or on bricks breaks the oath (shoes are taba'), but walking on a rug does not. If one swears not to sleep on someone's clothes, the majority of the body must be on the clothes for the oath to break.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم كھائی کہ فراش پہ نہیں سوئے گا پھر بچھونا بچھا کر سو گیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا
وَ مَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَنَامُ عَلَى فِرَاشِ فَنَامَ عَلَيْهِ وَفَوْقَهُ قَرَامٌ حَنَتْ لِأَنَّهُ تَبْعٌ لِلْفِرَاشِ فَيُعَدُّ نَائِمًا عَلَيْهِ وَإِنْ جُعِلَ فَوْقَهُ فِرَاشًا أَخَرَ فَنَامَ عَلَيْهِ لَا يَحْنِتُ لِاَنَّ مِثْلَ الشَّيْءِ لَا يَكُونُ تَبْعَالَهُ فَيَنْقَطِعُ النّبْسَةُ عَنِ الْأَوَّلِ وَلَوْ حَلَفَ لَا يَجْلِسُ عَلَى الْأَرْضِ فَجَلَسَ عَلَى بِسَاطٍ أَوْ حَصِيرِ لَمْ يَحْنِثُ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يُسَمَّى جَالِسًا عَلَى الْأَرْضِ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا حَالَ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ الْأَرْضِ لِبَاسُهُ لِأَنَّهُ تَبْعٌ لَهُ فَلَا يُعْتَبَرَ حَائِلًا وَإِنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَجْلِسُ عَلَى سَرِيرِ فَجَلَسَ عَلَى سَرِيرِ فَوْقَهُ بِسَاطُ اَوْ حَصِيْرٌ حَنَتَ لِأَنَّهُ يُعَدُّ جَالِسًا عَلَيْهِ وَالْجُلُوسُ عَلَى السَّرِيرِ فِى الْعَادَةِ كَذَالِكَ بِخِلَافِ مَا إِذَا جُعِلَ فَوْقَهُ سَرِيرًا اخَرَلَانَّهُ مِثْلُ الْأَوَّلِ فَقَطَعَ النِّسْبَتُهُ عَنْهُ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی شخص نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ اس فرش پر نہیں سوؤں گا۔ پھر ایسے فرش پر سویا جس پر بار یک چادر تھی تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ یہ چادر اس فرش کے تابع ہے۔ اس لئے وہ اس فرش پر سونے والا ہی سمجھا جائے گا۔ اور اگر فرش یعنی پچھونے کے اوپر دوسرا بچھونا بچھا کر اس پر سویا تو حانث نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ جو چیز ایک چیز کے مثل ہو وہ اس کی تابع نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی اوپر کا بچھونا نیچے کے بچھونے کا تابع نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے نیچے کے بچھونے پر سونے کی نسبت باقی نہیں رہے گی۔ بلکہ وہ اوپر والے بچھونے پر سونے والا کہا جائے گا۔ اور اگر تم یہ کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں بیٹھوں گا۔ پھر بچھونے یا ٹاٹ اور چٹائی وغیرہ پر بیٹھا تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایسے شخص کو زمین پر بیٹئے والا نہیں کہا جاتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر وہ تم کھانے والے اور زمین کے درمیان اس کا لباس ہو تو وہ زمین پر ہی بیٹھنے والا ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کا لباس اس کے تابع ہے اس لئے وہ حائل شمار نہ ہو گا۔ اور اگر اس نے لباس اتار کر زمین پر ڈال دیا اور اس پر بیٹھ گیا تو اب وہ حانث نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ لباس بچھونے کے حکم میں ہوگا۔ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ اس معین تخت پر نہیں بیٹھوں گا پھر اس پر بچھونا یا چٹائی وغیرہ بچھا کر بیٹھ گیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اس تخت سے مراد معین تخت ہے۔ (الجوہرہ) کیونکہ بچھونا یا چٹائی بچھانے سے بھی وہ تخت ہی پر بیٹھنے والا شمار ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ تخت پر بیٹھنے کی عادت اسی طرح جاری ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر وہ اس تخت کے اوپر دوسرا تخت بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھا تو حانث ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تخت بھی اس پہلے تخت کے جیسا ہے۔ اس لئے پہلے سے اس کا کوئی تعلق نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح... بخلاف ما اذا جعل فوقه سریرا اخر الخ ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ تخت کے اوپر بجائے چٹائی وغیرہ بچھانے کے دوسرا تخت بچھا لیا اور اس پر بیٹھ گیا (ف یعنی اوپر کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا کہلائے گا اور نیچے کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا نہیں کہلائے گا ) ۔ اگر یہ قسم کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں چلوں گا پھر جوتا یا موزہ پہن کر یا اینٹوں پر پاؤں رکھ کر زمین پر چلا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر فرش پر چلا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ت۔ اگر یہ کہا کہ اگر میں تمہارے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا تو میر اغلام آزاد ہے پھر وہ اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا مگر کچھ بدن باہر رہا۔ اب اگر زیادہ بدن اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر ہو تو حانث ہوگا۔ ورنہ نہیں۔
And whoever swears saying 'I will not sleep on a bed', then sleeps on it with a thin covering (qaram) over it: he breaks his oath because it is ancillary (tab') to the bed, so he is considered sleeping on it. And if another bed is placed on top of it and he sleeps on that, he does not break his oath because a thing similar to another is not ancillary to it, so the attribution to the first is cut off. And if he swears not to sit on the ground, then sits on a rug or a mat: he does not break his oath because he is not called 'sitting on the ground'. Contrary to when there is only his clothing between him and the ground, because it is ancillary to him, so it is not considered an intervening barrier. And if he swears not to sit on a specific bed (sariir), then sits on that bed with a rug or mat on top: he breaks his oath because he is considered sitting on it, and sitting on a bed in custom is like that. Contrary to when another bed is placed on top of it, because it is similar to the first and thus cuts off the attribution to it.
Source pages p. 121

Commentary
This passage provides a series of rulings on oaths related to sleeping on a bed and sitting on the ground or on a bed. The key principle is that an item that is subordinate (tab') to the main surface does not change the attribution: if a person swears not to sleep on a particular bed, but sleeps on it with a thin sheet over it, he breaks the oath because the sheet is ancillary. However, if he places another entire mattress on top, he does not break the oath because the new mattress is similar to the first and cuts off the relation. Similarly, if one swears not to sit on the ground, sitting on a rug or mat does not count as sitting on the ground; but if only his clothing separates him, he is still considered sitting on the ground because clothing is ancillary. For a specific bed, sitting on it with a covering counts as sitting on it; but placing another bed on top cuts the relation. The passage also covers walking on ground with shoes or bricks (breaking oath) and oaths regarding sleeping on someone's clothes (majority of body must be on them). These rulings illustrate how custom and the concept of ancillary items determine oath fulfillment in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
تَبَع (taba'): Ancillary; a subordinate item that is considered part of the main object in customary usage.
حَنِثَ (hanitha): To break an oath; to have one's oath violated by the performance of the forbidden act.
فِرَاش (firash): Bed; the surface on which one sleeps, including any bedding that is customarily considered part of it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone swears not to sit on a specific bed, then places a rug on it and sits on the rug, what is the ruling?
A) He breaks the oath because the bed is still the underlying surface.
B) He does not break the oath because the rug is a separate surface.
C) He breaks the oath because the rug is ancillary to the bed.
D) The ruling depends on the material of the rug.

Key Takeaway
Oaths on surfaces depend on custom and the distinction between ancillary and independent layers.

Oaths on Sitting on a Specific Throne: The Role of Custom
Rulings on oaths regarding sitting on thrones with coverings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi custom-based principle to determine whether an oath on sitting on a specific throne is broken when a covering or another throne is placed on it.

Core Idea
A subordinate covering does not change the subject of an oath; an independent object does.

In Hanafi fiqh, the subject of an oath is determined by common custom (urf). This lesson examines the rulings when someone swears not to sit on a specific throne and then places a bedding or a second throne on it. The distinction between subordinate and independent objects is crucial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath subject
The oath specifies a particular throne. The exact object must be determined.
2
Distinguish between subordinate and independent coverings
A bedding or mat is considered subordinate to the throne because it is normally used on it. A second throne is independent because it is a separate object.
3
Apply the customary rule
Custom holds that sitting on a throne with a bedding is still sitting on the throne. Placing a second throne creates a new object of sitting.
4
Determine hanth
If the covering is subordinate, the oath is broken (hanth). If independent, the oath is not broken.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم . حانث نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ جو چیز ایک چیز کے مثل ہو وہ اس کی تابع نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی اوپر کا بچھونا نیچے کے بچھونے کا تابع نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے نیچے کے بچھونے پر سونے کی نسبت باقی نہیں رہے گی۔ ف۔ بلکہ وہ اوپر والے بچھونے پر سونے والا کہا جائے گا۔ اور اگر تم یہ کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں بیٹھوں گا۔ پھر بچھونے یا ٹاٹ اور چٹائی وغیرہ پر بیٹھا تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایسے شخص کو زمین پر بیٹنے والا نہیں کہا جاتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر وہ تم کھانے والے اور زمین کے درمیان اس کا لباس ہو تو وہ زمین پر ہی بیٹھنے والا ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کا لباس اس کے تابع ہے اس لئے وہ حائل شمار نہ ہو گا (ف۔ اور اگر اس نے لباس اتار کر زمین پر ڈال دیا اور اس پر بیٹھ گیا تو اب وہ حانث نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ لباس بچھونے کے حکم میں ہوگا۔ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ اس معین تخت پر نہیں بیٹھوں گا پھر اس پر بچھونا یا چٹائی وغیرہ بچھا کر بیٹھ گیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا ۔ف۔اس تخت سے مراد معین تخت ہے۔ الجوہرہ) کیونکہ بچھونا یا چٹائی بچھانے سے بھی وہ تخت ہی پر بیٹھنے والا شمار ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ تخت پر بیٹھنے کی عادت اسی طرح جاری ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر وہ اس تخت کے اوپر دوسرا تخت بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھا تو حانث ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تخت بھی اس پہلے تخت کے جیسا ہے۔ اس لئے پہلے سے اس کا کوئی تعلق نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح... بخلاف ما اذا جعل فوقه سریرا اخر الخ ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ تخت کے اوپر بجائے چٹائی وغیرہ بچھانے کے دوسرا تخت بچھا لیا اور اس پر بیٹھ گیا (ف یعنی اوپر کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا کہلائے گا اور نیچے کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا نہیں کہلائے گا ) ۔ اگر یہ قسم کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں چلوں گا پھر جوتا یا موزہ پہن کر یا اینٹوں پر پاؤں رکھ کر زمین پر چلا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر فرش پر چلا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ت۔ اگر یہ کہا کہ اگر میں تمہارے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا تو میر اغلام آزاد ہے پھر وہ اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا مگر کچھ بدن باہر رہا۔ اب اگر زیادہ بدن اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر ہو تو حانث ہوگا۔ ورنہ نہیں۔
Sharh Urdu Hidayah volume six. He will not break his oath because when something is like another thing, it is not subordinate to it. That is, the upper bedding is not subordinate to the lower bedding; therefore, the relation of sleeping on the lower bedding ceases. f. Rather, he will be called one who sleeps on the upper bedding. And if you swear that you will not sit on the ground, then sit on a bedding or mat or rug, he does not break his oath because such a person is not called one sitting on the ground. On the contrary, if between the swearer and the ground there is his clothing, then he is considered sitting on the ground because his clothing is subordinate to him, so it is not considered a barrier. f. And if he takes off his clothing and spreads it on the ground and sits on it, then he does not break his oath because that clothing is in the ruling of a bedding. And if someone swears that he will not sit on a specific throne, then spreads a bedding or mat on it and sits, he breaks his oath. f. This throne refers to a specific throne (al-Jawhara). Because by spreading a bedding or mat, he is still considered sitting on that throne, as the custom of sitting on the throne continues. Contrary to if he places another throne on top of that throne and sits on it, he breaks his oath because this throne is also like the first throne, so there is no relation to the first. Explanation: Contrary to the case when he places another throne on top of the throne instead of a mat etc. and sits on it (f. That is, he will be called one sitting on the upper throne, and he will not be called one sitting on the lower throne). And if he swears that he will not walk on the ground, then wears shoes or socks or puts bricks under his feet and walks on the ground, he breaks his oath. And if he walks on a carpet, he does not break his oath. t. And if he said, 'If I sleep on your clothes or bedding, my slave is free,' then he sleeps on his clothes or bedding but some of his body remains outside. Now if the majority of his body is on his clothes or bedding, he breaks his oath; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage consists of several rulings from the Hanafi school regarding oaths (ymin) related to sitting, walking, and sleeping on specific surfaces. The key principle is that the subject of the oath is determined by common custom (urf) and the direct relation between the oath taker and the object. When an oath prohibits sitting on a specific throne, placing a bedding or mat on it does not change the fact that one is still considered sitting on that throne, so the oath is broken. However, placing a similar throne on top creates a new independent surface, so the oath regarding the original throne is not broken. Similarly, an oath against walking on the ground is broken if one walks on the ground with shoes or on bricks, but not if walking on a carpet, because the carpet is considered a barrier separating from the ground. For sleeping on someone's clothes, the ruling depends on where the majority of the body lies.

Key Terms
حانث (hānith): One who breaks an oath, i.e., violates the condition of the oath.
بچھونا (bichhona): Bedding or spread placed on a surface for sitting or sleeping.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if someone swears not to sit on a specific throne and then places a second throne on top of it and sits, what is the outcome?
A) He breaks his oath because he is still sitting on the same spot.
B) He breaks his oath because the second throne is subordinate.
C) He does not break his oath because he is considered sitting on the second throne.
D) He does not break his oath because the second throne is a covering.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the subject of an oath is determined by custom; subordinate coverings do not change the oath subject, but independent objects do.

Oaths on Sitting on the Ground: The Role of Clothing and Beddings
Rulings on oaths regarding sitting on the ground with various coverings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine whether an oath not to sit on the ground is broken when the person sits on a bedding, mat, or on clothing, according to Hanafi custom-based rulings.

Core Idea
Clothing worn is subordinate; clothing removed becomes like a bedding.

This lesson focuses on the Hanafi rulings for oaths involving sitting on the ground. The key is whether the person is considered 'sitting on the ground' according to custom. Beddings and mats create a barrier, while clothing worn does not, but removed clothing transforms into a bedding-like covering.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath subject
The oath is 'not to sit on the ground'.
2
Determine the type of covering
Ask: Is the covering subordinate to the person (e.g., clothing being worn) or an independent object (e.g., bedding, mat, or removed clothing)?
3
Apply custom
If the covering is subordinate (worn clothing), the person is still considered sitting on the ground. If independent (bedding, mat, or removed clothing spread), he is not considered sitting on the ground.
4
Conclude hanth
If sitting on ground with subordinate covering → hanth. If sitting on independent covering → la hanth.

اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد ششم . حانث نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ جو چیز ایک چیز کے مثل ہو وہ اس کی تابع نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ یعنی اوپر کا بچھونا نیچے کے بچھونے کا تابع نہیں ہوگا۔ اس لئے نیچے کے بچھونے پر سونے کی نسبت باقی نہیں رہے گی۔ ف۔ بلکہ وہ اوپر والے بچھونے پر سونے والا کہا جائے گا۔ اور اگر تم یہ کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں بیٹھوں گا۔ پھر بچھونے یا ٹاٹ اور چٹائی وغیرہ پر بیٹھا تو وہ حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ کیونکہ ایسے شخص کو زمین پر بیٹنے والا نہیں کہا جاتا ہے۔ اس کے برخلاف اگر وہ تم کھانے والے اور زمین کے درمیان اس کا لباس ہو تو وہ زمین پر ہی بیٹھنے والا ہو گا۔ کیونکہ اس کا لباس اس کے تابع ہے اس لئے وہ حائل شمار نہ ہو گا (ف۔ اور اگر اس نے لباس اتار کر زمین پر ڈال دیا اور اس پر بیٹھ گیا تو اب وہ حانث نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ وہ لباس بچھونے کے حکم میں ہوگا۔ اور اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ اس معین تخت پر نہیں بیٹھوں گا پھر اس پر بچھونا یا چٹائی وغیرہ بچھا کر بیٹھ گیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا ۔ف۔اس تخت سے مراد معین تخت ہے۔ الجوہرہ) کیونکہ بچھونا یا چٹائی بچھانے سے بھی وہ تخت ہی پر بیٹھنے والا شمار ہوتا ہے۔ کیونکہ تخت پر بیٹھنے کی عادت اسی طرح جاری ہے۔ بخلاف اس کے اگر وہ اس تخت کے اوپر دوسرا تخت بچھا کر اس پر بیٹھا تو حانث ہوگا۔ کیونکہ یہ تخت بھی اس پہلے تخت کے جیسا ہے۔ اس لئے پہلے سے اس کا کوئی تعلق نہ ہوگا۔
تشریح... بخلاف ما اذا جعل فوقه سریرا اخر الخ ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ تخت کے اوپر بجائے چٹائی وغیرہ بچھانے کے دوسرا تخت بچھا لیا اور اس پر بیٹھ گیا (ف یعنی اوپر کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا کہلائے گا اور نیچے کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا نہیں کہلائے گا ) ۔ اگر یہ قسم کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں چلوں گا پھر جوتا یا موزہ پہن کر یا اینٹوں پر پاؤں رکھ کر زمین پر چلا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر فرش پر چلا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ت۔ اگر یہ کہا کہ اگر میں تمہارے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا تو میر اغلام آزاد ہے پھر وہ اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا مگر کچھ بدن باہر رہا۔ اب اگر زیادہ بدن اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر ہو تو حانث ہوگا۔ ورنہ نہیں۔
Sharh Urdu Hidayah volume six. He will not break his oath because when something is like another thing, it is not subordinate to it. That is, the upper bedding is not subordinate to the lower bedding; therefore, the relation of sleeping on the lower bedding ceases. f. Rather, he will be called one who sleeps on the upper bedding. And if you swear that you will not sit on the ground, then sit on a bedding or mat or rug, he does not break his oath because such a person is not called one sitting on the ground. On the contrary, if between the swearer and the ground there is his clothing, then he is considered sitting on the ground because his clothing is subordinate to him, so it is not considered a barrier. f. And if he takes off his clothing and spreads it on the ground and sits on it, then he does not break his oath because that clothing is in the ruling of a bedding. And if someone swears that he will not sit on a specific throne, then spreads a bedding or mat on it and sits, he breaks his oath. f. This throne refers to a specific throne (al-Jawhara). Because by spreading a bedding or mat, he is still considered sitting on that throne, as the custom of sitting on the throne continues. Contrary to if he places another throne on top of that throne and sits on it, he breaks his oath because this throne is also like the first throne, so there is no relation to the first. Explanation: Contrary to the case when he places another throne on top of the throne instead of a mat etc. and sits on it (f. That is, he will be called one sitting on the upper throne, and he will not be called one sitting on the lower throne). And if he swears that he will not walk on the ground, then wears shoes or socks or puts bricks under his feet and walks on the ground, he breaks his oath. And if he walks on a carpet, he does not break his oath. t. And if he said, 'If I sleep on your clothes or bedding, my slave is free,' then he sleeps on his clothes or bedding but some of his body remains outside. Now if the majority of his body is on his clothes or bedding, he breaks his oath; otherwise not.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage consists of several rulings from the Hanafi school regarding oaths (ymin) related to sitting, walking, and sleeping on specific surfaces. The key principle is that the subject of the oath is determined by common custom (urf) and the direct relation between the oath taker and the object. When an oath prohibits sitting on a specific throne, placing a bedding or mat on it does not change the fact that one is still considered sitting on that throne, so the oath is broken. However, placing a similar throne on top creates a new independent surface, so the oath regarding the original throne is not broken. Similarly, an oath against walking on the ground is broken if one walks on the ground with shoes or on bricks, but not if walking on a carpet, because the carpet is considered a barrier separating from the ground. For sleeping on someone's clothes, the ruling depends on where the majority of the body lies.

Key Terms
حانث (hānith): One who breaks an oath.
بچھونا (bichhona): Bedding or spread.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi ruling in this passage, if someone swears not to sit on the ground and sits on a cushion placed directly on the ground, what is the outcome?
A) Oath is broken because the cushion is a covering.
B) Oath is broken because the person is sitting on the ground.
C) Oath is not broken because the cushion is independent.
D) Oath is not broken because the cushion is subordinate.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, an oath not to sit on the ground is broken only when sitting directly on the ground or on a subordinate covering like worn clothing.

Oaths on Walking and Sleeping: Custom and Majority Rule
Rulings on oaths regarding walking on ground and sleeping on clothes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to determine the Hanafi rulings for oaths on walking on the ground and sleeping on clothes, applying the principles of custom and majority of the body.

Core Idea
Walking on ground with shoes breaks oath; carpet does not. Sleeping on clothes depends on where most of body lies.

This lesson covers two distinct rulings: oaths about walking on the ground and oaths about sleeping on someone's clothes or bedding. The first relies on custom (shoes are like direct contact, carpet is a barrier), and the second relies on the majority of the body being on the specified object.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath for walking
The oath is 'not to walk on the ground'.
2
Distinguish between types of covering
Shoes and socks are customarily considered part of walking on the ground; bricks placed under feet also do not create a barrier. A carpet is a separate covering that prevents direct contact.
3
Apply custom to walking
Walking with shoes, socks, or on bricks still counts as walking on the ground. Walking on a carpet does not.
4
Identify the oath for sleeping
The oath is to sleep on someone's clothes or bedding, with a freeing of a slave as consequence.
5
Apply the majority rule
If the majority of the body (more than half) is on the clothes/bedding, the oath is broken. If less than half, the oath is not broken.

Source Text

تشریح... بخلاف ما اذا جعل فوقه سریرا اخر الخ ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جب کہ تخت کے اوپر بجائے چٹائی وغیرہ بچھانے کے دوسرا تخت بچھا لیا اور اس پر بیٹھ گیا (ف یعنی اوپر کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا کہلائے گا اور نیچے کے تخت پر بیٹھنے والا نہیں کہلائے گا ) ۔ اگر یہ قسم کھائی کہ زمین پر نہیں چلوں گا پھر جوتا یا موزہ پہن کر یا اینٹوں پر پاؤں رکھ کر زمین پر چلا تو حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور اگر فرش پر چلا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ت۔ اگر یہ کہا کہ اگر میں تمہارے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا تو میر اغلام آزاد ہے پھر وہ اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر سویا مگر کچھ بدن باہر رہا۔ اب اگر زیادہ بدن اس کے کپڑے یا بچھونے پر ہو تو حانث ہوگا۔ ورنہ نہیں۔

Oaths on Killing, Beating, Clothing, Speaking, Entering, and Washing
Chapter establishing that oaths on actions apply only to the living, except washing of the dead.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which actions in an oath apply only to the living and which apply to the dead, and explain the legal reasoning (ta'lil) behind the Hanafi ruling.

Core Idea
An oath on a life-specific action is broken only during life; washing the dead is an exception because it is a physical act.

In this passage from al-Hidayah, the Hanafi school lays down a general principle: oaths involving actions that inherently require a living subject—like causing pain, transferring ownership, or personal conversation—are confined to the lifetime of the person sworn about. However, actions purely physical, like washing the body, apply even after death. This lesson unpacks the definitions and reasoning (ta'lil) behind each case.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The text states that for matters where the living and dead share the same status, the oath applies to both; for matters specific to life, like pain or wealth, the oath is confined to life.
This principle governs all the following cases.
2
Analyze each action's illa
For each action (beating, clothing, speech, entering, washing), identify the defining characteristic that either requires life or does not. For example, beating is defined as a painful act on a living body; clothing at absolute use implies ownership; speech aims at conveying understanding; entering means visiting the person; washing is defined as pouring water for purification.
The illa determines whether the action can be realized on a dead body.
3
Apply the principle to each case
Based on the illa, determine if the oath is broken after death. Beating, clothing (ownership), speech, and entering are not realized on the dead, so the oath is not broken. Washing is realized, so the oath is broken.
Exception: if the intention in clothing is covering (satr), it may also apply to the dead.
4
Address the objection regarding the Prophet's speech to the dead
The hadith of Badr is raised as an objection that speech can benefit the dead. The Hanafi response distinguishes it as a miracle of prophethood and an afterlife matter, not analogous to worldly speech.
This does not override the general rule.
