باب اليمين في القتل والضرب وغيره
ترجمہ باب تحمل کرنے اور مارنے وغیرہ میں قسم کھانے کا بیان
باب اليمين في القتل والضرب وغيره .. الخ یہ باب مارنے اور قتل کرنے وغیرہ میں تم کھانے کے بیان میں ہے۔ اس موقع میں اصل بات یہ ہے کہ جس بات میں زندہ اور مردہ دونوں شریک اور برابر ہوتے ہیں یعنی اس کے حکم میں دونوں کا حال ایک جیسا ہوتا ہے تو اس کی قسم دونوں حالتوں زندگی اور موت پر واقع ہوگی اور جو بات فقط زندگی کے ساتھ مخصوص ہو جیسے دکھ، در دولت و خوشی تو یہ تم صرف زندگی ہی تک مخصوص ہوگی۔
قسم کھائی کہ اگر میں نے تم کو مارا تو میرا اعلام آزاد تو یہ تم زندگی تک محدود ہوگی
وَمَنْ قَالَ إِنْ ضَرَبْتُكَ فَعَبْدِي حُرٌّ فَهُوَ عَلَى الْحَيَاةِ لِأَنَّ الضَّرَبَ اسْمٌ لِفِعْلٍ مُؤْلِمٍ يَتَعَلَّقُ بِالْبَدَنِ وَالْإِيْلَامُ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ فِي الْمَيِّتِ وَمَنْ يُعَذِّبُ فِي الْقَبْرِ يُوضَعُ فِيهِ الْحَيَوَةُ فِي قَوْلِ الْعَامَّةِ وَكَذَلِكَ الْكِسْوَةُ لِأَنَّهُ يُرَادُ بِالتَّمْلِيكِ عِنْدَ الْإِطْلَاقِ وَمِنْهُ الْكِسْوَةُ فِي الْكَفَّارَةِ وَهُوَ مِنَ الْمَيِّتِ لَا يَتَحَقَّقُ إِلَّا أَنْ يَنْوِيَ بِهِ السَّتْرَ وَقِيلَ بِالْفَارِسِيَّةِ يَنْصَرِفُ إِلَى اللُّبْسِ وَكَذَا الْكَلَامُ وَالدُّخُولُ لِأَنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ الْكَلَامِ الْإِفْهَامُ وَالْمَوْتُ يُنَافِيهِ وَالْمُرَادُ مِنَ الدُّخُولِ عَلَيْهِ زِيَارَتُهُ وَبَعْدَ الْمَوْتِ يُزَارُ قَبْرُهُ لَا هُوَ
ترجمہ اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ اگر میں نے تم کو مارا تو میر اغلام آزاد ہے۔ تو یہ تم اس کے زندہ رہنے تک کے لئے ہے۔ یعنی اگر اس کو زندگی میں مارا تو غلام آزاد ہوگا۔ اور اگر اس کی موت کے بعد اسے مارا تو خانٹ نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ مارنا ایک ایسے دکھ دینے والے فعل کا نام ہے جس کا تعلق بدن سے ہو۔ جبکہ دکھ دینا مردہ کے بدن میں ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ لیکن قبر میں مردہ پر عذاب برحق ہے تو اس کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ جمہور اصل اسلام کے نزدیک مردہ میں دوبارہ (مخصوص حیات) رکھی جاتی ہے ( بلکہ یہ تو آخرت کے حکموں میں سے ہے۔ اور دنیاوی زندگی پر اس کا قیاس نہیں ہو سکتا ہے ۔ مارنے کے بارے میں جو حکم بیان کیا گیا وہی حکم لباس پہنانے اور دینے کا بھی ہے۔ یعنی اس حکم کا تعلق صرف اس کی زندگی رہنے تک ہو گا۔ اور مروں کا کفن اس میں شامل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جب مطلقا یوں کہا کہ واللہ میں زید کو لباس اور کسوت دوں گا تو اس سے مراد ما لک کر دینا ہوتا ہے اور اسی سے کفارہ ( یمین ) میں کسوت کا حکم ہے اور کسی مردہ کو کپڑے کا ( یا کسی اور چیز کا مالک نہیں بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر کہتے وقت کسوت سے اس کہنے والے کی مراد یہ ہو کہ میں اس کی ستر پوشی کروں گا تو کپڑے کا حکم مردہ سے بھی متعلق ہو جائے گا۔ اور فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا ہے کہ فارسی میں کسوت سے مراد صرف پہنانا ہوگا۔ فائدہ یعنی مالک بنانا ضروری نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس کے مرجانے کے بعد پہنایا تو بھی حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اسی طرح کلام کرنے اور داخل ہونا بھی زندگی کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ کیونکہ کلام سے یہ مقصود ہوتا ہے کہ اسے اپنا مفہوم و مضمون سمجھائے اور موت اسکے مخالف ہے اور داخل ہونے سے مراد اس کی زیارت ہے۔ مرنے کے بعد اس کی زیارت نہیں ہوتی ہے بلکہ اس کی قبر کی زیارت ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح.... و كذا الكلام و الدخول اس طرح کلام کرتا اور داخل ہونا بھی زندگی کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ فائدہ یعنی اگر یہ کہا کہ میں زید سے کلام نہیں کروں گا۔ تو اس کی زندگی میں کلام کرنے سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور موت کے بعد نہیں ہو گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کی موت کے بعد اس سے کلام کیا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ اس طرح اگر یہ کہا کہ میں زید کے پاس داخل نہ ہوں گا۔ تو زید کی زندگی تک حکم مخصوص رہے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر اس کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے پاس گیا تو حانث نہ ہوگا۔
لانَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ الْكَلَامِ الْإِفْهَامِ وَالْمَوْتُ يُنَافِيهِ وَالْمُرَادُ مِنَ الدُّخُولُ عَلَيْهِ زِيَارَتُهُ ... الخ کیونکہ کلام کی غرض تو یہ ہوتی ہے کہ مخاطب کو اپنا مضمون سمجھا دے۔ جبکہ اس کی موت اس کے منافی ہے۔ فائدہ یعنی موت کے بعد سمجھا نا ممکن نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بدر کے مقتول کا فروں کو ان کے نام لے کر پکار کر فرمایا تھا کہ تمہارے رب نے تم سے عذاب کا جو وعدہ کیا تھا وہ تم نے بیج پایا یا نہیں۔ اور جب آپ سے صحابہ کرام نے پوچھا کہ یا رسول اللہ کیا یہ مردے سنتے ہیں تو فرمایا کہ تم سے زیادہ سنتے ہیں۔ اس سے ظاہر ہوا کہ مردہ سے کلام کرنا بھی سمجھانے کے لئے مفید ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا کلام کرنا شان نبوت کا معجزہ تھا۔ اور ان مردہ کافروں کا سنتا اس دنیا وی سننے پر قیاس نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اسی لئے حدیث میں آپ نے صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم کو فرمایا کہ تم ان سے زیادہ سننے والے نہیں ہو۔ یعنی وہ تم سے زیادہ سنتے ہیں۔ پس زیادتی اسی معنی میں ہے کہ اسماع آخرت اور حضرت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے معجزہ کے طور پر ہے۔ والمراد من الدخول اور داخل ہونے سے مراد اس کی زیارت کرنے کی ہے۔ جبکہ موت کے بعد زیارت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ بلکہ اس کی قبر کی زیارت ہوتی ہے۔
قسم کھائی کہ اگر میں تم کو نسل دوں تو میر اعلام آزاد ہے موت کے بعد غسل دیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا وَلَوْ قَالَ إِنْ غَسَلْتُكَ فَعَبْدِي حُرٌّ فَغَسَلَهُ بَعْدَ مَامَاتَ يَحْنَثُ لِأَنَّ الْغُسْلَ هُوَ الْإِسَالَةُ وَمَعْنَاهُ التَّطْهِيرُ وَيَتَحَقَّقُ ذَلِكَ فِي الْمَيِّتِ
ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے کسی سے یہ کہا کہ اگر میں تم کو نس دان دوں تو میرا اعلام آزاد ہے۔ اب اگر مرنے کے بعد غسل دیا تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا
Chapter on oaths in killing, beating, etc. Translation: Chapter on swearing regarding causing harm, beating, etc. The chapter on oaths in killing, beating, etc. The basic principle in this context is that for matters in which the living and the dead share the same status, the oath applies to both states of life and death; but for matters specific to life, like pain, illness, wealth, and happiness, the oath is confined to life. If one swears: 'If I beat you, my slave is free,' then the oath applies to life, because beating is the name of a painful action that relates to the body, and causing pain is not realized in a dead person. As for the punishment in the grave, that is because the common people hold that a special life is placed in the dead. But that is among the rulings of the Hereafter and cannot be analogized to worldly life. The same ruling applies to clothing: when the word 'clothing' is used absolutely, it means giving ownership; thus the clothing in expiation (kaffarah) is also understood as ownership, and this cannot be realized with a dead person, unless he intended covering (satr). It was said that in Persian, it refers simply to wearing. Similarly, speech and entering are specific to life, because the purpose of speech is to convey meaning, and death prevents that; the purpose of entering is to visit him, and after death, one visits his grave, not him. Explanation: Speech and entering are specific to life. Benefit: If he said, 'I will not speak to Zaid,' he breaks his oath if he speaks during Zaid's lifetime, but not after death. Likewise, if he said, 'I will not enter upon Zaid,' it is confined to his lifetime. The objective of speech is to make the addressee understand, and death prevents that. The objective of entering is to visit him. If it is said that the Prophet (peace be upon him) called out to the killed polytheists of Badr and said, 'Did you find your Lord's promise true?' and when the Companions asked if the dead hear, he replied, 'They hear more than you,' that shows that speaking to the dead can be beneficial for understanding. The answer is that the Prophet's speech was a miracle of prophethood, and the hearing of those dead polytheists cannot be compared to worldly hearing. The excess mentioned in the hadith refers to hearing of the Hereafter and as a miracle of the Prophet. And the meaning of entering is to visit him; after death, one does not visit him but rather his grave. If one swears: 'If I wash you, my slave is free,' and he washes him after death, he breaks his oath, because washing means pouring water and its meaning is purification, and that is realized with the dead. Translation: And if someone said to someone, 'If I wash you, my slave is free,' then if he washes him after death, he breaks his oath.
Source pages p. 122

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on oaths concerning killing, beating, etc., establishes a key principle in Hanafi fiqh: oaths that involve actions necessarily involving a living person (such as causing pain, transferring ownership, communicating, or personal visitation) are limited to the lifetime of the person concerned. The text provides the legal basis (illa) for each: beating is defined as a painful act on the body, which cannot affect a corpse; clothing (kiswah) at absolute use implies giving ownership, which is impossible after death unless the intention is covering (satr); speech aims at conveying understanding, impossible after death; entering means visiting the person, not the grave. However, washing a dead body is an exception because washing (ghusl) is defined as pouring water for purification, which can be performed on a dead body, so the oath is broken. The passage also addresses an objection regarding the dead hearing the Prophet's speech at Badr, distinguishing it as a miracle of prophethood and a matter of the Hereafter, not analogous to worldly speech.

Key Terms
الضرب (al-ḍarb): Beating; a painful action that affects the body. It is defined as an act that causes pain to a living body.
الكسوة (al-kiswah): Clothing; in the context of oaths, it generally implies giving ownership (tamlik) unless the intention is covering (satr) or wearing (lubs), as in Persian usage.
الغسل (al-ghusl): Washing; defined as pouring water (isalah) with the meaning of purification (tathir). It can be performed on a dead body, so the oath applies after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone swears 'If I beat you, my slave is free,' and then beats the person after his death, does he break his oath?
A) Yes, because beating is a physical act that can be done on a dead body.
B) No, because beating is defined as a painful action that cannot be realized on a dead body.
C) Yes, because the dead can feel pain in the grave.
D) No, because all oaths are limited to the lifetime by default.

Key Takeaway
Oaths on actions that inherently require life (pain, ownership, communication, visitation) are not broken after death, but washing the dead is an exception because it is a physical act that can be performed on a corpse.

The Ruling on Oaths to Clothe a Dead Person
Ruling on oath to clothe a dead person, distinguishing ownership from covering.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when a person swears to give clothing to someone who then dies, and distinguish between the default implication of ownership and the exceptional case of intention to cover.

Core Idea
An oath to give clothing implies ownership, impossible after death, unless the intention was merely to cover the body.

In Hanafi fiqh, oaths regarding actions toward others are interpreted according to default meanings. This passage addresses the specific case of swearing to clothe a person who subsequently dies. The ruling depends on whether the oath implies transferring ownership or simply covering the body. Understanding the role of intention (niyyah) is key to determining whether the oath is fulfilled.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the default implication
The act is an oath to give clothing (kiswah) to a specific person. The default legal implication is that the oath-taker intends to transfer ownership of the garment to the recipient.
2
Determine the effect of the recipient's death
Since a dead person cannot own property, the default ownership-based fulfillment becomes impossible after death. Therefore, giving the garment after death does not fulfill the oath under the default interpretation.
3
Identify the exception based on intention
If the oath-taker's intention at the time of swearing was to cover the dead person's body (satr/covering), then the oath is fulfilled by clothing the deceased after death, because covering is physically possible.
Also consider the view of Faqih Abu al-Layth that in Persian, 'kiswah' only means to clothe, not to own, so giving after death always fulfills the oath.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مارنے کے بارے میں جو حکم بیان کیا گیا وہی حکم لباس پہنانے اور دینے کا بھی ہے۔ یعنی اس حکم کا تعلق صرف اس کی زندگی رہنے تک ہو گا۔ اور مروں کا کفن اس میں شامل نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ جب مطلقا یوں کہا کہ واللہ میں زید کو لباس اور کسوت دوں گا تو اس سے مراد ما لک کر دینا ہوتا ہے اور اسی سے کفارہ ( یمین ) میں کسوت کا حکم ہے اور کسی مردہ کو کپڑے کا ( یا کسی اور چیز کا مالک نہیں بنایا جا سکتا ہے۔ لیکن اگر کہتے وقت کسوت سے اس کہنے والے کی مراد یہ ہو کہ میں اس کی ستر پوشی کروں گا تو کپڑے کا حکم مردہ سے بھی متعلق ہو جائے گا۔ اور فقیہ ابواللیث نے کہا ہے کہ فارسی میں کسوت سے مراد صرف پہنانا ہوگا۔ فائدہ یعنی مالک بنانا ضروری نہیں ہے یہاں تک کہ اگر اس کے مرجانے کے بعد پہنایا تو بھی حانث نہیں ہوگا۔
The same ruling that was mentioned regarding beating applies to clothing and giving. That is, this ruling only pertains to his lifetime. And the shroud of the dead is not included in this. Because when one says absolutely, 'By Allah, I will give Zaid clothing and kiswah,' the intention is to make him the owner, and from this the ruling of kiswah in the expiation of an oath is derived. And a dead person cannot be made the owner of clothing (or any other thing). But if at the time of saying, the speaker's intention from kiswah is that I will cover his private parts, then the ruling of clothing will also apply to the dead. And Faqih Abu al-Layth said that in Persian, kiswah only means to clothe. Benefit: making the owner is not necessary, such that if he clothed him after his death, he does not become a breaker of the oath.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage extends the earlier ruling about beating a dead person to clothing. The general principle is that an oath to give something to a person only applies during that person's life, because after death, ownership cannot be transferred. However, if the oath-taker's intent is specifically to cover the dead person's body (i.e., to act as a shroud), then the oath becomes binding even after death because the action of covering is possible. The Persian usage of 'kiswah' implies simply putting on clothing, not ownership. Therefore, if one swears to clothe a person and that person dies, clothing him after death does not break the oath if the intention was covering, not ownership.

Key Terms
كسوت (kiswah): Clothing or garment; in the context of an oath it means either to give ownership of a garment or to cover the body, depending on intention.
حانث (hānith): One who breaks his oath, incurring the penalty of kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person swears, 'By Allah, I will give Zaid a garment,' and Zaid dies before he gives it, does he become a breaker of the oath if he gives it after death?
A) Yes, because the oath is absolute and must be fulfilled.
B) No, unless his intention was to cover Zaid's body.
C) Yes, because giving after death fulfills the literal meaning.
D) No, because the dead can own property.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, an oath to clothe a person is interpreted as a promise to transfer ownership unless the intention to cover is explicit; after death, only the covering intention can be fulfilled.

Oaths on Speech and Entry Are Limited to Life
Ruling on oaths about speaking to or entering upon a person, applying only during life.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that oaths about speaking to or visiting a person apply only during the person's lifetime and explain why the Prophet's address to the dead at Badr does not affect this ruling.

Core Idea
An oath about speaking to or visiting a person applies only during their life.

When you swear not to speak to someone or not to visit them, your oath is tied to actions that can only be done with a living person. Speech requires conveying meaning; entering requires visiting the person. After death, these actions become impossible or are of a different nature. This lesson dissects the ruling, its rationale, and addresses the potential objection from the Prophet's interaction with the dead at Badr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Consider a person who swears, 'I will not speak to Zaid' or 'I will not enter upon Zaid.' The ruling is that the oath is only binding during Zaid's lifetime. If Zaid dies and the person speaks to him or goes to his grave, the oath is not broken.
The key is that the oath's subject matter (speech or entry) is inherently connected to life.
2
Understand the rationale
Speech (kalām) aims to convey meaning (ifhām), which is impossible after death. Entry (dukhūl) means visiting the person (ziyārah), not visiting the grave.
Death negates the purpose of speech, and visiting a dead person is not the same as visiting the living.
3
Address the objection from the Badr incident
The Prophet (peace be upon him) spoke to the dead polytheists at Badr, and they heard. This might suggest that speech to the dead is possible. However, this was a miracle of prophethood and not a general ruling.
Miracles are not a basis for legal analogy (qiyās).
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If someone swears not to enter upon a friend, and the friend dies, visiting his grave does not break the oath because the act is now 'visiting the grave' not 'entering upon the person.'
The oath is interpreted according to customary understanding (urf).

Source Text

اسی طرح کلام کرنے اور داخل ہونا بھی زندگی کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ کیونکہ کلام سے یہ مقصود ہوتا ہے کہ اسے اپنا مفہوم و مضمون سمجھائے اور موت اسکے مخالف ہے اور داخل ہونے سے مراد اس کی زیارت ہے۔ مرنے کے بعد اس کی زیارت نہیں ہوتی ہے بلکہ اس کی قبر کی زیارت ہوتی ہے۔ تشریح.... و كذا الكلام و الدخول اس طرح کلام کرتا اور داخل ہونا بھی زندگی کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے۔ فائدہ یعنی اگر یہ کہا کہ میں زید سے کلام نہیں کروں گا۔ تو اس کی زندگی میں کلام کرنے سے حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اور موت کے بعد نہیں ہو گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اس کی موت کے بعد اس سے کلام کیا تو حانث نہیں ہو گا۔ اس طرح اگر یہ کہا کہ میں زید کے پاس داخل نہ ہوں گا۔ تو زید کی زندگی تک حکم مخصوص رہے گا۔ یہاں تک کہ اگر اس کے مرنے کے بعد اس کے پاس گیا تو حانث نہ ہوگا۔ لانَّ الْمَقْصُودَ مِنَ الْكَلَامِ الْإِفْهَامِ وَالْمَوْتُ يُنَافِيهِ وَالْمُرَادُ مِنَ الدُّخُولُ عَلَيْهِ زِيَارَتُهُ ... الخ کیونکہ کلام کی غرض تو یہ ہوتی ہے کہ مخاطب کو اپنا مضمون سمجھا دے۔ جبکہ اس کی موت اس کے منافی ہے۔ فائدہ یعنی موت کے بعد سمجھا نا ممکن نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ اگر یہ کہا جائے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے بدر کے مقتول کا فروں کو ان کے نام لے کر پکار کر فرمایا تھا کہ تمہارے رب نے تم سے عذاب کا جو وعدہ کیا تھا وہ تم نے بیج پایا یا نہیں۔ اور جب آپ سے صحابہ کرام نے پوچھا کہ یا رسول اللہ کیا یہ مردے سنتے ہیں تو فرمایا کہ تم سے زیادہ سنتے ہیں۔ اس سے ظاہر ہوا کہ مردہ سے کلام کرنا بھی سمجھانے کے لئے مفید ہے۔ اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کا کلام کرنا شان نبوت کا معجزہ تھا۔ اور ان مردہ کافروں کا سنتا اس دنیا وی سننے پر قیاس نہیں ہو سکتا ہے۔ اسی لئے حدیث میں آپ نے صحابہ کرام رضی اللہ عنہم کو فرمایا کہ تم ان سے زیادہ سننے والے نہیں ہو۔ یعنی وہ تم سے زیادہ سنتے ہیں۔ پس زیادتی اسی معنی میں ہے کہ اسماع آخرت اور حضرت رسول اللہ صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم کے معجزہ کے طور پر ہے۔ والمراد من الدخول اور داخل ہونے سے مراد اس کی زیارت کرنے کی ہے۔ جبکہ موت کے بعد زیارت نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ بلکہ اس کی قبر کی زیارت ہوتی ہے۔
Similarly, speaking and entering are also specific to life. Because the purpose of speech is to convey one's meaning and content, and death contradicts that. And the meaning of entering is to visit him. After death, one does not visit him, rather one visits his grave. Explanation: 'And likewise speech and entering' — so speaking and entering are also specific to life. Benefit: If he said, 'I will not speak to Zaid,' then speaking to him during his life makes him a breaker, but after death it does not. Thus, if he spoke to him after his death, he does not break the oath. Similarly, if he said, 'I will not enter upon Zaid,' the ruling is confined to Zaid's life, such that if he went to him after his death, he does not break the oath. Because the purpose of speech is to make understand, and death prevents that. And the intent of entering upon him is a visit. Explanation: 'Because the purpose of speech is to make the addressee understand one's content, and his death is contrary to that.' Benefit: After death, making understand is not possible. If it is said that the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) called out to the slain people of Badr by name and said, 'Have you found what your Lord promised you of punishment?' And when the Companions asked, 'O Messenger of Allah, do these dead hear?' He said, 'They hear better than you.' This shows that speaking to the dead is also beneficial for understanding. The answer to this is that the speech of the Messenger of Allah was a miracle of prophethood, and the hearing of those dead disbelievers cannot be analogized to worldly hearing. Therefore, in the hadith, the Prophet said to the Companions, 'You are not better hearers than they.' Meaning they hear more than you. So the excess is in the sense that it is the hearing of the Hereafter and as a miracle of the Messenger of Allah. 'And the meaning of entering is to visit him' — after death, there is no visit; rather, one visits his grave.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This passage clarifies that oaths concerning speech or entering a person's presence are limited to that person's lifetime. The rationale is that speech aims at conveying meaning, which is impossible after death, and entering aims at seeing the person, which is not possible after death (one can only visit the grave). The text addresses a potential objection from the incident of Badr where the Prophet spoke to the dead polytheists. The response is that this was a miracle specific to prophethood and not a general ruling, so it does not affect the fiqh principle. Therefore, if one swears not to speak to someone, speaking to them after their death does not break the oath.

Key Terms
كلام (kalām): Speech addressed to another person with the intention of conveying meaning.
دخول (dukhūl): Entering upon someone to visit them personally.
زيارة (ziyārah): Visiting a person alive; after death, it becomes visiting the grave, which is a different act.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man swears, 'I will not visit Zaid,' and Zaid dies, does visiting his grave after death break the oath?
A) Yes, because visiting the grave is a form of visiting.
B) No, because visiting the grave is not visiting the person.
C) Yes, if the intention was to avoid any visitation.
D) No, because the oath is automatically void upon death.

Key Takeaway
Oaths about speaking to or entering upon a person are limited to their lifetime because the legal definitions of these actions require life.

Oath to Wash: Applicable After Death
Ruling with proof via qiyas on the definition of ghusl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that washing a dead person fulfills an oath to wash, and explain the legal reasoning (qiyas) based on the definition of ghusl.

Core Idea
An oath to wash someone is broken even after death because the essence of washing—pouring water for purification—applies to the dead.

Oaths often involve actions we perform for the living. But what if the person dies before the action is done? Does the oath lapse? This lesson examines a ruling from al-Hidayah where an oath to wash another person is considered broken even if the washing occurs after death. The key lies in the definition of the action itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the case and ruling
Read the passage carefully. A man swears: 'If I wash you, my slave is free.' He washes the man after death. The text rules that he becomes a breaker (hanith). Start by noting the exact ruling: the oath is broken.
2
Understand the underlying definition
The text then provides the legal cause (illa). It defines ghusl as isālah (pouring water) and tathīr (purification). This definition is essential because it determines whether the act can be performed on a dead body.
The definition is taken from the Hanafi understanding of ghusl, not necessarily shared by all schools.
3
Apply the definition to the dead
Since pouring water and purification are both achievable on a corpse—indeed, ghusl al-mayyit is a ritual washing—the act of washing is realized. Therefore, the condition of the oath (washing you) is fulfilled, and the oath is broken.
The dead person is fully capable of being the object of the action because the action does not require a response or benefit.
4
Contrast with actions that cannot be done on the dead
Not all actions can be performed after death. For example, feeding or teaching require the recipient's participation. Compare these to washing, which is a physical action independent of the recipient's state.
This contrast reinforces why the definition of the specific action is crucial.
5
Consider cross-madhhab differences
The note in the Hanafi position box indicates that this ruling is mukhtalaf fih (disputed). Some scholars may argue that oaths for personal services are only valid during the person's lifetime. Hanafis counter by focusing on the objective definition of the act.
Understanding this difference helps you appreciate the Hanafi emphasis on linguistic and customary meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قسم کھائی کہ اگر میں تم کو غسل دوں تو میر اعلام آزاد ہے موت کے بعد غسل دیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا وَلَوْ قَالَ إِنْ غَسَلْتُكَ فَعَبْدِي حُرٌّ فَغَسَلَهُ بَعْدَ مَامَاتَ يَحْنِتُ لِأَنَّ الْغُسْلَ هُوَ الْإِسَالَهُ وَمَعْنَاهُ التَّطْهِيرُ وَيَتَحَقَّقُ ذَالِكَ فِي الْمَيِّتِ ترجمہ اور اگر کسی نے کسی سے یہ کہا کہ اگر میں تم کو غسل دوں تو میرا اعلام آزاد ہے۔ اب اگر مرنے کے بعد غسل دیا تو وہ حانث ہو جائے گا کیونکہ غسل کے معنی ہیں پانی بہانا اور اس کا مقصود اسے پاک کرنا ہوتا ہے اور یہ بات یعنی پاک کر نا مردہ کو نسل کرانے میں پائی جاتی ہے۔ تشریح ترجمہ سے واضح ہے۔
He swore: 'If I wash you, my slave is free.' Then he washed him after death; he becomes a breaker (hanith). And if he said, 'If I wash you, my slave is free,' and he washed him after he died, he becomes a breaker, because ghusl is the pouring of water and its meaning is purification, and that is realized in the dead. Translation: And if someone said to someone, 'If I wash you, my slave is free.' Now if he washed him after death, he becomes a breaker, because ghusl means pouring water and its purpose is to purify him, and this purification is found in washing the dead. Explanation: The translation is clear.
Source pages p. 123

Commentary
This ruling presents a case where a person swears that if he washes another person, his slave will be free. The question is whether washing the person after death constitutes breaking the oath. The text rules that it does, because the essence of ghusl is pouring water with the intention of purification, which is possible and indeed required for the dead (as in ghusl al-mayyit). Therefore, the action is realized after death. This is a clear application: even though the person is dead, the act of washing can be performed, so the oath is broken.

Key Terms
غسل (ghusl): The act of washing, specifically pouring water over the body for purification.
حانث (hānith): One who breaks his oath, incurring kaffarah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does washing a dead person after an oath to wash him make one a breaker of the oath?
A) Because the dead person becomes clean.
B) Because ghusl means pouring water and purification, which can be done on a dead body.
C) Because the dead person can feel the water.
D) Because the oath automatically applies to any action after death.

Key Takeaway
The applicability of an oath to a deceased person depends on whether the defined essence of the action can be realized on the dead body.

Oath Not to Beat Wife: Pulling Hair, Choking, Biting
Ruling on whether pulling hair, choking, or biting constitutes beating in an oath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of darb in oaths and apply it to determine whether an act constitutes breaking the oath.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, any act causing pain, even playfully, breaks an oath not to beat.

This lesson explores a common scenario: a husband swears not to beat his wife, then engages in actions like pulling hair, choking, or biting. The key question is whether these actions constitute 'darb' (beating) in the context of the oath. The Hanafi position, grounded in 'urf (custom) and qiyas, defines darb broadly as any painful act, regardless of intent. We will examine the ruling, the underlying proof, and a notable intra-Hanafi difference of opinion regarding playful actions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the oath and the alleged acts
The passage begins with an oath not to beat, followed by three acts: pulling hair, choking, and biting. Recognize that each act is being evaluated for whether it constitutes darb.
The acts are explicitly named in the source text.
2
Understand the Hanafi definition of darb
The text defines darb as 'fi'l mu'lim' (a painful act). This is a broad definition based on customary understanding ('urf). The illa (effective cause) is the presence of pain (īlām).
This definition is key; it is not limited to conventional hitting.
3
Apply the definition to each act
For each act—pulling hair, choking, biting—check if pain is caused. Since each can cause pain, each qualifies as darb, making the oath broken (hanith).
The text confirms that 'al-īlām qad tahaqqaq' (pain is realized).
4
Consider the playful context and the ikhtilaf
Some scholars argue that if the act is playful (mulā'abah), it is not darb because it is called jest, not beating. The passage notes this as a minority view.
This is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf; the text resolves it.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
The correct position (al-mukhtar) is that even in play, the oath is broken because the action causes pain. The objective criterion (pain) overrides subjective intent.
The text states 'khulāṣah fīhi ṣaḥīḥ' (the correct view is hanith).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَمَنْ حَلَفَ لَا يَضْرِبُ امْرَأَتُهُ فَمَدَّ شَعْرَهَا أَوْ خَنَقَهَا أَوْعَضَّهَا حَنَتْ لِأَنَّهُ اِسْمٌ لِفِعْل مُؤْلِمٍ وَقَدْ تَحَقَّقَ الْإِيْلَامُ وَقِيلَ لَا يَحْنِتُ فِي حَالِ الْمُلَاعَبَةِ لِأَنَّهُ يُسَمَّى مُمَازَحَةً لَا ضَرْبًا ترجمہ اگر کسی نے یہ قسم کھائی کہ میں اپنی بیوی کو نہیں ماروں گا لیکن اس کے سر کے بال کھینچے یا اس کا گلا دبایا یا دانت سے اس کا بدن دبا دیا تو حانث ہو جائے گا اگر چہ درستگی اور ہنسی مذاق کا موقع ہو کیونکہ مارنا ایک ایسے کام کا نام ہے جس سے تکلیف پہنچتی ہو اور ان تمام کاموں میں یہ دکھ پہنچانا پایا گیا۔ اور بعض مشائخ نے فرمایا ہے کہ اسی مذاق کی حالت میں حانث نہ ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اس حالت میں مار نہیں بلکہ دل لگی اور دل بستگی ہوتی ہے۔ فائدہ .... خلاصہ میں اس کو صحیح کہا ہے۔
And whoever swears, 'I will not beat my wife,' then he pulled her hair, or choked her, or bit her, he becomes a breaker (hanith), because [darb] is a name for a painful act, and pain has been realized. And it is said that he does not become a breaker in the case of playful jest, because it is called humor, not beating. Translation: If someone swears that he will not beat his wife, but he pulls her hair, or chokes her, or bites her body with his teeth, then he becomes a breaker, even if it is a time of correction and jest, because beating is the name of an act that causes pain, and in all these actions, causing pain is found. And some mashayikh said that in the case of jest, he does not become a breaker, because in that state it is not beating but play and affection. Benefit: In summary, the correct view is that he becomes a breaker.
Source pages p. 124

Commentary
This ruling defines 'darb' (beating) in the context of an oath. The general rule is that darb includes any action that causes pain. Therefore, pulling hair, choking, and biting all constitute beating and break the oath. However, there is a view that if the action is done playfully (mula'abah), it is not considered beating because the intent is jest, not harm. The commentary notes that the correct position (mufta bihi) is that even in jest, the oath is broken because the action itself causes pain. This shows that in Hanafi fiqh, the objective criterion of pain is given weight over subjective intent in the context of oaths.

Key Terms
ضرب (darb): Any act that causes pain, even if not a conventional hit.
إيلام (īlām): Causing pain, which is the defining characteristic of darb in oaths.
ملاعبة (mulā'abah): Play or jest, which some scholars argue negates the categorization as beating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man swears not to beat his wife, then playfully bites her arm. Is he a breaker of the oath?
A) No, because it was playful.
B) Yes, because biting causes pain.
C) No, because biting is not hitting.
D) Yes, only if she complains.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, darb in oaths is defined by the presence of pain, not the manner or intent; even playful acts that cause pain break the oath.
